1801 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF LA CROSSE v. SCHULTZ


No. 83-573


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


115 Wis. 2d 700; 341 N.W.2d 419; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4035



October 10, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of a circuit court for La Crosse county, DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the city's complaint for recovery of personal property taxes from appellee taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer lived out of state but practiced dentistry in the city. He paid city taxes on personal property located in his city offices, however, he eventually removed the personal property from the state. He continued his practice in the city using dental equipment owned by another person. He did not file any tax returns with the city. The city conceded that the defendant owned no property in the city on the proper assessment date. Nonetheless it sought to assess taxes arguing that the taxpayer had waived its right to contest the city's jurisdiction. The trial court found for the taxpayer. The court affirmed concluding that the defendant's failure to file a tax return did not bar him from raising the jurisdictional defense by operation of Wis. Stat. § 70.35. The court held that the defendant had the right, notwithstanding Wis. Stat. §§ 70.35 and 70.47(7)(a), to question the jurisdiction of the city to impose the tax at issue. The court found that the tax was void ab initio and unenforceable because the city had no power to impose it. The court held that the failure of the taxpayer to file a return was insufficient to confer jurisdiction to tax where none existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court dismissing the city's complaint for recovery of personal property taxes from the taxpayer was affirmed.

 

1802 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


HARRISON v. ALLSTATE INS. CO.


No. 82-2291, 82-2292


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


115 Wis. 2d 699; 341 N.W.2d 418; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3978



October 7, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 10, 1984


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Kenosha county: JOHN E. MALLOY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurance company appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which awarded damages to plaintiff guests for injuries suffered when they jumped from a second-floor balcony of the owners' duplex during a fire.


OVERVIEW: The guests were forced to jump because the only other access to the second floor, a stairway, was blocked by fire. The court affirmed the award of damages to the guests against the owners' insurance company. The court held that the trial court properly found, as a matter of law, that the owners' negligence caused the injuries because the balcony was above grade and, thus, the duplex violated the Kenosha, Wis., Code of Gen. Ordinances § 16.04(h) (1978) (Housing Code), which incorporated Wis. Stat. Admin. Code § Ind. 21.03, requiring two safe exits. Construing the Housing Code to require retroactive application of § 21.03 to the duplex fulfilled the legislative intent of establishing minimum safety standards for existing housing and was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the impairment of property rights was a reasonable consequence of the regulation of older housing, which was a legitimate exercise of police power. The court held that the guests proved that the duplex failed to comply with minimum housing standards and refused to consider whether another balcony met the requirements of § 21.03 because the issue was not raised at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments for the guests and against the insurance company.

 

1803 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HARRIS


No. 83-143-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


117 Wis. 2d 779; 343 N.W.2d 829; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4245



October 4, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie county: URBAN VAN SUSTEREN, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) quashing four search warrants and suppressing the evidence obtained in executing the warrants.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed from an order quashing four search warrants and suppressing the evidence obtained in executing the warrants. The trial court concluded that the warrants were invalid because the court commissioner who issued them did not have the necessary authority. On appeal, the court agreed that the warrants were invalid, but found that the suppression of evidence in this case would not further the purpose of the exclusionary rule. Therefore the court reversed the order and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to admit the evidence seized pursuant to the warrants.In this case, no constitutional right had been violated. The court commissioner who issued the warrants had been in office for five years and had regularly been issuing search warrants. He was a neutral magistrate. He acted upon probable cause, and there was no indication in the record that the Justice Department agents who sought the warrants acted in bad faith. The court found that the failure to formally authorize the court commissioner to issue search warrants was solely a bureaucratic oversight.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remandedthe trial court decision quashing four search warrants and suppressing the evidence obtained in executing the warrants.

 

1804 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ULLSVIK v. GOLD


No. 81-2013


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


115 Wis. 2d 693; 339 N.W.2d 365; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3934



September 27, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted summary eviction in favor of plaintiff, the personal representative of the estate of the tenant, dismissed the tenant's defense and counterclaim, and awarded double daily rent for the tenant's holdover period, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 704.27.


OVERVIEW: The tenant was served a notice to terminate and held over without the landlord's permission. The landlord sought eviction and the tenant attempted to assert the defense that he was being evicted because of his sexual preference for males. He counterclaimed for damages based on discriminatory eviction. The circuit court ruled in favor of the landlord, awarding double daily rent for the holdover period and dismissing the tenant's defense and counterclaim. The tenant appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that the circuit court did not err by dismissing discrimination on sexual preference as a defense and counterclaim under a Wis. Stat. § 799 eviction action. The circuit court was required to impose Wis. Stat. § 704.27 on the tenant for holding over without the landlord's consent and Wis. Stat. § 704.27 passed judicial scrutiny under both due process and equal protection standards. The record did not indicate that rational and logical grounds for the statute did not exist. The court did not consider the issue of whether to impose an undertaking to stay the evidence judgment for post-eviction-judgment double rent violated equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1805 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. BARAJAS


No. 83-154-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


115 Wis. 2d 696; 339 N.W.2d 366; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3872



September 26, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH ADAM FINE, Judge. Affirmed. APPEAL from an order of the of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RUDOLPH T. RANDA, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of abandonment under Wis. Stat. § 52.05(1), and which denied his postconviction motion. Defendant alleged that the jury instruction was constitutionally infirm and that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not pay any support for three years after his divorce. As a result, defendant was convicted of abandonment under Wis. Stat. § 52.05(1). On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: The jury charge properly did not include language stating that a refusal to work would not be willful if defendant concluded that his working conditions were oppressive, because defendant testified that he quit his job because he was dissatisfied with himself and with the job, and because there was no indication that defendant perceived the job as oppressive. Defendant did not pay any child support for the years that he did earn money. The jury could infer from defendant's reasons for quitting his job that his subsequent efforts to secure employment were not exhaustive. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

 

1806 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roth


No. 83-312-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


115 Wis. 2d 163; 339 N.W.2d 807; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3861


August 16, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
September 26, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John F. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found him of guilty of theft by lessee, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(e) and (3)(b). Defendant appealed the order denying his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant paid a deposit and rented an automobile from a leasing firm. Defendant returned the automobile two months after the date it was to be returned. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for theft by a lessee under § 943.20(1)(e) and (3)(b). The court held that § 943.20(1)(e) was constitutional and did not have to include the element of an "intent to defraud" in order to withstand a constitutional challenge. The court found that the "theft-by-lessee" statute did contain an element of criminal intent, the failure to return rented property within 10 days, which withstood a constitutional challenge. The court held that § 943.20(1)(e) did not imprison one for a debt contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 16, because defendant was liable on account of his criminal act, intentionally failing to return the rented property within 10 days. The court held that defendant waived his claim of error regarding the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on the element of intent to defraud because he failed to request such an instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order against defendant.

 

1807 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Horenberger


No. 82-2405-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


114 Wis. 2d 598; 338 N.W.2d 530; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3781



August 22, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Granted December 6, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of armed robbery, party to a crime; false imprisonment, party to a crime; and, burglary, party to a crime and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction of armed robbery, false imprisonment and burglary, defendant argued, among other things, that he was denied due process of law because the complaint and the information failed to provide sufficient notice of the offense charged. A defendant's right to be informed of the nature and cause of the accusations against him was guaranteed by the U.S. Const. amend. XI and Wis. Const. art. I § 7. The test to determine whether a complaint met that constitutional standard was twofold: (1) whether the accusation was such that the defendant could determine whether it stated an offense to which he was able to plead and prepare a defense, and (2) whether conviction or acquittal was a bar to another prosecution for the same offense. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction. It held that the complaint charged defendant with all the offenses as a party to the crime. As such, defendant should have known that he was required to defend on that basis. Defendant's conviction may also be pled as a bar to future prosecutions to the same offense. Accordingly, the complaint gave defendant adequate notice and therefore, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and the denial of his motion for a new trial was affirmed.

 

1808 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. PIETKIVITCH


No. 82-2371


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


114 Wis. 2d 595; 338 N.W.2d 528; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3656



July 26, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: STEPHEN A. SIMANEK, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) that revoked his driving privileges for six months pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305 on the ground that he refused a chemical test after his arrest for operating a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: An altercation between defendant and his arresting officer left defendant with bruises and a scalp laceration. While he was being treated at a hospital, another officer recited the informing the accused form to defendant from memory and explained it to him. When the officer tried to read the form, however, defendant loudly and repeatedly stated that he could not hear the officer. He did not answer when he was asked if he refused to take the test. He claimed on appeal that he was suffering from hysteria at the time and was disabled under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(3)(b)(5)d. He also claimed that the revocation of his license placed him in double jeopardy. The court affirmed the order. Ample evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant's conduct was alcohol-related and not due to a physical inability to refuse or consent. The trial court was therefore not required to determine whether hysteria resulted in a physical disability within the meaning of § 343.305(3)(b)(5)d. Defendant was not placed in double jeopardy because refusal to take a chemical test and driving while under the influence of an intoxicant were two separate acts warranting two separate responses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1809 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kenwood Merchandising Corp. v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 82-2023


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


114 Wis. 2d 226; 338 N.W.2d 312; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3632


June 1, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
July 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Harold B. Jackson, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a former employer and its insurer, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by defendant Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) granting defendant former employee disfigurement benefits under Wis. Stat. § 102.56 (1975). Plaintiffs alleged that § 102.56 (1975) was unconstitutional and that LIRC improperly awarded both disfigurement and disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: An employee lost his thumb and two fingers of his right hand in a work-related accident. He left his employment and, after retraining, obtained a position as a bank teller. LIRC subsequently awarded the employee a lump sum for permanent partial disability as well as a lump sum of lost earnings due to disfigurement under Wis. Stat. § 102.56 (1975). The trial court upheld LIRC's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: LIRC properly awarded both disfigurement and partial disability benefits for the same injury. Plaintiffs did not establish that § 102.56 (1975) was unconstitutional on due process grounds because the evidence was sufficient to establish a disfigurement award under Wis. Stat. § 102.56 (1981), which plaintiffs conceded to be constitutional. Because there were sufficient avenues of review, Wis. Stat. § 102.56 (1975) did not violate Wis. Const. art. IV, § 1. Because the bank's customers had a tendency to recoil from the employee's disfigured hand, the evidence was sufficient to support the disfigurement award. A doctor's report was sufficient to support the disability award, although the doctor had voluntarily surrendered his medical license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1810 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HYNITE CORP.


No. 82-1730


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


114 Wis. 2d 592; 337 N.W.2d 856; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3683



June 27, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH G. GORENSTEIN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, through its Department of Natural Resources (DNR), appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed an action brought by the DNR for forfeitures and injunctive relief against appellee corporation arising out of alleged violations of air quality regulations.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the DNR's action after concluding that Wis. Adm. Code, § NR 154.18(1), the regulation upon which the action was based, was unconstitutionally void for vagueness. On review, the court noted that, as a matter of judicial prudence, a court should not decide the constitutionality of a statute or regulation unless it is essential to the determination of the case before it. The court did not reach the constitutionality issue because it determined that the appeal could be decided without passing on the constitutionality question. According to the court, after the corporation was notified of the allegations, it requested a hearing. The DNR never granted the hearing request even though Wis. Stat. § 144.35 (1977) mandated both notice and hearing. Based on the lack of a hearing, the court affirmed dismissal of DNR's action against the corporation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the action.

 

1811 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


DRUML CO. v. SEWERAGE COMMN. OF MILWAUKEE


No. 82-1338


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


114 Wis. 2d 591; 337 N.W.2d 856; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3684



June 27, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 30, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH G. GORENSTEIN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city sewerage commission and a sludge company, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted a declaratory judgment for plaintiff corporation that the contract between the sewerage commission and the sludge company was void for failing to comply with the prevailing wage rate.


OVERVIEW: The corporation held for six years a sludge hauling and disposal contract for disposing of sewage/sludge with the sewerage district. It was subsequently out-bid by another sludge company. The corporation brought a declaratory judgment action to declare the sewerage commission contract awarded to the sludge company invalid because it violated a prevailing wage rate law. The commission and the sludge company argued that Wis. Stat. § 66.293 was inapplicable to a sludge hauling and disposal contract because the latter did not constitute public works. The trial court, however, found in favor of the corporation. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the contract was void because 1931 Wis. Laws ch. 441 was not substantially complied with. The court noted that invalidity of a contract ordinarily resulted from a failure to comply with provisions which related to essential matters. The court held that the prevailing wage rate was essential to the contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the contract between the sewerage commission and the sludge company was void for failing to comply with the prevailing wage rate, in an action for a declaratory judgment by the corporation, which held the contract before the sludge company out-bid it.

 

1812 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Stehling v. Beaver Dam


No. 82-1053


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


114 Wis. 2d 197; 336 N.W.2d 401; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3550


March 16, 1983, Argued  
June 27, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dodge County: Henry G. Gergen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their action against respondent city that contested a special tax for a sidewalk.


OVERVIEW: The city approved a resolution requiring the property owners to construct a sidewalk in front of their properties. The owners did not build the sidewalk. The Board of Public Works contracted for its construction. The expense was assessed as a special tax against the owners. The owners then filed an action for a judgment declaring that the actions of the city constituted an invalid exercise of police power and that the assessment unconstitutionally took their property for public use. The trial court dismissed the complaint, finding that Wis. Stat. § 66.615(3) did not require a finding of benefits to the property subjected to the tax, and that a tax assessed under § 66.615(3) was a constitutionally valid exercise of police power. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that although generally, pursuant to both U.S. Const. amend. V and Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 a private property could not be assessed for a public improvement unless the improvement benefitted the property, a municipality could, under the exercise of its police power, order installation of a sidewalk. It could then assess the properties on which the sidewalk fronted, regardless of whether the properties were benefitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1813 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


EMPLOYERS INS. OF WAUSAU v. MITCHELL


No. 82-2262


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


114 Wis. 2d 592; 337 N.W.2d 857; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3740



June 20, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 10, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: RICHARD W. BARDWELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action by plaintiff workmen's compensation insurers (insurers), defendant state officials appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which held certain provisions of the budget review bill, Wis. Stat. §§ 94d, 820c, 820e, 820m, 820s, 2065(5)(b), and 2204(26(c) (1979), unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The insurers paid monies into worker's compensation security funds, but the 1979 budget review bill attempted to terminate the funds by awarding a portion of the monies in the funds to the insurers and paying the remainder into the state's general fund. The insurers filed an action to obtain injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment that the payment to the general fund was unconstitutional. The trial court entered a judgment declaring certain provisions of the budget review bill unconstitutional as a taking of property without due process to the extent that it terminated the temporary fund and distributed the monies to the state's general fund. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the insurers had a property interest in the fund, because the monies were held for their benefit. Because the underlying facts were undisputed, the insurers were not required to submit proof in support of their claim, nor did they waive the right to contest the taking because they accepted funds under a separate section of the budget review bill. Wis. Stat. § 646.71 (1979) remained in effect, because Wis. Stat. § 820s (1979), which repealed it, was declared unconstitutional and was a nullity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that certain provisions of the budget review bill were unconstitutional.

 

1814 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF MONONA v. DISPLAYMEDIA, INC.


No. 82-762 & 82-763


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


114 Wis. 2d 590; 337 N.W.2d 855; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3755



June 15, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 30, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the dismissal of its complaints against two billboard owners for violating Monona, Wis., Building Code § 13.09(8)(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the city argued, inter alia, that (1) the billboard owners did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Monona, Wis., Building Code § 13.09 as it applied to noncommercial speech; and (2) the circuit court erred in interpreting § 13.09 as an unconstitutional restraint on noncommercial speech. Upon review, the court found that the circuit court correctly held that § 13.09 unconstitutionally restrained freedom of speech rights guaranteed by the First Amendment to the United States Constitution. The ordinance allowed any onsite commercial advertising but forbade noncommercial messages on billboards everywhere unless permitted by specific exception. Those noncommercial messages that were excepted had additional stringent restrictions on size and often required prior approval, giving greater protection to commercial speech than noncommercial speech although more protection was generally accorded to the latter. No legitimate, governmental purpose was put forward by the city which served as a rational basis for its treatment of the various classifications of noncommercial messages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the city's complaints against the billboard owners.

 

1815 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SMITH v. NORVILLE


No. 82-788


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


114 Wis. 2d 590; 337 N.W.2d 855; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3685



June 13, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied November 15, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH G. GORENSTEIN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injury victims challenged a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found that respondent property owners were not negligent in the victims' personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The victims suffered injuries when the balcony of the duplex leased by one of the victims collapsed. The jury found that the owners were not negligent. On appeal, the court affirmed. The fact that the "safe place" statute, Wis. Stat. § 101.11(1), did not apply to the victims' case because the owners' building had less than three tenants did not deny the victims equal protection of the law. There was a rational basis for the classification set forth in the statute, and thus, it was constitutional. Further, the victims were not entitled to a res ipsa loquitur instruction because they presented sufficient evidence concerning the owners' alleged negligence to rule out the availability of that instruction. The court found that the trial court properly gave a falsus in uno instruction because there were discrepancies between the testimony of one of the victims regarding her work history and her actual employment record. Finally, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 906.06(2), the victims were not permitted to use the affidavit of one of the jurors, which showed that the jury intended to award damages, to impeach the special verdict finding of no negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1816 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STEEL v. WILKINSON


No. 82-1132


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


114 Wis. 2d 591; 337 N.W.2d 856; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3687



June 13, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 9, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: WILLIAM A. JENNARO, Judge. Modified and as modified, affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment modified and as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that denied their request for injunctive relief against defendants, city, mayor, and aldermen, for converting a highway from vehicular traffic to a pedestrian mall and that awarded attorney fees against each resident to defendants.


OVERVIEW: After the city converted a highway to a pedestrian mall pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.298, the residents claimed that the conversion constituted a public nuisance and sought injunctive relief. The trial court denied the mandatory injunction, dismissed the complaint, and granted attorney fees to defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of the injunction, holding that § 66.298, the pedestrian mall statute, had preemptive effect over Wis. Stat. § 349.03(2), forbidding municipal ordinances more restrictive than highway user statutes. The court concluded that the specific statute permitting the designation of streets as pedestrian malls prevailed over § 349.03(2), which was a more general statute. However, the court concluded that the trial court erred in assessing attorney fees against each resident complainant because there was only one complaint against defendants, who were united in interest, employed the same attorney, and filed one answer to the original complaint. The trial court did not err in rejecting defendants' amended complaint as untimely after it had already denied the motion for mandatory injunction and had dismissed the original complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied the residents' motion for injunctive relief but modified the judgment by reducing the amount of attorney fees awarded to defendants.

 

1817 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. MOORE


No. 82-1927


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


114 Wis. 2d 592; 337 N.W.2d 856; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3695



June 7, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac county: JEROLD E. MURPHY, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of reckless driving in the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) and sought review. Defendant argued that he was not informed of his statutory right to demand a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was never notified that he was entitled to a jury trial on his reckless driving charge. Defendant pleaded by telephone and did not personally appear. The court reversed the conviction and held that there was no compelling reason why people who personally appeared at arraignment received notification of the right to a jury trial, while those who pleaded by mail or telephone did not have a right to the same information. The court further held that a condition precedent in Wis. Stat. § 345.34 was that defendant be informed of his right to demand a jury trial. The court found that defendant must have been informed that he had the right to a jury trial, and he had the burden to demand such trial and pay the jury tender.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded to the trial court with instructions to allow defendant to file his demand for a jury trial in writing and pay his fee.

 

1818 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


J.F. Ahern Co. v. Wisconsin State Bldg. Com.


No. 81-1274


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


114 Wis. 2d 69; 336 N.W.2d 679; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3553; 40 A.L.R.4th 940


July 28, 1982, Argued  
June 7, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order denying Brown and Dunn's motion to dismiss reversed and judgment and orders otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissed plaintiff contractors' action for declaratory judgment that defendants, State Building Commission, Department of Administration (DOA), and individuals, violated Wisconsin statutes and the constitutional principle of the separation of powers in decisions on the construction of a state office building. The contractors appealed and defendants cross-appealed on procedural issues.


OVERVIEW: The contractors sought to enjoin the DOA from entering contracts for the design and construction of state office buildings without competitive bidding. The contractors also sought a declaratory judgment that the Commission unconstitutionally exercised its authority. The contractors alleged that the DOA's action violated the separation of powers doctrine. Because commencement of the action determined jurisdiction, failure to serve legislative committees with amended complaints did not affect jurisdiction. The court held that failure to serve the Attorney General with the notice required by Wis. Stat. § 895.45(1)(1975) required dismissal of the individuals. As Wisconsin citizens, the contractors had standing to contest the constitutionality of statutes related to public expenditures. The court held that the Commission's decision to waive competitive bidding in favor of the design/build process was based on rational factors of economy, efficiency and the public welfare, and was not arbitrary or capricious. Because the Commission's power over construction contracts was subject to the governor's veto, there was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the contractor's action for declaratory judgment against the Commission, the DOA, and individuals alleging a violation of Wisconsin statutes and the separation of powers doctrine. The court held that the trial court erred in failing to dismiss claims against the state officials in their individual capacities.

 

1819 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olson


No. 82-679-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


113 Wis. 2d 249; 335 N.W.2d 433; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3537


May 9, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
May 25, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Moria Krueger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree sexual assault, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d), and from the order denying his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the sexual assault of a four-year-old boy. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by allowing the victim to testify at the preliminary hearing and at trial, by conducting voir dire of the victim before the jury, and by refusing to instruct the jury on lesser included offenses of child abuse and battery. He also contended that Wis. Stat. § 940.225 was unconstitutional as applied to the case. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant did not object at trial to the victim's competency to testify and so waived his objection. The magistrate did not abuse his discretion in permitting the victim to testify at the preliminary examination. Defendant did not object at trial that he was prejudiced by conducting the voir dire concerning the victim's competency to testify before the jury and so waived his objection. Because acquittal on sexual assault and conviction for battery or child abuse was impossible, the trial court did not err by refusing to instruct the jury on child abuse or battery as lesser included offenses. Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1820 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. NEELIS


No. 82-1534-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


113 Wis. 2d 726; 336 N.W.2d 707; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3587



May 11, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 10, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington county: JAMES B. SCHWALBACH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for modification of the sentence imposed after he was found guilty of operating a motor vehicle after revocation of his license in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1).


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to six months in jail despite defendant's submission of a physician's letter stating that a jail sentence would probably worsen his permanent mental and emotional defects. After defendant's motion for sentence modification was denied, the court, on appeal, affirmed, holding that Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2) required the imposition of at least a six month sentence. Section 343.44(2) prohibited the granting of probation within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 973.09(1)(a) for one convicted of driving after revocation. The court also concluded that the imposition of the six month sentence did not violate his right not to be subject to cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Wis. Const. art. I, § 6. The trial court was obliged to impose the jail sentence on defendant, and it had no jurisdiction to place conditions on that sentence. However, defendant had a right to appropriate attention to any medical problems that he might suffer during his jail terms. If the conditions of imprisonment posed a serious threat to his health, he was not without remedy because he was entitled to challenge his confinement conditions by appropriate writs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1821 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


AMERICAN STATE EQUIP. CO. v. NORTHWESTERN MUT. LIFE INS. CO.


No. 82-1361


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


113 Wis. 2d 723; 334 N.W.2d 589; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3465



April 25, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MARVIN C. HOLZ, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff suppliers challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to defendant landowner. The trial court dismissed the suppliers' action for foreclosure of a lien against the landowner's property, under Wis. Stat. § 779.01, to recover the rental value of equipment used to demolish a structure on the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The suppliers urged the court to adopt a construction of the term "materials" in § 779.01(3) to include the rental of machinery or equipment, so as to conform the private lien law to the public lien law set out in Wis. Stat. §§ 779.14 and 779.15. The court noted that prior decisions of the Wisconsin Supreme Court had repeatedly held that the rental value of machinery and equipment was not a lienable item under either the public or the private lien law. While those earlier cases were archaic, the legislature was aware of those decisions when it restricted its alterations to the public lien law. The court held that the parties had transacted their business in strict compliance with existing law and it was not the place of the court to substitute its judgment for that of the legislature. The court held that, while the legislature established a broader classification of lienable items in the public lien law, the classifications did not deny the equal protection of the laws to the suppliers. The court concluded that the public and the private lien law classifications were reasonable in the context of the case and complied with the appropriate standards of reasonableness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Way

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for modification of his sentences after his conviction upon a guilty plea to one count of battery to a peace officer, which was a violation of Wis. Stat. §. 940.20(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to one count of battery to a police officer, pursuant to Wis. Stat. §. 940.20(2), after a traffic arrest. He was sentenced to six months in the county jail with certain privileges, a $ 500 fine, $ 100 in costs, and a six-month additional sentence if he failed to pay the fine. Before the due date for the fine, defendant fled the state. He was arrested upon his return. The trial court held a show cause hearing, denied defendant's motion for an extension, and imposed the additional sentence under Wis. Stat. §. 973.07, to be served consecutively. It held that the trial court had jurisdiction to order a commitment for failure to pay the fine to be served consecutively to the original commitment, that a place of confinement issue was moot, that the six-month sentence for failure to pay the fine was not an abuse of discretion in light to defendant's ability to pay, and that defendant's history and conduct justified the two-year sentence for escape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for modification of his sentences for battery to a police officer.

STATE v. JOHNS

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions for first-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(b) and taking a hostage in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.305 entered by the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin). Defendant also appealed an order denying his post-conviction motions.

Stat. § 940.305, which contained all of the elements of taking a hostage.

GILBERT v. STATE


No. 82-1203


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


113 Wis. 2d 723; 334 N.W.2d 589; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3520



April 15, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county, ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order reversed and remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent state medical examining board (board) revoking the doctor's license for unprofessional misconduct.


OVERVIEW: The doctor was accused of unprofessional conduct in his handling of an auto accident victim's care. The victim died from shock and blood loss after several hours in the emergency room and numerous delays in treatment. The former hospital administrator notified the board. The board conducted an investigation and determined that the doctor engaged in unprofessional conduct. The board revoked the doctor's license. The doctor sought review in the trial court, which affirmed. The doctor sought further review. On appeal, the court reversed the ruling, finding that the doctor could not be disciplined without evidence of a violation of the standard of care. The court held that such evidence had to come from experts and the board could not rely on its own expertise or that of its members in judging the doctor's actions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and directed the board to reinstate the doctor's license to practice medicine. The court also remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1825 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. LOFTHOUSE


No. 82-728-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


112 Wis. 2d 674; 333 N.W.2d 733; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3456



March 28, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood county: NATHAN E. WIESE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of violating Wis. Stat. §§ 948.13 and 948.14, neglecting to supply an animal with sufficient food and water, and failing to provide an animal with proper shelter, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged after county humane officers and other witnesses observed a lack of food, water and space for defendant's animals. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions. The jury could reasonably find that fecal encrusted bowls and the buckets with dead mice contained no "potable" water, and could reasonably infer that the condition of the water containers and buckets was not an isolated incident. The jury could infer from the evidence that the dogs and cats put on considerable weight after being removed, that they had not been fed enough to maintain them in a healthy condition. The jury could find that kennels in which a dog could not lie down without lying in fecal material were not periodically cleaned as required by Wis. Stat. § 948.14(4). The court rejected defendant's claims that the applicable statutes were void for vagueness. Both statutes adequately informed defendant of his obligations to his animals under the statutes. The instructions as to the elements of the offenses adequately charged the jury with the proper standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1826 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SRENASKI v. CITY OF MANITOWOC


No. 82-1077


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


113 Wis. 2d 722; 334 N.W.2d 588; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3495



March 16, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc county: FRED H. HAZLEWOOD, Judge. Modified and as modified, affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment modified and as modified affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs drivers appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which, at a hearing on a motion for summary judgment, determined that a penalty provision of a municipal ordinance of defendant city relating to violations for overtime parking violated the equal protections clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The trial court also found that the unconstitutional portion could be severed.


OVERVIEW: The drivers alleged the ordinance fostered unequal protection of the law because drivers who opted to contest their overtime parking tickets had to pay, if convicted, more than if they did not contest the ticket. The trial court agreed and removed part of the language relating to the actual amount of the fine to be paid by those contesting the ticket. The court agreed the ordinance was unconstitutional finding that, in effect, the city was arbitrarily distinguishing between members of the same class (those who received overtime parking violations) by penalizing those who chose to contest the violation. The court also found the unconstitutional portions of the penalty provision could be severed. However, the court found that the decision of the trial court did not go far enough in excising the malignant portion of the ordinance. The court noted that severing the invalid parts of the penalty provision would leave the statute with only one sentence, which might not serve the city's purposes. The court noted that a new ordinance would be valid as long as the reasonable person had proper notice and was treated alike with the members of the class who opted not to contest the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court finding a portion of the penalty provision of the statute unconstitutional was modified to sever out the entire invalid language in the ordinance. As modified, the judgment was affirmed. However, as the taxpayers came under the ordinance as severed, their cases could not be dismissed on grounds of unconstitutionality.

 

1827 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Brennan v. Employment Relations Com.


No. 82-906


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


112 Wis. 2d 38; 331 N.W.2d 667; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3222; 119 L.R.R.M. 2016


January 12, 1983, Submitted on Briefs  
February 23, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: David V. Jennings, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant official appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which determined that Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4)(jm), which governs arbitration for the Milwaukee Police Department, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission found that the city and the Milwaukee Police Association had reached a bargaining impasse and ordered the parties to proceed to final and binding arbitration pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4)(jm). The official brought suit claiming the statute to be unconstitutional. The court rejected the official's constitutionality challenge. The statute did not constitute special legislation because its title referred to Milwaukee. The title was not part of the statute and the plain language of the statute encompassed all cities of the first class, not just Milwaukee. The court determined there was no ambiguity in the interplay of Wis. Stat. §§ 111.70(4) (jm) and 111.77(8). The former clearly governed all cities of the first class, while the latter clearly governed those within its population limits not already governed by the former. The court agreed with the trial court that § 111.70(4) (jm) did not prohibit the arbitrator from considering those cost factors enumerated in § 111.77(6). The question of a municipality's ability to pay was not given shorter shrift under one statute than it was under the other.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

CITY OF MUSKEGO v. VANDEN PLAS

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which fined defendant after a jury found him guilty of violating Muskego, Wis., Ordinance ch. 17, § 801(7)(3) by raising pigs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating a zoning ordinance that had been interpreted to prohibit the raising of pigs. The court disagreed with the trial court's interpretation, holding that livestock meant pigs and the ordinance allowed the raising of pigs in some circumstances, which defendant fulfilled. The court therefore reversed the judgment against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the imposition of a fine against defendant for raising pigs.

STATE v. WATSON


No. 82-306


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


112 Wis. 2d 669; 332 N.W.2d 313; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3367



February 10, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied May 23, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that denied his postconviction motion. He had pled guilty to two counts of false imprisonment, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.30, one count of battery, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.19(1), and one count of endangering safety by conduct regardless of life, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.30; all the crimes arose out of his attacks against two women in one day.


OVERVIEW: The information alleged, and the trial court determined, that defendant had been convicted of five previous crimes. In applying the repeater statute, Wis. Stat. § 939.62, the trial court sentenced defendant to eight years on each false imprisonment charge, three years on the battery charge, and 11 years on the endangering safety charge with the sentences to be consecutive. Wis. Stat. § 939.62(1) provided that where the actor was a repeater, and the present conviction was for any crime for which imprisonment could be imposed, the maximum term of imprisonment set by law for that crime could be increased as prescribed. The court rejected the argument of defendant that the use of singular nouns in Wis. Stat. § 939.62 showed a legislative intent to enhance only one crime. Regarding defendant's claim that the repeater statute had been selectively applied to favor women and that it was thus a violation of the equal protection of the laws, the court found insufficient evidence had been presented for it to find an abuse of discretion by the trial court's denial of an evidentiary hearing on the matter.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Estate of Halsted


No. 82-145


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 606; 331 N.W.2d 609; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3217


December 8, 1982, Argued  
February 10, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from orders of the Circuit Court for Sauk County: James W. Karch, Judge, and Robert F. Curtin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the personal representatives and the heirs, sought review of orders of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion to strike respondent Department of Revenue's statute of limitations defense. Appellants also appealed from the order dismissing their petition for a hearing on the determination of tax due and directing them to pay additional tax and interest.


OVERVIEW: After the decedent died, a claim was filed against his estate. Appellants disputed the validity of the claim and, therefore, did not include it as a debt of the decedent on the state inheritance tax return. Although the Department issued a certificate pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 72.30(3)(c ), showing the tax due, appellants did not petition for a hearing until more than six months later. The trial court refused to strike the Department's statute of limitations defense and it dismissed appellants' petition for a hearing on the determination of tax due. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that under Wis. Stat. § 72.30(4), appellants' petition for a redetermination of the estate tax was barred where it was filed more than six months after the date the state issued the certificate. Finally, the court refused to find that § 72.30(4) was unconstitutional by denying appellants' due process of law because the statute did not extinguish the right to claim the deductions appellants' claimed on its amended returns before the right to assert them could have been made in court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

State v. Novack


No. 82-1345-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


111 Wis. 2d 701; 332 N.W.2d 312; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3284



January 19, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood county: FRED A. FINK, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of disorderly conduct in violation of Wis. Stat. § 947.01. He also alleged that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: An auxiliary deputy sheriff was patrolling a picnic when he heard a firecracker explode. While the deputy was lecturing a group of bystanders on the law concerning fireworks, defendant addressed the deputy by name with insulting and vulgar language. Defendant was arrested for disorderly conduct. At defendant's trial, the deputy testified that he felt the remark reflected on his authority and was slanderous and profane, but that he did not feel physically threatened. On appeal of defendant's conviction, the court affirmed. The court held that the conviction did not violate defendant's First Amendment right to free speech. It noted that the words did not constitute obscenity, as the crowd that overheard the remark thought it was a joke and was not shocked. However, the court found that the grossly offensive and insulting remark directed personally at the deputy constituted "fighting words." The trial court properly refused to give an instruction that stated that a law-enforcement officer was required to bear more in the way of abuse and insult than people in general. Defendant's sentence was not excessive, as he was charged and convicted as a repeater.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Rodriguez v. State


No. 82-1178-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


111 Wis. 2d 701; 332 N.W.2d 312; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3242



January 13, 1983 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied April 22, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: HAROLD B. JACKSON, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder, party to a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's common law wife purchased heroin from the victim. She shortchanged him, and he confronted her about her conduct. A struggle ensued in which the victim was killed. A witness nearby saw the events and testified that defendant killed the victim, and that she had known defendant for approximately a year prior to the killing. The witness identified defendant from a photograph the day after the killing and in person two days after the killing at the district attorney's office. Defendant appealed from his conviction and argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict him. The court ruled that by failing to challenge the witness's identification at trial, defendant waived the issue of the constitutionality of the identification. The witness maintained that she recognized defendant as the victim's killer when she saw him in the district attorney's office. The court could not conclude that there was insufficient evidence to convict defendant. The trial court's ruling not to offer a general theory of defense instruction without a theory of prosecution instruction was not error. Defendant did not request a specific theory of defense instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the order of the trial court.

State v. Dahlk


No. 81-1681-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


111 Wis. 2d 287; 330 N.W.2d 611; 1983 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3204


May 17, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
January 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Mark A. Frankel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a jury trial of violating Wis. Stat. § 945.04(1), permitting real estate under his control to be used as a gambling place. Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction and the order denying his motion to dismiss the amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged after undercover police officers attended meetings in a warehouse owned by defendant in which a pyramid scheme was introduced. All money transactions were to be completed in the warehouse. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held as follows: 1) the trial court did not err in allowing the State to file an amended complaint because the amendment expanded the factual basis to include club activities conducted on other dates but did not change the charge; 2) the amended complaint alleged facts which, if proven, showed that defendant's pyramid club redistributed money among individuals by a process which, although accompanied by some salesmanship, was predominantly controlled by chance and it therefore stated sufficient facts to constitute the offense charged, that defendant permitted the operation of a lottery on his premises, within the meaning and intent of Wis. Stat. § 945.04(1); and 3) defendant failed to show that § 945.04(1) was unconstitutionally vague for failure to warn that a pyramiding scheme was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of permitting real estate under his control to be used as a gambling place.

State v. Van Dyke


No. 81-1808-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


110 Wis. 2d 741; 330 N.W.2d 247; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4258



December 28, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 8, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL D. GUOLEE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of attempted murder, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.01, 939.32, one count of armed robbery, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.32(1)(a), (2), and six counts of first-degree murder, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, among other things, he was denied his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to counsel and deprived of his U.S. Const. amend. V right against self-incrimination and that the trial court erred when it found that there was no misjoinder of the counts. In affirming, the court held that: (1) there was no violation of defendant's Sixth Amendment right to counsel at the time of questioning about the murders because he was repeatedly advised of his Miranda rights, which included advisement of the right to counsel; (2) the trial court's findings that there was a knowing and voluntary waiver of defendant's Fifth Amendment rights were not against the great weight and clear preponderance of the evidence, and the State had met its burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt; (3) there was no misjoinder because there were similar characteristics between the crimes, the crimes occurred over a short period of time in a relatively confined area of the city, and the crimes had common factors that established a common scheme or plan tending to establish defendant as the perpetrator; (4) the imposition of six consecutive life sentences did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re M.T.


No. 81-291


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


110 Wis. 2d 741; 330 N.W.2d 247; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4317



December 28, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 8, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: EDWIN C. DAHLBERG, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which terminated her parental rights to her two minor children.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the trial court abused its discretion in terminating her parental rights and that it did not make sufficient findings of fact upon which to base its finding of unfitness. The court held that (1) the ultimate decision whether to terminate parental rights was discretionary and that it would not find an abuse of that discretion if the record showed that discretion was exercised and if there was a reasonable basis for the court's determination; (2) the trial court's findings that there was a lack of substantial relationship between the children and either parent, that it would be in their best interests to sever the relationship, and that it was unlikely that either child could enter into a more permanent and stable family relationship with the mother were rational in light of the applicable law and thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in terminating the mother's parental rights; (3) the trial court was not required to make additional evidentiary findings to support its finding of the mother's unfitness because the facts it found were sufficient to support the ultimate issue of her unfitness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which terminated the mother's parental rights.

STATE v. PETERSON

Defendant was convicted with possession of a controlled substance (marijuana), with intent to deliver, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance (marijuana), with intent to deliver, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m)(b). After the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence obtained by a search warrant, defendant entered a guilty plea. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

STATE v. CITY OF BELOIT


No. 82-527


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


110 Wis. 2d 744; 330 N.W.2d 249; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4266



December 22, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JAMES L. CARLSON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which refused to dismiss citations issued to the city's garbage trucks and held that weighing procedures by appellee State of Wisconsin (State) by a motor vehicle inspector were valid.


OVERVIEW: On four occasions, garbage truck drivers for the city received citations for violating weight tolerances while operating on class A highways. The garbage truck drivers had been stopped by motor vehicle inspectors who had the garbage trucks weighed using a method where weight was calculated using the rear axle. A trial was held on the four citations. The city sought dismissal of the citations arguing that Wis. Stat. § 348.15(3)(b) set forth tolerances and not weight limit prohibitions. Despite the city's allegations of improper weighing procedures and of being cited under an ineffective statutory subsection, the trial court refused to dismiss the complaints. The trial court imposed fines, penalties and costs against the city. The city appealed contending that even if the scale readings were accurate in all four cases, reversal was required because § 348.15(3)(b)'s prohibition portion was repealed leaving only the explanatory segment of the statute under which a party could not be charged. The court found that the city's proposed interpretation of § 348.15(3)(b) created an absurd result, thus affirmed the trial court order denying dismissal of the citations against the city.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment against the city was affirmed.

STATE v. FERRARA


No. 82-658-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


110 Wis. 2d 744; 330 N.W.2d 249; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4291



December 21, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 8, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Polk county: ROBERT O. WEISEL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of three counts of third-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3). He also appealed from an order denying postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to establish the element of non-consent. He also contended that § 940.225(3) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the case and that the statute unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to defendant on the issue of consent. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and that the statute was not vague and did not shift the burden of proof. The court noted that the complainant testified that she did not consent and that testimony of other witnesses present at the scene established beyond a reasonable doubt that the acts defendant construed as consent were the product of threats of force and violence. The court concluded that the evidence showed that consent was not freely given as required by § 940.225(4). The State proved words and actions indicating non-consent and that the subsequent acquiescence of the complainant was not freely given.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and order denying postconviction relief.

STATE v. CHURCHILL

Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which denied his post-conviction motion to withdraw his plea of no contest to a charge of battery in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.19.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's plea was entered pursuant to a plea bargain. In return for the plea, the State agreed to dismiss one count of the original charge alleging that defendant was a "repeater" subject to enhanced penalties under Wis. Stat. § 939.62, and to recommend a 10-day jail sentence to be served consecutively to any time defendant was then serving. The State abided by the plea bargain. Defendant was found guilty of battery on his plea of no contest and was sentenced to two years' probation, with 10 days in county jail during non-working hours. Defendant filed a motion to withdraw the plea under Wis. Stat. § 974.06, which was denied. Defendant's post-conviction motion was based on the ground that the plea bargain was illusory because the repeater charge could not properly have been asserted against defendant, and thus that his plea was not knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily made. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's plea was voluntarily made and that the plea was not rendered involuntary by subsequent judicial determinations which were not sought by defendant, but which in retrospect diminished the value of the plea bargain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

MILLIGAN v. CICHACKI


No. 80-265, No. 80-266, No. 80-267


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


110 Wis. 2d 741; 330 N.W.2d 247; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4313



December 13, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge county, THOMAS W. WELLS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions plaintiff citizens challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) that dismissed their complaints against defendant city/employer alleging that defendant employee maliciously and unlawfully caused criminal complaints to issue against them and that the city was negligent in the hiring and continued employment of the employee in violation of common law negligence and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The issues raised by the appeal were whether the city was immune from liability under the part of Wis. Stat. § 895.43(4) (1977) that precluded actions for the intentional torts of city employees, whether the city was immune from liability under that part of § 895.43(4) that precluded actions for acts done in the exercise of legislative, quasi-legislative, judicial, or quasi-judicial functions, and whether the complaints stated a cause of action against the city under 42 U.S.C. § 1983. The court affirmed the orders, opining that the city's hiring and retention of the employee were discretionary acts and thus, under the Wisconsin approach, they were by definition accorded the same immunities given quasi-judicial or quasi-legislative acts under Wis. Stat. § 895.43(4) (1977). The court concluded that the citizens failed to state a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 cause of action against the city because their complaints alleged mere negligence while gross negligence or deliberate indifference was necessary at a minimum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

State v. Kay Distributing Co.


No. 82-715-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


110 Wis. 2d 29; 327 N.W.2d 188; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4045


October 18, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
November 23, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County: Nick F. Schaefer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) which dismissed a criminal complaint charging defendant with violation of Wis. Stat. § 66.054(8a)(i), prohibiting the sale of similar malt beverages at different prices to different retailers. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on the grounds that the complaint did not allege a crime and that § 66.054(8a)(i) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a wholesaler of fermented malt beverages. The State issued a criminal complaint against defendant charging it with four counts of selling similar quantities of fermented malt beverages at different prices to different retailers, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 66.054(8a)(i). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that it did not allege a crime under § 66.054(8a)(i) and that § 66.054(8a)(i) was unconstitutionally vague because the meaning of "similar quantities" was ambiguous. The trial court concluded that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and dismissed the complaint. The court reversed, concluding that § 66.054(8a)(i) was not unconstitutionally vague and that two of the four counts of the complaint were sufficient to establish probable cause. The court determined that the statutory language "similar quantities" was not unconstitutionally vague where such statutory language had a sufficiently definite meaning because of its common usage.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the criminal complaint against defendant because the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that two of the four counts of the criminal complaint were sufficient to establish probable cause and remanded those counts for trial.

In Interest of J.


No. 81-2267


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


110 Wis. 2d 7; 327 N.W.2d 198; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4056


March 1, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
November 23, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County: Henry B. Buslee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Nonfinal order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a juvenile, appealed from a nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), that ordered the juvenile waived in the action against him for first-degree murder, burglary, and attempted burglary.


OVERVIEW: The district attorney petitioned for waiver of the case against the juvenile. Prior to the waiver hearing, the juvenile presented a discovery demand to the district attorney, asserting authority to do so pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 48.293(2), 971.24(1) and 971.25(1). The district attorney refused to provide the information demanded, and the juvenile brought on a motion to compel discovery. When the trial judge denied the motion, the waiver hearing proceeded. The state submitted relevant testimony and evidence at both the prosecutive merit and waiver portions of the hearing. The juvenile was ordered waived. Upon discretionary review by the court the main issue was whether a juvenile had the same full discovery right prior to the prosecutive merit portion of a waiver hearing that was afforded to a criminal defendant prior to trial. The court held that a juvenile did not have such a right and affirmed. The court held that the plain wording of § 48.293 provided no access to peace officer reports or broad discovery of the type envisioned under the criminal discovery statutes, §§ 971.23 to 971.25, prior to a waiver hearing.


OUTCOME: The nonfinal order of the lower court ordering the juvenile waived was affirmed.
