Cornejo v. Polycon Industries, Inc.


No. 82-296


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 649; 327 N.W.2d 183; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4053


October 13, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
November 22, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Elliot N. Walstead, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent employer's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the employee's claims that the employer acted in bad faith, inflicted emotional distress, and committed fraud and outrage in its actions concerning the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was hired and injured his hand three days later. He returned to work a month later only to leave again with a disability certificate from a different doctor. He was fired for failing to call in three consecutive days of absence. The employee then filed a worker's compensation claim and alleged the employer unreasonably refused to rehire him after a work-related injury in violation of Wis. Stat. § 102.35(3). The employer was ordered to pay lost wages and attorneys' fees. The employee returned to work and was laid off three days later. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and found that the employee was barred from maintaining the action because of the availability of an exclusive remedy under § 102.35(3). The court also determined that the trial court's decision did not violation Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 because the employee was provided with his day in court to attempt to obtain a remedy provided by the legislature. The court found that the employee's exclusive remedy was found in the worker's compensation statutes and that to allow a different remedy would have undermined the legislative intent of the worker's compensation statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court to grant the employer's motion for summary judgment.

STATE v. BROWN


No. 82-1020-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


109 Wis. 2d 699; 328 N.W.2d 724; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4176



November 16, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LEE E. WELLS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of carrying a concealed weapon under Wis. Stat. § 941.23, and which denied his postconviction motions. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred by not granting his motion to suppress evidence, that § 941.23 was unconstitutional, and that there was no evidence that his gun was concealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car that police officers stopped for a traffic violation. The officers saw defendant remove something from his pocket and hide it under the front seat. The officers ordered defendant out of the car and found a gun partially hidden in the front seat. As a result, defendant was convicted under Wis. Stat. § 941.23 of carrying a concealed weapon. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: Defendant's actions gave the officers sufficient concern for their safety to order defendant out of the car, to pat him down, and to look into the car. Because an officer could see part of the gun in plain view, the gun could not be suppressed. Because an interrogating officer gave defendant his Miranda rights before defendant made his statements, the statements could not be suppressed. The court had to follow the Wisconsin Supreme Court's holding that § 941.23 was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, and that § 941.23 did not require the State to prove specific intent. Because the gun was only partially visible, it was concealed as defined by § 941.23.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State ex rel. La Follett v. Board of Supervisors


Nos. 81-1119, 81-1805


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 621; 327 N.W.2d 161; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4050


October 20, 1982, Oral Argument  
November 10, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Daniel P. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Milwaukee County Board of Supervisors and the Milwaukee County Executive, challenged a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granting a writ of mandamus, which found ministerial duties on their part to, respectively, raise capital funds for appellee Milwaukee Metropolitan Sewerage District and to approve any board resolution to that end.


OVERVIEW: The county board approved by resolution a bond issue to finance the sewerage district's capital budget, but the county executive's inaction resulted in the bond issue's demise. The trial court granted mandamus, finding the county board and county executive had ministerial duties. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statutory obligation of the county board to provide financing to the sewerage district was subject to the county executive's veto power under the state constitution. The trial court abused its discretion by compelling mandamus because the county executive's duties were not clear and unequivocal, and mandamus was appropriate only where such duties were clear and unequivocal. Because the county executive had power to veto the resolution, mandamus was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and order granting the sewerage district a writ of mandamus.

 

1847 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Killebrew


No. 81-1345-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 611; 327 N.W.2d 155; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4046


March 2, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
November 9, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Mark A. Frankel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint charging defendant with escape from a correctional camp system in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.42(3) on the ground that it violated defendant's double jeopardy rights.


OVERVIEW: After defendant, who had been convicted of forgery and driving a motor vehicle without consent, was transferred to a correctional camp, he left the camp without permission. Upon return to custody, he was charged with violating a prison administrative rule and was placed in "program segregation." He sought dismissal of the pending criminal escape charge on double jeopardy grounds, and the trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that double jeopardy considerations did not bar the imposition of both criminal and administrative sanctions in the form of segregation from the general prison population imposed for conduct which violated both a criminal statute and a prison rule. The court's inquiry focused on the question of whether the administrative discipline was intended as punishment for the escape. It weighed the purposes of the double jeopardy clause, the nature of defendant's interests, and the character of the administrative decision. The court concluded that the primary purpose of the administrative sanction was not punitive; instead, it sought to correct defendant's behavior and to maintain prison security and order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

In re K.C.


No. 82-246


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


109 Wis. 2d 697; 327 N.W.2d 723; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4199



November 4, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: F. H. SCHLIGHTING, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which terminated their parental rights under Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) (1977), as amended by 1979 Wis. Laws ch. 330.


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the parents' parental rights. They appealed arguing, among other things, that Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) (1977), as amended by 1979 Wis. Laws ch. 330, was unconstitutionally vague, and denied them equal protection. Further, the parents claimed there was insufficient evidence to justify termination. The court upheld the trial court's order. First, the court held that the parents lacked standing to challenge whether § 48.40(2)(b) was unconstitutionally vague. The court reasoned the parents fell within the hardcore of § 48.40(2)(b) proscriptions because of their conduct. The court specifically noted that, among other things, the record showed that the parents were of very low mentality, could not maintain a household, and the mother exhibited strange behavior toward the newborn at the hospital. The court reasoned that given all of the factors, they did not have standing to raise the vagueness issue, and were given fair notice. Second, the court held no equal protection violation arose because § 48.40(2)(b) provided a substantial objective guideline that evenhandedly applied to all persons. Last, the court held the evidence sufficiently justified termination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Holy Name School of Congregation of Holy Name of Jesus v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 81-2245


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 381; 326 N.W.2d 121; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4044


August 16, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
October 19, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County: Gordon Myse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer, a Catholic school, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), affirming a decision of the Labor and Industry Review Commission that had affirmed a decision of respondent, the Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations, that respondent employee, a teacher, was qualified to receive unemployment compensation benefits pursuant to Chapter 108 of the Unemployment Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: The teacher had agreed to live by Catholic principles when she started at the school. When she planned to marry a divorced man, she was informed that, according to Catholic tenets, her fiancee's prior marriage had to be annulled and that failure to do so would be a breach of her contract. The board of education decided not to renew her contract, although she could reapply once her marriage was blessed. Although the annulment process was initiated, the teacher married before it was completed because of a family crisis. She applied for unemployment compensation, and the Department determined that she was entitled to unemployment benefits because she was not discharged for "misconduct" under Wis. Stat. § 108.04(5). The appeal tribunal affirmed and also found that she did not voluntarily terminate her employment under Wis. Stat. § 108.04(7)(a). The Commission also affirmed, finding that the teacher had not intended to leave her employment. The circuit court and the court also affirmed, the latter concluding that the Commission's findings of fact were supported by credible and substantial evidence that the teacher did not wilfully or intentionally disregard her employer's interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's affirmation of the Commission's decision that the teacher was entitled to unemployment benefits.

State v. Williamson


No. 81-1961-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 83; 325 N.W.2d 360; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3947


August 24, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
September 27, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Lee E. Wells, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of the misdemeanor offense of carrying a concealed weapon contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.23.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of carrying a concealed weapon when a police officer discovered defendant had a gun after the officer stopped and subsequently frisked defendant. At the time defendant was stopped and frisked, he was with a friend who had previously been arrested for carrying a concealed weapon. Defendant appealed. In reversing the judgment of conviction, the court held that the evidence against defendant should have been suppressed because the stop and subsequent frisk of defendant was illegal and unconstitutional where a person of reasonable caution would not have believed that the police officer's actions were appropriate because the officer was not able to point to particular facts from which he reasonably inferred that defendant was armed and dangerous where he based the stop on the fact that defendant was looking around and pointed at the officer's squad car, made a furtive gesture, and then turned and walked away when the police officer exited his squad car. The court further held that defendant's mere propinquity to his friend who in the past had been arrested for carrying a concealed weapon, without more, did not justify frisking him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause.

Grogan v. Public Service Com.


No. 81-1947


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 75; 325 N.W.2d 82; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3942


May 13, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
September 22, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: William C. Sachtjen, Reserve Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions to enter judgment declaring sec. PSC 136.02(4) (b)4, Wis. Admin. Code, invalid insofar as it prohibits the supply of natural gas for outdoor residential lighting for plaintiffs' gas lights ordered and received prior to March 1, 1980, and to determine whether an order should be entered restraining the commission from enforcing secs. PSC 134.062(2) (e) and 136.10, Wis. Admin. Code.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which was entered for defendant Public Service Commission of Wisconsin in the homeowners' action for a declaratory judgment to invalidate rules that prohibited the supply of natural gas for outdoor residential lighting. The homeowners' action also sought an order to restrain the Commission from enforcing certain rules.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners filed an action for a declaratory judgment invalidating the Commission's rules that prohibited the supply of natural gas for outdoor residential lighting and for an order to restrain enforcement of the rules. The trial court found that the homeowners owned gas lights that they operated before the effective date of the challenged rules but entered a judgment that declared that the rules were valid. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment. The court remanded the case with directions to enter a judgment declaring that Wis. Admin. Code § PSC 136.02(4)(b)(4) was invalid insofar as it prohibited the supply of natural gas for the homeowners' lights and to determine whether an order should be entered restraining the enforcement of Wis. Admin. Code §§ PSC 134.062(2)(e), 136.10. The court concluded that the Commission's implied general authority to regulate for conservation purposes was limited by the express provisions of Wis. Stat. § 196.97. The court further concluded that the Commission lacked authority to prohibit the supply of natural gas to lights that were ordered and received before the effective date of its rule that specified gas lights as a nonessential use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against the homeowners. The court remanded the case with directions to enter a judgment declaring a rule of the Commission invalid insofar as it prohibited the supply of natural gas for the homeowners' outdoor residential lighting and to determine whether an order should be entered restraining the Commission from enforcing certain rules.

 

1852 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 81-1895-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 64; 325 N.W.2d 76; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3949


June 8, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
September 21, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Vilas County: Timothy L. Vocke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Vilas County (Wisconsin), which convicted them of failing to cause their minor child to attend school as required by Wis. Stat. § 118.15(1)(a). Defendants contended that the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction over them, that it erred in denying their motion for a bill of particulars and in its allocation of the burden of proof, and that § 118.15(1)(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants pled guilty to charges that they failed to cause their six-year-old son to attend school in violation of Wis. Stat. § 118.15(1)(a). The court found that defendants' guilty pleas constituted a waiver of nonjurisdictional defects and defenses including claims of constitutional violations prior to the plea. The trial court's misallocation of the burden of proof involved a possible due process deprivation that was waived by their guilty plea. Defendants were also precluded from challenging the trial court's personal jurisdiction over them. The court affirmed defendants' convictions, finding that the criminal complaint alleged the material elements of the crime and that § 118.15(1)(a) was constitutional as applied. By citing the proper statutory basis for the crime and by including factual allegations relating to the elements of the crime charged, the complaint charged a legally known offense. The statute's failure to define "private school" did not render it unconstitutionally vague because common usage and other statutory provisions regarding private schools supplied a definition such that persons of ordinary intelligence did not need to guess the statute's meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

1853 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Brockmeyer v. Dun & Bradstreet


No. 81-2024


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 44; 325 N.W.2d 70; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3945; 115 L.R.R.M. 4029


August 2, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
September 10, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Ralph G. Gorenstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of plaintiff employee in his wrongful discharge action.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated from his position with the employer due to several problems that had appeared in the office that was under his supervision, which included an open affair with his secretary and general lack of attentiveness to his duties. The employee filed a wrongful discharge action on the ground that the employer's conduct violated the State's public policy set forth pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 111.01. At the conclusion of the trial, the employee's request that § 111.01 have been included in the jury instructions was denied, but the trial court still found in his favor. On appeal, the court reversed. The court ruled that based on the employee's record of problematic behavior within the company and his refusal to submit a written report about the course of events that led to the resignation of the secretary, the employer acted honestly and in good faith where they exercised proper business judgment in reaching the decision to terminate the employee, who was an employee at-will. Because there was no evidence of retaliatory action or bad faith, the employer's decision to terminate the employee was not a wrongful discharge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the employer in the employee's wrongful discharge action.

In re Long


No. 81-1550


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


109 Wis. 2d 685; 325 N.W.2d 737; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4008



September 7, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie county: URBAN P. VAN SUSTEREN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant invalid challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which found that the invalid was incompetent and in need of protective services for her person and estate, in an action filed by respondent county department of social services for guardianship and protective placement. The invalid contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the finding of incompetency.


OVERVIEW: The department of social services filed an action for guardianship and protective placement for the invalid. The trial court found that the invalid was 76 years old and had liver disease. Her only income was a monthly Social Security check for $ 367. The invalid lived in an apartment above a neighbor who assisted her with daily life. The trial court found that the neighbor did not adequately care for the invalid. The trial court held that the invalid was incompetent and in need of protective services for her person and estate. The invalid appealed and contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the judgment. The court affirmed and held that the invalid's physical impairments substantially impeded her ability to care for herself. The court found that the invalid was also incompetent to manage her estate. The invalid turned her monthly checks over to the neighbor and relied upon him to use the money for her necessities. The neighbor took the money without providing for such necessities and the invalid did nothing to protest. The court also held that the invalid did not have a right to a jury trial under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5 since it been waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Milwaukee County v. Milwaukee Dist. Council 48-American Federation of State, etc.


No. 81-1185


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


109 Wis. 2d 14; 325 N.W.2d 350; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3948


April 26, 1982, Argued  
September 7, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leander J. Foley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied its motion for a temporary injunction and granted respondent district council's motion for summary judgment in an action challenging the constitutionality of the Municipal Employment Relations Act (MERA), Wis. Stat. § 111.70.


OVERVIEW: After a mediator was appointed pursuant to the MERA to determine whether an impasse in negotiations between the county and the council required the appointment of a mediator-arbitrator, the county filed an action against the council, seeking a temporary injunction declaring Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4) unconstitutional because it illegally delegated legislative authority to mediators-arbitrators. The trial court granted the council's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that: (1) the MERA's legislative purpose was ascertainable; (2) the statute provided sufficient standards to guide the arbitrators; and (3) adequate procedural and judicial safeguards existed. Thus, the statute satisfied the necessary constitutional requirements. The county's authority to fix or change the compensation of its employees was not impaired by participating in binding arbitration. Finally, the court found that the MERA did not violate the equal protection or due process clauses of either the United States or the Wisconsin Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1856 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


LAJSIC v. PERKINS


No. 81-2355


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


109 Wis. 2d 688; 325 N.W.2d 738; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3978



September 3, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: HARVEY L. NEELEN, Reserve Judge. Reversed and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sellers challenged the order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) dismissing their third-party complaint against third-party defendant home builder in a suit by plaintiff purchasers against the sellers resulting from a leaky basement.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers bought a home from the sellers. After the purchaser discovered water leakage in the basement, they sued the sellers, alleging breach of warranty, or alternatively, fraudulent or negligent misrepresentation. Thereafter, the sellers filed a third-party complaint against the builder, arguing that it had breached the construction contract because the home had not been constructed in a workmanlike manner. Alternatively, they alleged a right to indemnification from the builder if the purchasers were successful in their underlying action. The trial court dismissed the third-party complaint on the basis that it was barred by the six-year statute of limitations set forth in Wis. Stat. § 893.43. The trial court ruled that the statute of limitations commenced to run on the date of the execution of the construction contract. On appeal, the court noted that in a breach of contract action, the statute of limitations commenced to run on the date of the breach. Because under § 893.43, the issue was the date of the breach, the court reversed the order and remanded the cause so that the trial court could determine on which date the cause of action accrued.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the third-party complaint was reversed and the matter was remanded with directions.

 

1857 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. 81-1981-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 703; 324 N.W.2d 447; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3776


June 28, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
August 25, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: William U. Zievers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of soliciting for prostitution, under Wis. Stat. § 944.32, and denied his motion to vacate the judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of soliciting for prostitution under § 944.32. After his motion to vacate the judgment was denied, defendant sought review. On appeal defendant argued that § 944.32 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad on its face. The court agreed with the verdict, and upheld that constitutionality of § 944.32. The court held that § 944.32 was directed at speakers who intentionally proposed an illegal commercial transaction, and that thus it did not implicate speech protected by the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that the requirement in § 944.32 that the speaker have a specific intent to accomplish an unlawful purpose mitigated whatever vagueness there may be in the notice given by the term "solicit," as used in the statute, and insured that the statute could not be properly be applied to innocent activity. Because the testimony covered every element of § 944.32, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the verdict. Further, the court held that it was reasonable to punish solicitation of ongoing prostitution more severely than solicitation of a single felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the trial court.

Boller v. Commercial Ins.


No. 81-1764


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


108 Wis. 2d 783; 324 N.W.2d 831; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3902



August 18, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied October 11, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: MAX RASKIN, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed in part; reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a rental center and its insurer, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which held that the center was negligent per se, awarded treble damages, and reduced the amount of compensatory damages awarded to respondents, a minor child and her guardian ad litem. The child, by the guardian, had filed a negligence action against the center and its insurer for damages when she was attacked by a dog.


OVERVIEW: A rental center owned a German shepherd dog, which was allowed on the center's property outside of the building and had previously injured a boy. Later, as a six-year old child, who came to the rental center with her father, stopped to pet the dog, she was attacked, and the child then filed a negligence action against the rental center and its insurer seeking damages resulting therefrom. On appeal from a judgment for the child, the court held that: (1) there was sufficient evidence to conclude that the rental center was negligent as a matter of law for allowing its dog to roam the business premises because it failed to exercise ordinary care to control the dog, knowing that it had previously bitten a child; (2) there was no error in ruling that the rental center was negligent as a matter of law prior to the close of its case because the remaining testimonies were merely cumulative; and (3) the elements for treble damages under Wis. Stat. §§ 174.01, 174.04 (1977) were satisfied because the dog's acts constituted a "sudden assault," the previous child was "peacefully walking" when he was injured, and the attack on the child herein occurred outside the owner's enclosure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment finding that the rental center was negligent as a matter of law, and reversed that part of the trial court's judgment reducing the jury's award for compensatory damages. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to enter a judgment on the basis of the jury's findings.

In re Baby Girl K


No. 82-087


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


108 Wis. 2d 785; 324 N.W.2d 833; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3908



August 17, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Granted October 19, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon county: LEO D. CROOKS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the father of a minor child, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), terminating his parental rights to the child pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6)(a)2.


OVERVIEW: The mother testified that the father, who was incarcerated in the fifth month of her pregnancy, did not aid her in any way, and that he once tried to strangle her and twice asked her to smuggle marijuana into prison. The child was placed in a foster home immediately after birth. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. It held that the gender-based classification in § 48.415(6)(a)2, which required an unwed father to develop a substantial relationship with his child in order to retain parental rights, was substantially related to an important governmental objective of promoting the best interests of children and thus did not violate the father's equal protection rights. It held that the finding that termination of parental rights was in the child's best interests was supported by the overwhelming weight of the evidence of the father's lack of responsibility; that the evidence supported the finding that the father had an opportunity to develop a substantial relationship as required by § 48.415(6)(a)2 despite his incarceration; and that a specific finding of unfitness was unnecessary where termination of parental rights was so clearly in the child's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Zinn v. State


No. 81-1772


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


108 Wis. 2d 783; 324 N.W.2d 831; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3874



August 5, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Granted October 11, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Washington county: J. TOM MERRIAM, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Wisconsin, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), denying the State's motion to dismiss a complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The complaint was brought against the State by respondent property owner, alleging damages for temporary inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR) made a determination of the ordinary high watermark (OHWM) of a small lake on the owner's property that brought 200 acres of the owner's dry land within the OHWM in an expanded version of the once small lake, giving the public and all abutting property owners access to her property up to the high watermark and giving the public access to the actual lake. On the owner's petition for rehearing, the DNR reestablished the OHWM at an elevation placing the small lake wholly within the owner's property and considering no dry land as part of the lake bed. The complaint characterized the period between the rulings as an unconstitutional taking and sought damages as well as compensation for litigation expenses for recovering the land. The court reversed the order and dismissed the suit. It reasoned that the erroneous determination had only a temporary effect, as there was only about a month before rehearing was granted, immediately rescinding the effect of the initial hearing under Wis. Stat. § 227.12; further, there was no restriction upon the owner's use of her property as required to constitute a taking.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

Reserve Life Ins. Co. v. La Follette


No. 81-1467


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 637; 323 N.W.2d 173; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3766


March 2, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
July 27, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed its complaint against defendants, the Attorney General and Insurance Commissioner, seeking a judgment declaring that Wis. Stat. § 207.04(1)(m) was unconstitutional in that it violated the Contracts Clause of the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions as applied to the insurer's health insurance policies issued before June 16, 1974.


OVERVIEW: Under § 207.041(1)(m), refusing to offer inclusion of coverage for the services of chiropractors on health insurance polices issued on renewed after June 16, 1974 constituted an unfair or deceptive act. The insurer had renewed over 800 polices without offering coverage for chiropractic treatment, and it sought a declaration that § 207.041(1)(m) was unconstitutional because it violated the contracts clause. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the insurer's complaint. The court held that the statute did apply to existing contractual relationships, and the renewal of each health policy resulted in a continuation rather than a new and independent contract. Further, forcing the insurer to offer additional coverage compelled it to undertake an obligation beyond that to which it had agreed, and thus § 207.041(1)(m) did impair the insurer's existing contractual relationship arising out of policies renewed after June 16. 1974. However, it was undisputed that the insurer could increase its premiums to meet the cost of the additional coverage, and it failed to demonstrate, as required, that the impairment to its continued polices was substantial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1862 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue v. J. C. Penney Co.


No. 81-1740


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 662; 323 N.W.2d 168; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3764


April 8, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
July 27, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: W.L. Jackman, Reserve Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for entry of an order consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of revenue sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by the state tax appeals commission in an action to assess a use tax against respondent department store on catalogs and advertising supplements known as "preprints."


OVERVIEW: The department assessed a use tax against the store on its catalogs shipped from Indiana to Wisconsin and on its preprints distributed with Wisconsin newspapers. The store appealed the assessment and the commission found in favor of the store. The circuit court affirmed the commission's decision. The department appealed and argued that the store "used" the catalogs in Wisconsin. The court concluded that the catalogs remained the property of the printer until they were delivered. After delivery, the recipients assumed ownership of the catalogs and were free to read, keep, or destroy them. The store contended that its preprints fell within the newspaper exception to the tax. The court found that the preprints contained only advertising for the store's products and that, standing alone, they did not fit the definition of "newspaper." The store maintained that it escaped liability because it did not store, use, or otherwise consume the preprints in Wisconsin. The court held that the facts established a use of the preprints in Wisconsin and that they were owned by the store after their delivery to the newspaper and before they were delivered to their ultimate recipients.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order with respect to the catalogs but reversed the order with respect to the preprints and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Mowers v. St. Francis


No. 81-2108


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


108 Wis. 2d 630; 323 N.W.2d 157; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3771


June 16, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
July 23, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: William A. Jennaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to respondent city in the property owners' action for declaratory relief as to the validity of certain special assessments levied against their abutting properties pursuant to a city ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The city levied special assessments against the property owners' abutting properties pursuant to a resolution authorizing the same which was adopted pursuant to a city ordinance. The property owners contended that the city ordinance was invalid because it exceeded the authority granted to municipalities by Wis. Stat. ch. 66 to levy special assessments. The property owners also contended that the city was equitably estopped from denying the validity of the ordinance at issue because the action it took in vacating the ordinance was equivalent to conceding its invalidity. The trial court granted summary judgment to the city and dismissed the property owners' action as moot after the city vacated the resolution authorizing the special assessments. The court held that the city's action in vacating the resolution was exactly the remedy the property owners sought and thus, the dismissal of their action was not action taken to their detriment. Thus, the elements of equitable estoppel were not met. The court further held that the city ordinance at issue was not unconstitutional because it was enacted under the police power given to the city by Wis. Stat. § 66.62.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1864 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lesieur


No. 81-1187-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


108 Wis. 2d 777; 324 N.W.2d 828; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3808



July 20, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied October 12, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of second-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(a) and sentenced him to four years imprisonment. Defendant also appealed an order denying his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury regarding the meaning of sexual contact employing the language of § 940.225(5)(a). Defendant claimed that the instruction diluted the State's burden of proof of an element of the charged offense to something less than the beyond a reasonable doubt standard. Defendant further argued that the error was not harmless. The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial, finding that an instruction on sexual contact that employed the language of § 940.225(5)(a) impermissibly reduced the State's burden of proving an element of the offense of sexual assault. Further, the court could not say that the instruction was harmless because the facts in evidence raised the possibility that the contact was accidental. Defendant also challenged the portion of the jury instruction that explained the "without consent" element of § 940.225(2)(a). The court held that where a person was charged with violating § 940.225(2)(a) and the victim was under 15 years of age, non-consent was not an element of the offense. Thus, there was no conclusive presumption due process problem when the trial court instructed the jury that a person under 15 could not consent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and order and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

1865 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Town of Liberty Grove v. Weborg


No. 81-2088


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


108 Wis. 2d 780; 324 N.W.2d 830; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3829



July 20, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for Door county: EDWIN C. STEPHAN, Judge. affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owners of commercial fishing vessels challenged small claims judgments of the Circuit Court for Door County (Wisconsin) for unpaid personal property taxes assessed by plaintiff town on their vessels for two taxable years.


OVERVIEW: The town presented its case by a stipulation on the record acknowledging that unpaid assessments for personal property taxes had been made against the owners' vessels. The owners alleged that their vessels were exempt from taxation under Wis. Stat. § 70.15 and that, if the vessels were not exempt, the taxing statute violated the Equal Protection and Commerce Clauses of the United States Constitution. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the town. The owners offered no competent and substantial credible evidence proving a violation of the Equal Protection Clause. A state's taxation of a vessel owned by one of its citizens and having a situs in the state was not unconstitutional even though the vessel was used in interstate commerce. The owners did not show that their vessels were exempt under § 70.15. There was a presumption against the exemption, and the testimony of a single witness who did not know the amount of interstate use of the disputed vessels during the years in question was insufficient to rebut the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgments.

Waage v. Waage


No. 81-1796


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


108 Wis. 2d 779; 324 N.W.2d 829; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3823

NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent ex-husband sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which rendered judgment in a divorce proceeding between the husband and petitioner ex-wife. The husband alleged that the trial court abused its discretion in dividing the estate, in establishing the valuation of property, and in setting the amount he was required to pay in property taxes, insurance, maintenance, and guardian ad litem fees.


OVERVIEW: The husband appealed from certain aspects of the divorce judgment. The court affirmed that portion of the judgment ordering the husband to pay homeowner's insurance, property taxes, and mortgage payments, as these amounts were supported in the record. The husband was properly ordered to pay the major portion of the guardian ad litem fees, as the fees were incurred because the husband raised a constitutional challenge to the joint custody statute without serving the requisite notice for such a challenge. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in requiring the husband to pay maintenance during the pendency of the proceedings even though the wife was a registered nurse. It properly considered the emotional effect of the divorce on the wife's failure to seek employment for nine months. The court noted an arithmetical error regarding the net value of the assets held by the husband and remanded for new findings. It also directed the trial court to set forth its findings regarding the value and ownership of certain property. It found that the trial court abused its discretion in not setting forth what Wis. Stat. § 767.255 factors it considered in dividing the estate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with respect to the amounts the husband was required to pay in taxes, insurance, maintenance, and guardian ad litem fees. It reversed the judgment with respect to the division of the marital estate and the valuation and distribution of certain assets. The court remanded for the trial court to review the evidence and to state its findings and decision on those issues.

State v. Reynosa


No. 81-1825-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


108 Wis. 2d 775; 324 N.W.2d 298; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3710



June 21, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied August 17, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order and a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL J. SKWIERAWSKI, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of first degree murder, party to a crime, and denied her motion for a new trial based upon newly discovered evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant while in a tavern with her son walked up to the victim and made a derogatory comment to her. Defendant then grabbed the victim by the blouse. Defendant's son grabbed the victim by the hair and appeared to be punching her in the stomach area. The victim was lying on the floor in a pool of blood. After the stabbing defendant remained in the tavern and stated that she had screwed the victim. Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, party to a crime. Her motion for a new trial was denied. On review, defendant's major assertions were that the trial court erred when it refused to give a lesser-included instruction on manslaughter heat of passion and that the evidence was insufficient as a matter of law to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of the crime of first degree murder, party to a crime. The court held that there was no evidence that defendant had the requisite state of mind to justify the submission of a manslaughter heat of passion instruction. The court ruled that considering defendant's behavior at the scene of the crime the jury could have found that defendant desired to aid in the commission of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first degree murder, party to a crime, and the denial of her motion for a new trial based upon newly discovered evidence.

 

1868 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re A.L.R.


No. 81-1292


Court of appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


108 Wis. 2d 772; 324 N.W.2d 296; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3763



June 18, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied September 1, 1982


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: W. L. JACKMAN, Reserve Judge, presiding. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Order affirmed.  


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which terminated her parental rights to her daughter under Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2) (1977).


OVERVIEW: After being adjudicated as a "child in need of protection and services," (CHIPS), the trial court granted the State's petition under Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) (1977) to terminate a mother's rights. On appeal, the court considered the mother's attack on the statute's constitutionality, despite her failure to serve notice on the Attorney General as required under Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11), concluding that the mother's belated notice after oral argument was sufficient to cure any defect. The court then reviewed the statute de novo and held that the mother had not met her burden of proving that Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) was vague, overbroad, a violation of equal protection or due process, or an abuse of the prosecutor's discretion. The court then reviewed the findings and determined that they supported its conclusion that the mother's parental rights should be terminated. Furthermore, although not required to consider the child's best interests because the petition was filed before those factors were required to be considered in a TPR, the court held that the trial court did not err in concluding that it was in child's best interests that the mother's parental rights be terminated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court terminating a mother's parental rights.

St. Luke's Hosp. v. Peterson


No. 81-1591


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


108 Wis. 2d 772; 324 N.W.2d 297; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3732



June 11, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Racine county: JAMES WILBERSHIDE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a hospital patient and personal injury plaintiff, and his attorney, sought review of a summary judgment from the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), entered for respondent hospital on its lien claim under Wis. Stat. § 779.80.


OVERVIEW: The hospital treated the patient when he was injured in a motorcycle accident. It had a lien for the cost of the services under § 779.80. The attorney negotiated a settlement of the patient's claim with the tortfeasor's insurer. The insurer sent the attorney two checks, one in the amount of the hospital lien, payable jointly to appellants and the hospital, and one for the balance payable to appellants. The attorney refused to release the first check to the hospital unless it recognized his lien for the cost of collection. In affirming the summary judgment for the hospital, the court first declined to review appellants' claim, raised for the first time on appeal, that the hospital lien must be subject to reasonable attorney fees or § 779.80 would be unconstitutional. The court then noted that the hospital had not contracted for collection and satisfaction of the hospital lien with the attorney or the patient. Thus appellants' claim was equitable in nature. But the court noted that appellants had failed to give the hospital timely notice of their claim, which was essential to permit their recovery on equitable principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for the hospital.

 

1870 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cannon v. Moran


No. 81-420


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 669; 321 N.W.2d 550; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3583


October 28, 1981, Argued  
May 25, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: W.L. Jackman, Reserve Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Director of State Courts and the Secretary of the Department of Employee Trust Funds, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted judgment in favor of respondent employees and held that 1979 Wis. Laws 38 was invalid because it impaired the retirement contracts of the employees and deprived them of property without due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The employees initiated an action against the Director and the Secretary contending that 1979 Wis. Laws 38 was unconstitutional because it impaired their retirement contracts. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the employees and held that the statute deprived them of property without due process of law. U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 outlawed any state law which impaired the obligation of contracts. The court found that legislation impaired a contract if it altered the contractual relationship between the parties. However, the court determined that the statute had not directly affected the terms of the pension contracts between the employees and the employers. The court held that, in the absence of contractual or constitutional restraints, the legislature was allowed to alter public salaries and public pensions at will. The court determined that the statute was not violative of the equal protection provisions of the U.S. and state constitutions, and that it was valid as to the employees. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the trial court and held that the law impairing the employees' retirement contracts was not unconstitutional and was not depriving them of due process of law.

Jenks v. Wisconsin Dep't of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 81-1540


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 714; 321 N.W.2d 347; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3585


March 18, 1982, Submitted on Briefs  
May 25, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to review denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael J. Barron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff union presidents appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that affirmed defendant Labor & Industry Review Commission of Wisconsin's holding and found for defendants Wisconsin Department of Industry and employer. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 108.04(10) was constitutional and that nonstriking employees who lost work through a strike were ineligible for unemployment benefits.


OVERVIEW: The Labor and Industry Review Commission of Wisconsin (LIRC) rendered a judgment for the Wisconsin Department of Industry and an employer and found that under Wis. Stat. § 108.04(10) nonstriking employees that lost their jobs because of another union's strike with their employer were ineligible for unemployment compensation benefits even if they had not supported the strike. This decision was challenged by some union presidents but affirmed by the trial court and the court. Generally, the LIRC's findings of fact were conclusive if supported by substantial evidence, and its determinations on questions of law were given great weight and sustained if reasonable. The court found that the trial court correctly deferred to the LIRC's interpretation of § 108.04(10), which accorded with the plain meaning of that statute. The court also found that § 108.04(10) was constitutional under the Equal Protection Clause because it created reasonable classifications that were based upon substantial distinctions, that were germane to the purpose of law, that were based upon existing circumstances, that applied equally to all members of the classifications, and that were conducive to the public good.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's findings that the commission's decision denying benefits was warranted and that the challenged statute was constitutional.

Tri-State Home Improv. Co. v. Labor & Industry Review Comm'n


No. 81-1731


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


107 Wis. 2d 748; 322 N.W.2d 701; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3619



May 21, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Granted


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: PATRICK T. SHEEDY, Judge. Reversed and cause remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which reversed and set aside the Commission's decision that affirmed a determination by the Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations that respondent company's salesmen were employees for purposes of unemployment compensation.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that the first question to be decided was whether the company met its burden to show that its salesmen were not its statutory employees by showing that they were free from the company's direction and control and by showing that the salesmen were customarily engaged in independently established businesses as required by Wis. Stat. § 108.02(3)(b). The court reversed the judgment, finding that the company effectively limited and controlled which sales tactics the salesmen engaged in by use of a contract checklist. The court found that use of the checklist controlled the representations made by the salesmen to potential customers. Further, the court determined that the company failed to establish that the salesmen were engaged in independently established trades, businesses, or professions because the salesmen had no ownership interest or investment in materials. The company also contended that Wis. Stat. § 108.02(5)(k)6 and 7 were unconstitutional in that they denied the company equal protection and violated the uniform taxation provision of Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court concluded that the company had no standing to raise the issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause.

VILLAGE OF WHITEFISH BAY v. CONSOER-TOWNSEND & ASSOCS.


No. 81-251


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


107 Wis. 2d 745; 322 N.W.2d 699; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3600



May 17, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LOUIS J. CECI, Judge. Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Wisconsin Supreme Court, which vacated the judgment affirming the trial court, the appeal of plaintiffs, the Village of Whitefish Bay, the Village of Fox Point, and the City of Glendale, from the trial court's decision dismissing their complaint against defendant contractors, was reconsidered. The trial court dismissed the action, denied the cause of action for fraud, and denied the motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs hired the contractors to construct a municipal water facility. During the construction, a water main was disconnected and reconnected by the contractors. About 15 years later, the water main broke and plaintiffs filed the action alleging it was due to the unworkmanlike manner in which it was reconnected. The trial court dismissed the action. The court originally affirmed, but the supreme court vacated the decision and remanded. On remand, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court held that the water main was an improvement to real property with the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 893.155 and was subject to its limitations. The court found, however, that the statute applied prospectively and did not bar plaintiffs' claim. The court found that under Wis. Stat. § 802.03(2), the claim for fraud had to be stated with particularity and include the elements that 1) an untrue statement of fact was made, 2) it was made with the intent to defraud and for the purpose of inducing the other party to act on it, and 3) the other party did rely on it and was injured. The court found that plaintiffs had not alleged facts sufficient to establish fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment of the trial court that denied the fraud claim. The court reversed the part of the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the claim for damages.

STATE v. HELMS


No. 81-1728


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


107 Wis. 2d 748; 322 N.W.2d 701; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3671



May 14, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Grant county: JOHN R. WAGNER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction from the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle after suspension of her driver's license. She failed to appear, was found guilty, was sentenced to five days in the county jail with Huber privileges, and was assessed for impaneling the jury. She contended that the trial court erred by assessing costs under Wis. Stat. § 814.51, and ordering her to pay for impanelment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that assessment of costs and jury impanelment fees fell within the discretion of the trial court. Where the trial court had based its findings on facts in the record and reliance on appropriate law, they could not be disturbed on review. Although assessment of jury impanelment fees for failure to appear was not specifically provided for in Wis. Stat. § 814.51, the court had the assessment power to insure efficient management of court business. The court next considered defendant's equal protection challenge on her claim that, as she was imprisoned in another county because she was a woman, that her sentence was unconstitutional, The court held that Wis. Stat. § 973.03(1) permitted the county, at its expense, to house a prisoner in an appropriate facility. Defendant's county did not have jail facilities for women.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and assessment of costs.

 

1875 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HASSE


No. 81-1979-CR-NM


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


107 Wis. 2d 744; 321 N.W.2d 366; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4349



April 27, 1982, RELEASED  
April 27, 1982, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Wisconsin), which convicted him of three counts of tampering with electric meters, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.36(1)(b). The public defender's office filed a no merit report pursuant to Wis. R. Crim. P., Wis. Stat. § 809.32, concluding that further proceedings on behalf of defendant would be frivolous and without arguable merit.


OVERVIEW: After a close examination of the record, the court agreed with the no merit report filed by the public defender and concluded that further proceedings on behalf of defendant would be frivolous and without arguable merit. Defendant's motion to suppress all evidence seized by employees of Wisconsin Public Service at his farm had no merit because the evidence was not seized by the police and the search was not prohibited by the Fourth Amendment as defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in the electric meters and wires installed on his property. There was no basis for suppressing a detective's observation of a "framed door assembly" inside defendant's home because the detective was invited in by one of defendant's children and the framed door assembly was in plain view. Contrary to defendant's argument, Wis. Stat. § 196.171, relating to the inspection of utility equipment by utility employees, authorized the seizure of the items taken. The trial court's rulings on the admissibility of various other evidence were not error, and a jury instruction describing the statutory presumption in Wis. Stat. § 941.36(2) did not contain an unconstitutional presumption of guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1876 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stubbendick


No. 81-908-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


107 Wis. 2d 739; 321 N.W.2d 364; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3558



March 26, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Rock county: MARK J. FARNUM, Judge. Judgment of conviction for assault modified and, as modified affirmed. Judgment of conviction for burglary affirmed. Order denying postconviction relief modified and, as modified, affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --The sentence appealed from for second-degree sexual assault is reduced from ten years to not more than six years and, as modified, the judgment and order denying postconviction relief are affirmed. The judgment of conviction and sentence for burglary and the order denying postconviction relief on that sentence are affirmed. The sentence for sexual assault shall run concurrently with the burglary sentence. Defendant shall receive credit on each sentence for time incarcerated on the vacated and modified sentences for second-degree sexual assault.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of burglary and second-degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.10(1)(a), 940.225(2)(a). He also appealed an order denying postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the trial court unconstitutionally imposed a longer sentence after a trial than the prior sentence it had imposed on defendant's no contest plea and subsequently vacated. The court held that the increased sentence for sexual assault deprived defendant due process because it was not based on objective facts unknown to the trial court at the time of the first sentence. When imposing the 10-year sentence for sexual assault, the trial court had before it essentially the same objective information in the presentence report as it had when sentencing defendant to six years. The trial court did not state that it relied on procedural history, defendant's employment record before his no contest plea, or an innocuous prison record when imposing the longer sentence. It did not include those facts among its reasons for the harsher sentence, which it had to do if the sentence was to be sustained. The trial court's belief that defendant might have feigned remorse when first sentenced and was not remorseful at the second sentencing was not an objective fact. Defendant's right to due process was not denied by the sentence for burglary because it was the original sentence.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentence for sexual assault by reducing it from 10 to not more than six years. As modified, the court affirmed the sexual assault judgment and order denying postconviction relief. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence for burglary and the order denying postconviction relief on that sentence. The court ordered that the sexual assault sentence run concurrently with the burglary sentence.

 

1877 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. DYES v. ISRAEL


No. 81-1699


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


107 Wis. 2d 743; 321 N.W.2d 367; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3561



March 26, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge county: HENRY G. GERGEN, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate contended that the forfeiture of good time earned while serving prior sentences, which was forfeited in connection with an earlier parole revocation, violated his constitutional right to due process and the standards of fundamental fairness.


OVERVIEW: In 1955 the inmate was sentenced to prison for not more than 30 years. Twice he was released on parole, and on each occasion he violated his parole by committing a serious crime and was returned to prison. When he was released on parole for a third time, he had more than 11 years of good time credits. He again violated parole, and parole revocation proceedings were initiated. The inmate signed a standard waiver of hearing form, which advised him of his due process right to a revocation hearing and that one consequence of a parole revocation could be loss of earned good time. When all of the inmate's good time was automatically forfeited, he petitioned for habeas corpus claiming that the forfeiture of good time violated his constitutional right to due process and standards of fundamental fairness. The court rejected the petition. Wis. Stat. § 53.11(7)(b), which required an automatic forfeiture of good time upon revocation of parole, was not declared unconstitutional until after the inmate's parole was revoked, and the decision declaring the statute unconstitutional did not apply retroactively. Accordingly, it was immaterial whether the inmate knew his good time could be forfeited.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Fontana v. Fontana-on-Geneva Lake


No. 81-654


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 226; 319 N.W.2d 900; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3432


December 31, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
March 25, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County: Robert H. Gollmar, Reserve Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which granted a refund of property taxes levied against respondent resort hotel.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the assessment was void because the assessor failed to consider the best information he could practicably obtain, the actual costs of construction of a new addition. The trial court then determined the proper amount of reassessment based on a subsequent sale of the property. The village argued that the taxpayer had the obligation to present the assessor with evidence and that the assessor was not required to seek out evidence of actual construction costs. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that (1) the assessor had an obligation to use the best information available; (2) the actual construction cost figures were recent and substantiated; (3) accurate figures showing actual costs gave better information on which to form the basis of an assessment than a mere estimate; and (4) the trial court had the authority to determine the amount of taxes, regardless of whether the court proceeded under Wis. Stat. § 74.74 or Wis. Stat. § 75.54.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the resort hotel in its action against the village for a refund of property taxes.

STERNBERG v. TESCH


No. 81-1723


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


107 Wis. 2d 743; 321 N.W.2d 367; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3531



March 23, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon county: DANIEL L. LaROCQUE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed, with $ 500 attorney's fees plus costs to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint against respondent tenants for their breach of an apartment lease. The judgment also awarded double damages and attorney's fees to the tenants for the landlord's failure to return their security deposit in violation of Wis. Admin. Code § Ag. 134.06.


OVERVIEW: The landlord rented an apartment to the tenants pursuant to a written lease. After complaining about the amount of heat the landlord was providing, the tenants notified the landlord by letter that if he could not maintain sufficient heat, they would move out of the apartment the following month. The landlord responded by advising them that he considered their letter as a notice of their intention to vacate the apartment. The landlord thereafter initiated suit for rent on the remaining lease, damages to the apartment, and costs for rerenting. On appeal from the dismissal of the suit and award of double damages and attorney fees, the court affirmed. The court held that the landlord was estopped from claiming rent after the date effective in the landlord's letter. The landlord's letter was an act upon which the tenants could and did reasonably rely to their detriment. The trial court did not err in its application of Wis. Admin. Code § Ag. 134.06, which required the landlord to return the tenants' security deposit within 21 days of their surrender of their premises or be liable for double damages and attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which dismissed the complaint and awarded the tenants double damages and attorney fees. The court awarded attorney's fees plus costs to the tenants.

 

1880 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Noranda Exploration, Inc. v. Ostrom


No. 81-236


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 205; 320 N.W.2d 530; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3423; 76 Oil & Gas Rep. 370


November 19, 1981, Argued  
March 23, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Oneida County: Timothy L. Vocke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants state officials appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), in favor of plaintiff mineral explorer in the explorer's suit to have Wis. Stat. § 107.15 declared unconstitutional. Defendants alleged that § 107.15 was a valid exercise of the State's police power and did not unconstitutionally take the explorer's property or impair its contracts.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 107.15 required an explorer to provide the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR) with geologic data obtained from exploration drill holes and Wis. Stat. § 107.15(4)(f) limited the confidentiality period. The explorer sued state officials and a trial court declared Wis. Stat. § 107.15 unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and held as follows: Section 107.15 provided the State with information useful for a variety of environmental and tax purposes. Thus, § 107.15 had a reasonable and rational relationship to the furtherance of the public welfare and was a valid exercise of police power. The diminution of the value of the data after the confidentiality period did not render the data useless to the explorer. Thus, § 107.15 was not a taking in violation of U.S Const. amend V and XIV or Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. Because Wis. Stat. § 107.15 was a reasonable exercise in police power, it did not violate the contracts clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Wis. Const. art. I, § 12 although Wis. Stat. § 107.15 did affect a confidentiality clause in a contract that the explorer had with a landowner. Therefore, § 107.15 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.
