Janesville v. County of Rock


No. 81-2241


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


107 Wis. 2d 187; 319 N.W.2d 891; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3429


February 24, 1982, Argued  
March 19, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County: Gerald W. Jaeckle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county, its board of supervisors, and its clerk, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) in a declaratory judgment action brought by respondents, three cities located in the county. The circuit court agreed with the cities that the county was required to adopt its original tentative plan to withdraw its supervisory districts following the 1980 federal census.


OVERVIEW: In response to requirements set forth in Wis. Stat. Ann. §§ 5.15(1)(a), 5.15(2)(a), 59.03(3)(b)2 (Supp. 1981), which required cities with a population of 1,000 or more timely to establish wards following publication of the final result of a federal decennial census, appellants adopted a tentative plan fixing the boundaries of its supervisory districts and submitted the plan to the cities. Each city then redrew its ward boundaries to satisfy statutory requirements and conform to appellants' tentative plan. Appellants then came back to the cities, asking that they once again redraw their ward boundaries to accommodate a new tentative plan. Refusing to do so because the 60-day window of time had expired, the cities filed suit. On appeal, appellants contended that in the absence of fraud or arbitrary action, the judiciary was without power to compel appellants to adopt or refrain from adopting particular reapportionment legislation. The court found judicial relief was in fact available because appellants failed to follow the statutory requirements for redistricting. The court determined that appellants had been properly enjoined to adopt a plan based upon the original tentative plan.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1882 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re M.M.G.


No. 81-832


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


107 Wis. 2d 738; 321 N.W.2d 364; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3556



March 18, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: JOHN H. LUSSOW, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County, which denied their motion to vacate orders which terminated their parental rights to their three children.


OVERVIEW: One of the parents' children was convicted of sexually assaulting a sibling. Two adult males babysitting for the children also sexually assaulted the child. The parents continued to use the adult males as babysitters even after learning of the sexual assaults. The children had behavioral problems that improved dramatically upon removal from the home. The parents denied any problems and did not take advantage of counseling, therapy, and a day care program offered by the county. The trial court terminated their parental rights and denied their motion to vacate the termination orders. The court affirmed finding that the parents could not complain that Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) was vague because failing to remove children from the presence of a babysitter known by a parent to have sexually assaulted one of them was plainly within the zone of hard core conduct that would form the grounds for termination of parental rights. The court held that because any reasonable person would know that the parents' parental rights would be put in jeopardy by their conduct, they had no standing to challenge the application of the statute to them on the ground of vagueness.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court denying the parent's motion to vacate orders which terminated their parental rights was affirmed.

STATE v. QUADRINI


No. 81-241-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


106 Wis. 2d 774; 319 N.W.2d 178; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3362



February 23, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: WILLIAM U. ZIEVERS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree murder, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made incriminating custodial statements, and he challenged the trial court's refusal to suppress them. In affirming the conviction the court held that the statements were voluntary. The court noted that the statements were not involuntary simply because the conversation between the police and defendant moved from lighter, general matters to those surrounding the crime. The court also held that the statements were not obtained in violation of defendant's right to counsel, holding that the standard for waiver was the same for the rights secured by U.S. Const. amend. V and VI, and further noting that although defendant stated that his lawyer had told him not to make a statement, defendant also stated that he did not want a lawyer present during the conversation. The court then held that the trial court properly excluded psychiatric testimony offered by defendant on the issue of his intent. Finally the court held that defendant's waiver of trial by jury was properly refused, noting that this result was mandated by Wis. Stat. § 972.02(1) when the State withheld consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction.

 

1884 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. CHURCHILL


No. 81-1694-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


106 Wis. 2d 777; 319 N.W.2d 180; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3418



February 23, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock county: EDWIN C. DAHLBERG, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order denying new trial is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for a new trial after he was convicted of criminal damage to property. Defendant alleged that he was denied his right to an impartial jury because he did not realize that one juror knew his mother; that the trial court improperly admitted evidence of other crimes, and that newly discovered evidence required a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant slashed his former girlfriend's tires and was convicted of criminal damage to property under Wis. Stat. § 943.01(1). The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: A post trial hearing was held on defendant's claim of juror bias, but the trial court found that defendant was not biased because one juror belatedly realized that she knew defendant's mother. The juror had stated on voir dire that she would try the case solely on the evidence and the instructions. Thus, defendant was not deprived of his right to an impartial jury under U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV and under Wis. Const. art. I, § 7. Under Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2), the trial court properly admitted evidence of defendant's other tire slashings to show identity and motive because all the tire slashings were similar and near in time. The invalidation of five of defendant's eight prior convictions did not require a new trial under a claim of newly discovered evidence because it was not reasonably probable that the new evidence would result in an acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1885 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sandy v. Sandy


No. 81-873


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 230; 316 N.W.2d 164; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3267


October 28, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
January 27, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Robert V. Baker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a divorce action, appellant wife challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which provided that custody of the children of the wife and respondent husband and exclusive possession of the parties' home were to alternate between them every two months.


OVERVIEW: In issuing its order, the trial court determined that the family court commissioner had inherent authority to enter the order because it was in the "best interests of the children." The wife asserted that the family court commissioner and trial judge lacked authority to order a party to vacate the home during a divorce action unless there was some showing of actual or threatened domestic violence pursuant to Wis. Stat. §767.23(1m) and Wis. Stat. § 813.025(2). Based on legislative history, the court rejected the wife's arguments and found that the family court commissioner and trial judge did have such authority when the order to vacate was issued after notice and a hearing, and the order was necessary to protect the best interests of the children. The family court commissioner's order in this case was entered after a contested hearing and was therefore, affirmed. In addition, the requirement of showing physical violence under § 813.025(2) only applied to ex parte orders and did not affect the authority of family court commissioners to order a spouse to vacate a parties' home during a divorce action after notice and hearing. The commissioner did not abuse his discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Hoffman


No. 80-1224-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


106 Wis. 2d 185; 316 N.W.2d 143; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3268


October 28, 1981, Argued  
January 26, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Michael B. Torphy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that convicted her of one count of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of first degree murder. A witness, who testified against defendant at a preliminary hearing, later died and defendant was charged with his murder. Defendant was found guilty of murdering the original victim but not the second. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that additional evidence was not required to recharge defendant because the first preliminary hearing culminated in a bindover and the State did not seek to accomplish at the second preliminary what it was unable to accomplish at the first. The court determined that even if the allegations, which defendant claimed were false, were stricken it did not alter the court's holding that the complaint stated probable cause. The offenses were not misjoined because they were of the same type and occurred over a relatively short period of time. Defendant's motion for severance was properly denied because she did not demonstrate substantial prejudice. The prosecutor's questions and comments directed solely to her parents' failure to come forward with certain information did not constitute impermissible comment on defendant's silence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In Interest of SDR


No. 81-914


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


106 Wis. 2d 772; 318 N.W.2d 26; 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3294



January 15, 1982 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition to Review Denied


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: WILLIAM D. GARDNER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county (Wisconsin) extending a dispositional order transferring the legal custody of appellant to the Department of Health and Social Services for a period of one year.


OVERVIEW: The State petitioned for an extension of appellant's dispositional order. When a hearing could not be scheduled prior to termination of the original dispositional period of one year, the trial court extended the original judgment for 30 days pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.365(6). A hearing was later held, and the trial court ordered the dispositional order extended. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 48.365 was constitutional and did not deprive appellant of his liberty without due process of law. The court found that Wis. Stat. §§ 48.355(4) and 48.365(6) were required to be read in pari materia to permit the original dispositional order to continue for one year and 30 days in those cases in which a petition for extension was timely filed but the trial court was unable to hold a full hearing before expiration of the original order. The trial court properly permitted the extension of the original dispositional order for a period not to exceed 30 days. Appellant was not deprived of his liberty without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Village of Whitefish Bay v. Consoer-Townsend


No. 81-251


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


105 Wis. 2d 763; 318 N.W.2d 22; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3415



December 23, 1981

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LOUIS J. CECI, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipalities sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the municipalities' complaint against appellee contractors on the basis of the expiration of the six-year statute of limitations for improvements to real estate, as provided in Wisc. Stat. § 893.155.


OVERVIEW: Three municipalities brought an action against two contractors, alleging negligence in the construction of a water main that broke and damaged the street above it. The lower court dismissed the action as untimely under the six-year statute of limitations of Wis. Stat. § 893.155. The municipalities appealed. On appeal, the court rejected the argument of the municipalities that the statute was unconstitutional, concluding that the municipalities had no vested property right until the pipeline burst and injury was sustained. The injury did not occur until after the enactment of the statute and thus precluded a determination that the statute was unconstitutional. The court also rejected the claim of the municipalities that their complaint also alleged fraud. The court found that the allegations of the complaint did not allege the specific pleading requirements of Wis. Stat. § 802.03(2). The court rejected the municipalities' claim to amend their complaint because they raised the issue for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

Wisconsin Public Serv. v. Public Serv. Comm'n


No. 79-1929


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


105 Wis. 2d 762; 318 N.W.2d 22; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3452



December 22, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order 1 of the circuit court for Brown county: ROBERT J. PARINS, Judge. Reversed. 


1 The Wisconsin Supreme Court determined on a prior appeal that this order was a final order from which an appeal could be taken. Bearns v. DILHR (WPA v. PSC), 102 Wis.2d 70, 306 N.W.2d 22 (1981).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Public Service Commission of Wisconsin (PSC), sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which remanded a PSC order that directed respondent, the Wisconsin Public Service Corporation (WPS), to place on its book certain expenditures incurred in seeking authority to construct a two-unit nuclear power generating facility in a town.


OVERVIEW: The WPS and other utilities submitted to the PSC a joint application for authority to construct power-generating facilities. The applicants withdrew their application with the consent of the PSC. Prior to withdrawal, they spent certain funds developing their application, an amount that they expected to capitalize when the project was completed. The expenditures did not appear on the utilities' books as operating expenses. The PSC held hearings related to the accounting treatment of the costs and ordered the accounting of the expenditures. Essentially, the PSC directed the WPS to write off the money spent in nuclear power plant development costs. The WPS contested certain aspects of the accounting treatment. The trial court determined that the PSC's method of accounting, which precluded the expenses from appearing as operating expenses, was inconsistent with the PSC's finding that the expenses were prudently made and not chargeable to stockholders. The court reversed the trial court and concluded that the PSC did not abuse its discretionary authority to direct the manner and form in which the utilities kept their books and that the order did not confiscate utility property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and reinstated the PSC's order that had directed the utilities to write off certain nuclear power plant development costs.

 

1890 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooley


No. 81-493-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 642; 315 N.W.2d 369; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3395


November 11, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
December 21, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael D. Guolee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) for the offense of second-degree sexual assault. The appeal raised the questions of whether a juror should have been dismissed for cause, whether defendant waived his right to a twelve-member jury, and whether the charging statute, Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2) (e), was unconstitutional, depriving the trial court of subject-matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: When a juror notified the trial court that she knew a State's witness, the juror was examined and voir dire was permitted. The trial court determined that the juror was impartial and denied defendant's motion to strike the juror for cause and grant a mistrial. The trial court granted defendant the option of proceeding with an eleven-member jury with the impartial juror removed. Defense counsel chose to proceed with the smaller jury. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court applied the correct standard and did not abuse its discretion in determining that the challenged juror was impartial. It was the exercise of the option of a smaller jury panel that raised the dispositive issue. Relying on decisions of the Wisconsin Supreme Court, which found the guaranty of a twelve-member jury in the Wisconsin Constitution, the court conclude that the procedural safeguards for waiver of trial by jury applied equally to waiver of a full twelve-member jury. Because the record did not indicate a waiver by defendant, the conviction would not stand. The contention that the trial court had no subject-matter jurisdiction was foreclosed by the court's decision in a case cited for reference.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment and order were reversed and the cause was remanded.

Ryder v. Israel


No. 81-657


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


105 Wis. 2d 764; 318 N.W.2d 23; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3460

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dodge county: THOMAS W. WELLS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a pro se petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the circuit court, alleging that a detainer warrant issued by the State of Illinois was unconstitutional. The inmate's public defender informed the inmate that the trial court did not have jurisdiction and referred the inmate to the Illinois' public defender office. The trial court subsequently entered an order denying the petition. The court affirmed, holding that the Uniform Interstate Agreement on Detainers applied only to outstanding indictments, informations, or complaints, and was inapplicable pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 976.05(1). Because the inmate had an adequate remedy when and if the State of Illinois demanded his return, the denial of the habeas corpus petition was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Teaching Assistants Ass'n v. Shain


No. 80-2274


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


105 Wis. 2d 759; 317 N.W.2d 510; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3540



November 24, 1981

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane county: RICHARD W. BARDWELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiffs, the association, its presidents, and others, to enforce a structured agreement and arbitration award against defendant chancellor, plaintiffs sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted the chancellor's motion for summary judgment on the ground of failure to state a cause of action, and dismissed plaintiffs' suit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued the chancellor, individually and in his capacity as chancellor, for an injunction and other relief, alleging that he exceeded his authority in terminating a structured agreement entered into by the Association and the university, and further alleging that he directed the university to fail to comply with an arbitration award. The trial court denied a preliminary injunction on the ground of sovereign immunity, because plaintiffs failed to establish jurisdiction over the state. I, § 10 because the chancellor did not enact a law impairing the obligations of contracts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing plaintiffs' suit.

State v. Linden


No. 81-1092-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


105 Wis. 2d 762; 317 N.W.2d 512; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3495



November 17, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: TED E. WEDEMEYER, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of misconduct in public office in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(5).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his conviction for misconduct in public office in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.12(5), defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction and that § 946.12(5) was unconstitutional. He also argued that the trial court should have instructed the jury on the defense of mistake pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.43(1). Affirming the conviction, the court found that the eight elements necessary for a conviction of misconduct in public office had been established. Defendant was a public employee at the time that the offense was committed, was acting under the color of his office or employment, and accepted a payment of $ 25.00 for his regular work from a person seeking a building permit. The money was for the performance of a service or duty, and defendant received a thing of value. The court held that the statute was constitutional as applied to defendant. The court rejected defendant's defense of mistake of fact. Defendant knew what the scope of his employment was and the fees set by law for an application for building permits. He knew what his compensation set by law was, and that the check for $ 25.00 was in excess of the fees and his salary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for misconduct in public office.

 

1894 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Nystrom v. Family Ins. Corp.


No. 81-156


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


105 Wis. 2d 759; 317 N.W.2d 510; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3517



November 10, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie county: GORDON MYSE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow brought an action based upon a work-related accident that resulted her in husband's death against respondent, her husband's co-employee and respondent insurer under the underinsured motorist provision of her husband's automobile insurance policy. The widow appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which dismissed her complaint with prejudice and denied her leave to amend her complaint.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the accident the decedent and the co-employee were working in the scope of their employment. After putting power steering fluid into a vehicle, the co-employee started the vehicle which he thought was in park. The vehicle, which was actually in second gear, lurched forward and struck the decedent causing his death. On appeal from a judgment dismissing her complaint, the widow argued that the provision that made worker's compensation an exclusive remedy, Wis. Stat. § 102.03(2), did not apply; that § 102.03(2) was unconstitutional; and that she was entitled to recover on the uninsured motorist provision of her husband's policy. The court rejected these arguments and affirmed. The court held that even though the co-employee operated the vehicle, the exemption under § 102.03(2) did not apply because the employer owned the vehicle. The statute was constitutional, and because the widow had received benefits under the statute, she could not attack its constitutionality. Because the court held that worker's compensation was the exclusive remedy, she was not entitled to recover damages from the person she identified as the uninsured motorist in her theory of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the widow's complaint with prejudice and denied her leave to amend.

 

1895 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


G. Heileman Brewing Co. v. La Crosse


No. 81-297


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 152; 312 N.W.2d 875; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3366; 25 A.L.R.4th 176


July 31, 1981, Argued  
October 27, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and Cross Appeals from an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County: Peter G. Pappas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed judgments of dismissal by the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) of four actions demanding the return of property taxes paid after another circuit court declared the type of property assessed to be exempt. Defendants, a city, a county, and the Wisconsin Department of Revenue (State) cross-appealed from the portion of the trial court's order which held that it had jurisdiction to hear the taxpayer's actions.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed for the return of property tax payments on certain property for four years after a circuit court in another county found that such property was exempt because it was manufacturing property or specific processing equipment and not real estate. The claims were denied, resulting in the instant actions. The trial court found for the State, and the court affirmed, agreeing that the trial court had jurisdiction and that the taxpayer's complaints did not state claims because the taxpayer had not filed the actions within one year of paying the contested taxes, as required by Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1). Although the taxpayer argued that the limitations period did not apply because the tax assessments were void ab initio, the court found that public policy required that even where tax assessments were void ab initio, a taxpayer could not recover if the taxes were voluntarily paid. However, the taxpayer had not pled that the payments were involuntary or made under protest. The State had an interest in allocating its resources, and a balancing of the parties' equities favored the State because it would have been injured by having to refund taxes that had already been spent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the State.

1897 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re K.


No. 80-1869


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


105 Wis. 2d 91; 312 N.W.2d 840; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3369


July 29, 1981, Argued  
October 7, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County: John Bolgert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent, the Sheboygan County Social Services Department, filed a complaint, petitioner father's parental rights to his six-year-old son were terminated based on Wis. Stat. § 48.40(b) (1977) and Wis. Stat. § 48.40(d) (1977). The father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to vacate the order which terminated his parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The father was to be imprisoned for 18 years for the second-degree murder of his wife. The circuit court granted the Department's petition to terminate the father's parental right based on Wis. Stat. §§ 48.40(b), (d) (1977), and denied the father's motion to vacate the order. In affirming the judgment and order, the court held that the father's claim that the §§ 48.40(b), (d) were void for vagueness failed because the statute did not carry the dangers of the absence of fair warning, the impermissible delegation of discretion, or the undue inhibition of the legitimate exercise of a constitutional right. The court held that due process did not require the circuit court to consider less restrictive alternatives to termination, and that no more was required than responsible determinations of unfitness and the best interests of the child. The court also held that the application of the preponderance of the evidence standard of proof was constitutional and did not violate the father's due process rights. The court found no abuse of discretion or constitutional error in the circuit court's failure to specifically label the Department's compelling state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied the father's motion to vacate the order which terminated his parental rights.

 

1898 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. DEER LAKE IMPROVEMENT ASSN. v. POLK CTY. BD. OF ADJUSTMENT


Nos. 80-2148, 80-2149


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


104 Wis. 2d 743; 314 N.W.2d 363; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3682



September 15, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Polk county: ROBERT O. WEISEL, Judge. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: By the Court.--Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the decision of appellee zoning board to grant appellee owner a special exception permit for the construction of a motel.


OVERVIEW: The association alleged the trial court erred in determining that certain requirements of the zoning ordinance did not apply where special exception permits were sought for uses such as motels. The association also argued the trial court erred in not conducting an evidentiary hearing. The court affirmed finding that the failure of the zoning board to require motel projects to meet the additional standards required of condominiums and multiple dwelling unit projects was not contrary to the intent of the ordinance. The court noted that the ordinance required consideration of twelve specific criteria before special exceptions could be granted for motels. The court followed the rules of statutory construction and concluded that the use of a colon in the local ordinance indicated that the following subsections related only to the uses specified in the ordinance. The court held that because none of the subsections referred to motels, those provisions did not apply to special exception permits for motels. The court concluded that the decision to take additional testimony as authorized by Wis. Stat. sec. 59.99(13) was discretionary and there was no abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court affirming the decision of the zoning board to grant the owner a special exception permit for the construction of a motel was affirmed.

 

1899 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF JANESVILLE v. JACKSON


No. 81-405


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


104 Wis. 2d 741; 313 N.W.2d 280; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3772



August 26, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: JOHN H. LUSSOW, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County requiring him to forfeit a sum of money for having operated a motor vehicle faster than the posted speed limit within the limits of a city contrary to Janesville, Wis., Ordinance § 10.04.010, which adopted Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(e).


OVERVIEW: A police officer drove alongside defendant in order to clock his speed before stopping him. Defendant alleged that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction, the city lacked standing, his constitutional rights were violated, and hearsay was improperly admitted. The court affirmed the judgment. The circuit court had jurisdiction to enforce penalties imposed by a city ordinance. The city had the power to enact its speed limit ordinance and the right to file an action to enforce it. Defendant was not entitled to a criminal prosecution because a city's action to enforce its ordinance was civil in nature. Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 17, required criminal actions to be prosecuted by the state alone and the penalty of a forfeiture was not a criminal sanction. The statutory requirement of a jury fee was not contrary to Wis. Const. art. I, § 5, and by failing to pay the fee defendant waived his right to a jury trial. Defendant had no right to counsel and was not entitled to be represented by a person who was not a licensed attorney. Records of the police officer's speedometer were business records pursuant to Wis. R. Evid., Wis. Stat. § 908.03(6) and therefore not inadmissible hearsay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court judgment that required defendant to forfeit a sum of money for having violated a municipal ordinance by operating a motor vehicle faster than the posted speed limit.

 

1900 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. WEBSTER


No. 80-1523


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


104 Wis. 2d 737; 313 N.W.2d 278; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3778



August 25, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court for Clark county: LOWELL D. SCHOENGARTH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin) for subjecting a child to cruel maltreatment, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.201.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a teacher at her husband's religious school. They believed that corporal punishment of students was biblically mandated and the parents must consent to it before their children were accepted as students. Defendant disciplined a child for not correctly repeating a word on a phonics card. She struck him repeatedly with the left side of a dowel-like pointer. An examining doctor testified that the child had moderate bruising. A sheriff's investigator testified that the bruising was severe. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The word cruel in the statute was not equated with intent to cause or with indifference to pain and a culpable mental state was not an element of the crime of child abuse. There was credible evidence that defendant inflicted severe pain and suffering. The jury was entitled to conclude that a necessity did not exist, notwithstanding defendant's religious beliefs. Defendant received effective assistance of counsel when a witness's discussion of the relative safety of the pointer was not relevant to the issue of whether the child's injuries constituted severe bruising and was not prejudicial to defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1901 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF RIPON v. RETZLAFF


No. 81-271


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


104 Wis. 2d 741; 313 N.W.2d 280; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3739



August 5, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac county: EUGENE F. McESSEY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin), which convicted him on a jury verdict of violating the City's disorderly conduct ordinance, which was the statutory counterpart of Wis. Stat. § 947.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another youth, who had dropped out of the City's high school, entered the school during school hours and flipped a lighted cigarette onto a classroom floor. That action disrupted the classroom, and the teacher went into the hall to investigate. Defendant then ran through the halls, further disrupting students and an open house. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict. Wis. Stat. § 66.12(1)(a) and Wis. Stat. § 968.07(1)(d) authorized the officer to make a warrantless arrest because the ordinance had a statutory counterpart. Further, defendant's counterclaim in response to the ordinance citation was not a valid pleading under Wis. Stat. § 66.12(1)(a). In the court's view, the prepayment of jury fees in an ordinance forfeiture action was not unconstitutional under either Wis. Const. art. I, § 5, or Wis. Const. art. I, § 9. A teacher's explanation that she went into the hallway to investigate the disturbance because she had been told that it was part of her duties was not hearsay. None of the evidentiary rulings complained of showed that the trial court was prejudiced against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1902 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. MYERS


No. 80-1760-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


104 Wis. 2d 738; 313 N.W.2d 278; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3761



August 5, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jefferson county: JOHN B. DANFORTH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second-degree sexual assault in violation Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(e), after a jury trial. The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) granting defendant's motion for a new trial. The trial court ruled that inadmissible evidence had so prejudiced the jury that a new trial must be granted.


OVERVIEW: During trial, the State offered evidence to prove that an act of intercourse had occurred and that the semen found on the victim could have come from defendant. The victim testified that she had not had any sexual intercourse for three days prior to the sexual assault, and a pathologist attempted to corroborate her testimony by stating that he had found semen in a sample taken from the victim. Defendant's objection to the pathologist's statement was sustained; however, it was not stricken from the record, nor was a cautionary instruction given to the jury. The trial court granted defendant's motion for a new trial, finding that the cumulative effect of the statements had created unfair prejudice. The State sought reversal, and defendant also argued that the trial court's instruction on the issue of consent improperly shifted the burden of proof from the State to defendant. The court affirmed, finding no abuse of discretion by the trial court, especially where the victim's testimony was corroborated by inadmissible evidence. The court also found no error in the jury instruction because the State still had to prove lack of consent as an element of the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1903 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bence v. Milwaukee


No. 80-1815


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


103 Wis. 2d 679; 309 N.W.2d 883; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3341


June 17, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
July 30, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leander J. Foley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a retirement fund, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which declared unconstitutional a portion of an ordinance that incorporated the terms of a collective bargaining agreement and thereby increased plaintiff retirees' benefits.


OVERVIEW: The retirees filed the instant action for declaratory relief and they alleged that a city ordinance which governed pension benefits denied them equal protection because its increased benefit payment provision distinguished between employees who retired on a particular date and those who retired after that date. The trial court declared unconstitutional the portion of the ordinance which set the distinguishing date for the increased retirement benefits. The court affirmed, holding that (1) there was no rational basis for distinguishing between employees who retired after the date specified in the ordinance from those who retired prior to that date because both groups of employees retired prior to the enactment and effective date of the ordinance; (2) the trial court properly determined that the date specified in the ordinance denied the retirees equal protection; and (3) the trial court properly severed the provision regarding the effective date for the increased pension benefits because the severance did not undermine the intent of the ordinance and it left intact the balance of the ordinance which described the nature of and conditions for pension benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1904 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Oliver v. Travelers Ins. Co.


No. 80-1681


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


103 Wis. 2d 644; 309 N.W.2d 383; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3333


May 29, 1981, Argued  
July 22, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County: John C. Ahlgrimm, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured driver sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, an insured and its insurer, in the driver's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The driver and the insured were co-employees. When the accident between them occurred, the driver was leaving work and the insured was on the job by driving an employer-owned vehicle. The insured along with the insurer responded to the driver's personal injury complaint by asserting that the driver's claim was barred by the provisions of the Worker's Compensation Act, Wis. Stat. § 102.03(2). The insured and the insurer were granted summary judgment and the driver sought review. He argued on review that § 102.03(2) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court found that if common law recovery of damages caused by a negligent co-employee were allowed, the economic burden suffered from industrial accidents would be unduly placed upon the shoulders of the workers rather than on the industry itself. The court rejected the driver's argument that the "certain remedy" clause of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 was violated by the application of Wis. Stat. § 102.03(2). The court held that absent a statutory foundation for suit, the certain remedy clause of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9, had not conferred on plaintiffs the right to bring a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of an insured and its insurer.

 

1905 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ELMBROOK GLASS & GEN. CONTRS., INC. v. FAUST


No. 80-1159


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


103 Wis. 2d 691; 310 N.W.2d 652; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4233



July 15, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: HAROLD J. WOLLENZIEN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which had granted recovery to appellee land contract vendor after her strict foreclosure on property destroyed by fire and already the subject of an action by two companies and an individual against the insurer for the value of the building under Wis. Stat. § 203.21 (1975).


OVERVIEW: The companies and the individual had filed the insurance suit seeking to recover under the policy, but the land contract vendor intervened in the action and was given a judgment on the value of the land under the policy. The insurer challenged the application of the statute and the right of the land contract vendor to recovery after a strict foreclosure. The court found that: (1) there had been no error in the application of § 203.21, which had been repealed, where the repeal was not retroactive and any repeal of the rights under the statute would have been an unconstitutional direct impairment of a contract right created under the law; (2) the limitations on a mortgagee's recovery on foreclosure did not apply to strict foreclosure on a land contract; and (3) the land contract vendor was entitled to the land and the insurance proceeds were the equivalent of the destroyed structure under the doctrine of equitable conversion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the land contract vendor and against the insurer.

 

1906 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. JOHNSON


No. 80-1108-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


103 Wis. 2d 691; 310 N.W.2d 652; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4232



July 8, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha county: NEAL P. NETTESHEIM, Judge. Judgment and order modified; sentence vacated; as modified and vacated, cause remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order modified; sentence vacated; as modified and vacated, cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of armed robbery while concealing his identity and the order that denied his motion for post-conviction relief, arguing that, because he used an imitation pistol, he did not use a dangerous weapon in committing the robbery and thus could not be convicted of armed robbery as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant used a replica pistol during a robbery and was charged with and convicted of armed robbery while concealing his identity. The trial court sentenced defendant to consecutive sentences of 10 years for the robbery and three years for the concealment. Defendant appealed. In modifying the judgment and order, the court concluded that, because the imitation pistol was not a dangerous weapon, defendant could not be convicted of armed robbery as a matter of law. While Wis. Stat. § 943.32(2) had been modified and in its current form permitted the jury to take into consideration the victim's subjective belief, the fact that the legislature amended the armed robbery statute reflected that its past definition of "dangerous weapon" did not include a replica of a gun. As such, the judgment was modified from a conviction of armed robbery to one of robbery while concealing identity. The sentence was vacated as erroneous, as concealing identity was not an independent substantive offense but created an aggravated form of the other crime. Upon remand, the trial court was directed to impose a single sentence, but it could consider concealment in so doing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief were modified to reflect a conviction for the offense of robbery rather than armed robbery. The sentences imposed were vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on the modified judgment.

 

1907 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Menomonee Falls v. Michelson


No. 80-1026


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


104 Wis. 2d 137; 311 N.W.2d 658; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3353


April 30, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
June 24, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: Harold J. Wollenzien, Judge. Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County: John P. Buckley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed; judgment vacated and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which declared that the homeowner was in violation of an ordinance from respondent village that required persons to disconnect any drain or other connection on their premises through which rain or surface water could be discharged into the public sanitary sewer system.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner argued that her constitutional rights were violated by the retrospective and selective application of the village ordinance. She also challenged the lower court's order that denied her demand for a jury trial. The court ruled that application of the ordinance to the homeowner was constitutional. The homeowner had no vested right to have a drain connection between her premises and the public sanitary sewer system. Therefore, her constitutional rights were not violated when the village required her to disconnect the drain. The court ruled that the right given to a property owner to connect with a municipal sewer was in the nature of a license only and did not become a vested right merely because an owner was put to considerable expense. The court also found that the homeowner's rights under the Equal Protection Clause were not violated because the village was not enforcing the ordinance against all homeowners at once. The homeowner failed to meet her burden of overcoming the presumption that the ordinance was being constitutionally administered. The court did hold that the homeowner had acquired a vested right in a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the lower court and remanded to the circuit court for a jury trial.

State v. Black Steer Steak House, Inc.


No. 80-1764-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 534; 307 N.W.2d 328; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3306


March 24, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
May 26, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County: Karl F. Peplau, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Wisconsin sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) that dismissed its criminal complaint against respondent steak house for the steak house's alleged violation of the credit restrictions imposed by Wis. Stat. § 176.05(23)(c) on retail liquor licensees.


OVERVIEW: The steak house was charged with purchasing intoxicating liquors on credit from a liquor wholesaler in violation of Wis. Stat. § 176.05(23)(c). The trial court dismissed the charge on the basis that the statute unconstitutionally discriminated against the steak house in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. On appeal, the State contended that even though the statute discriminated against the steak house, it was not unconstitutional because a rational basis for the discrimination existed. The court ruled that the steak house did not overcome the presumption of the constitutional validity of Wis. Stat. § 176.05(23)(c), noting that the rational basis for the passage of the statute was to prevent monopolistic practices in the liquor industry. The court held that because the steak house failed to show the nonexistence of this fact, the steak house failed prove that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case.

 

1910 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. AUGUSTINE


No. 80-1530-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


102 Wis. 2d 726; 308 N.W.2d 771; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4083



May 12, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: JOHN E. MALLOY, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) of the offense of possession of a container of tear gas contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.26(1). Defendant was ordered to pay a fine of $ 2500, or if not paid within 60 days to serve 60 days in jail with Huber privileges. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for a traffic offense, pursuant to which a body search was conducted. The police found a small container of chemical mace in defendant's pocket an charged him with possession of a container of tear gas, a class E felony under Wis. Stat. § 941.26(2). The penalty for committing a class E felony was a maximum fine of $ 10,000 or imprisonment not to exceed two years, or both. Defendant sought the imposition of sentence under § 939.61(1) on the grounds that sentencing him for a violation of a felony violated the equal protection clause and was cruel and unusual punishment. The court affirmed and noted defendant's point that a person who carried a concealed and dangerous weapon was guilty of a misdemeanor under § 941.23 and that a person who carried a switchblade knife was guilty of a misdemeanor under § 941.24. The court noted that legislative enactments were presumed to be constitutional. The court found that the legislature's attempt to prevent the use of tear gas as an offensive or defensive weapon was a legitimate concern and was a legitimate reason for imposing a more stringent penalty on the possession of tear gas than for possession of a concealed weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1911 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF MADISON v. SILLS


No. 80-1768


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


102 Wis. 2d 723; 308 N.W.2d 421; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4132



April 27, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane county: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: --judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) for making loud and unusual noise in violation of Madison, Wis., Gen. Ordinance 24.04(2). The appeal was not from the judgment of conviction but from pretrial orders denying the defendant's motion to dismiss the citation on grounds that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and, therefore, void.


OVERVIEW: The court denied the State's motion to dismiss under Wis. Stat. §§ 808.04 and 809.50 for failure to timely appeal because the issue of subject matter jurisdiction could not be waived. On review, defendant argued that the word "unusual" impinged on the First Amendment's protection of free speech. He conceded that the State had the power to regulate noise. The court concluded that the issue of the State's authority to regulate unusual noise was not properly before the court because defendant had only been charged with that portion of the ordinance relating to loud noise, not unusual noise. He lacked standing to challenge, on grounds of facial vagueness, the prohibition of unusual noise that may be unconstitutionally applied to others. A facial overbreadth adjudication, which would have allowed defendant to hypothesize as to possible unconstitutional applications of the ordinance, was not warranted because the ordinance did not regulate a pure form of expression such as a newspaper comment or a petition to a public official.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Federated Rural Electric Ins. v. Madison Equal Opportunity


No. 79-538


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


102 Wis. 2d 719; 308 N.W.2d 419; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4143; 26 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P32,077



April 27, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Dane county circuit court: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed from a judgment of the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment granting the motion of defendants, a city, its equal opportunity commission, and a discharged former employee of the company, to dismiss a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief in the company's action regarding an employment discrimination ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a complaint with the commission alleging that he had been fired because of his marital status (separated) and his physical appearance (less than conservative dress) in violation of Madison Wis., General Ordinance § 3.23. The commission found probable cause and scheduled a public hearing. In response, the company commenced this instant action seeking a declaration that the employment discrimination ordinance, § 3.23, was beyond the power of the city to act and that it was void under the federal constitution. In affirming the judgment of the circuit court, the court held that the power to prohibit employment discrimination based upon factors other than those prohibited by the Wisconsin Fair Employment Act (WFEA) was one which the legislature could confer on the city and, therefore, was one which the city possessed under Wis. Stat. § 62.11(5), the home rule amendment to Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3. These provisions did not violate the spirit of WFEA nor impede its purposes, but complemented them. Second, the court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendants.

 

1913 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. BROZOVICH


No. 80-1842-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


102 Wis. 2d 724; 308 N.W.2d 421; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4041



April 23, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county (Wisconsin) denying petitioner's motion seeking postconviction relief following petitioner's conviction for being a party to the crime of attempted burglary, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05, 939.32 and 943.10, and of possession of burglarious tools, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.12.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of being a party to the crime of attempted burglary and of possession of burglarious tools. He was also convicted of habitual criminality and was sentenced to consecutive prison terms. Petitioner filed a pro se motion to vacate the conviction and sentence. The trial court denied the motion.
