Also without merit was petitioner's argument that the conviction for possession of burglarious tools placed him in double jeopardy for the conviction of the attempted burglary. Each crime required proof of an additional fact that the other did not. And, the possession of burglarious tools was not a lesser included crime of attempted burglary. The court found that petitioner waived his objections to the party to a crime instruction given by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The denial of the postconviction motion was affirmed.

 

1914 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. STEVENS


No. 80-527-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


102 Wis. 2d 720; 308 N.W.2d 419; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4065



April 21, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county: MICHAEL S. FISHER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was questioned by police at a bar after she attempted to use a false identification card. She was ordered not to enter the tavern, but she was not arrested. Defendant's sister was subsequently arrested for driving without a valid license and defendant and her boyfriend followed the sister and the police to the station in their car. Defendant was questioned again at the station and she made a statement which contradicted her previous statement. She was arrested for obstructing an officer. A police officer brought defendant's purse inside the station with defendant's consent and a prison matron subsequently found marijuana inside it. Defendant pled guilty to possession of marijuana. The court held that (1) the fact that defendant gave conflicting information to the police officer constituted sufficient probable cause for him to believe that defendant was giving him false information and thus, her arrest was valid; (2) the search of defendant's purse was a proper inventory search and the marijuana, which was in plain view, was properly seized; and (3) defendant's purse was not unlawfully seized by police as defendant had consented to the retrieval of her purse from her car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1915 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Campbell


No. 80-335-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 243; 306 N.W.2d 272; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3289


October 24, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
April 21, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed, cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review after the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissed a criminal complaint against defendant for child abuse. The issue on appeal was whether the complaint stated probable cause to believe that defendant had violated Wis. Stat. § 940.201.


OVERVIEW: The complaint was based upon the statement of a woman who resided in the apartment next door to that occupied by defendant, his wife, and their 10-day-old baby. The complaint alleged that on a given date the three came to the woman's apartment at approximately 9:30 at night. The woman said that defendant claimed to have thrown the baby against the wall. She stated that she saw him blow marijuana smoke into the baby's face to induce sleep. The complaint was silent as to whether the baby suffered any injury as a consequence of defendant's alleged actions. The trial court dismissed the complaint, reasoning that physical injury to the child was a necessary element of the crime of cruel maltreatment under the child abuse statute. The court reversed and remanded. It was possible to imagine many types of such conduct that would have been unlikely to result in physical injury to the victim, but that would have been abhorrent to most. Physical injury was not an element of the crime of cruel maltreatment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the complaint against defendant and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1916 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Atl. Mut. Ins. Co. v. Steinpreis


No. 79-1646


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


102 Wis. 2d 719; 308 N.W.2d 419; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4148



April 10, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage county: JAMES H. LEVI, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant motorist appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which held that the motorist was liable to plaintiff, the subrogated collision insurer of another motorist, as a result of a collision between vehicles driven by the two motorists. The trial court found the motorist was 70 percent causally negligent and awarded the insurer 70 percent of the damage suffered by the insured to his vehicle.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the motorist argued, inter alia, that the trial court had denied him his right to a jury trial under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5, had erroneously held that subpoenas signed by the motorist were not valid, and had permitted the introduction of documents prepared by the insurer. The court agreed that the lower court had violated the motorist's right to a jury trial because there was no evidence in the record that the motorist had waived such right under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 805.01(2) and (3). The court rejected the motorist's argument that, because he was proceeding pro se, he had the authority to sign subpoenas under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 805.07(1). The court found that, under the express language of the Rule, subpoenas could be issued by any "attorney" of record and that that the subpoena power was thus not extended to pro se litigants. The court also concluded that a copy of the draft showing the payment to the insured and a computer printout that described the insured's policy and the claims that had been made had been properly authenticated under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 909.01 by the insurer's claims representative and were admissible as business records under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 908.03.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

1917 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Grand Bazaar Liquors, Inc. v. Milwaukee


No. 79-1712


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


102 Wis. 2d 208; 306 N.W.2d 255; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3290


February 17, 1981, Submitted on Briefs  
April 7, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael J. Barron, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which declared Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(2) valid. Appellant city appealed from the judgment declaring § 90-25.1(3) invalid. After the application for a liquor license was denied, the applicant sought a writ of mandamus commanding the city to issue the license and a judgment declaring the ordinance unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In a declaratory judgment proceeding, the trial court declared Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(2) constitutionally valid, and Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(3) invalid. The applicant argued that Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(2), which required every holder of a Class "A" liquor license to receive at least one-half of its income for the premises from liquor sales, was unconstitutional because it constituted an unreasonable and arbitrary exercise of the police power; denied equal protection of the laws; and violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The court held that the applicant failed to meet its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt the unconstitutionality of Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(2). The applicant failed to meet its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that no reasonable basis existed to support Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(3). The trial court erred in declaring Milwaukee City Code of Ordinances § 90-25.1(3) unconstitutional and that portion of the judgment was reversed, and the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment, which declared the section of the liquor ordinance exempting certain retailers unconstitutional, and affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

 

1918 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SAAVEDRA v. VILLAGE OF UNION GROVE


No. 80-1226


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


101 Wis. 2d 736; 306 N.W.2d 308; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3925



March 24, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine county: JAMES WILBERSHIDE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a village, a county, and a county sheriff, challenging the county's agreement to provide law enforcement services to the village. The Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief may be granted. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county entered into a contract under which it would furnish police services to the village. The county sheriff would retain full authority on the manner in which the services would be rendered. All arrests made by deputy sheriffs in the village were to be made under municipal ordinances whenever possible. Plaintiff was arrested by a county deputy sheriff within the village and charged with violating an ordinance. He filed an action challenging the contract of the county and the village. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the contract was authorized by Wis. Stat. § 59.083 (1977) where that provision vested a county board with all powers of a local, legislative, and administrative character, including police, where those powers could be exercised by the county board in any village on request of the village, and where the village could request that the county exercise such powers on certain terms and conditions which the county board could accept; (2) § 59.083 was presumed to be constitutional; and (3) plaintiff failed to show beyond a reasonable doubt that § 59.083 offended Wis. Const. art. VI, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1919 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SOMMER v. TOWN OF PINE LAKE


No. 80-1250


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


101 Wis. 2d 737; 309 N.W.2d 309; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3966



March 24, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Oneida county: DANIEL L. LaROCQUE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Jugment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a summary judgment of the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his complaint for recovery of real property taxes paid to respondent town.


OVERVIEW: The property owner complained that his property had been overassessed. The circuit court held that the owner had waived his right to contest the reassessment of his home because he refused the assessor's written request to view the interior of the home. The owner's position was that the view required by Wis. Stat. § 70.47(7)(aa) was limited to the exterior. In affirming the summary judgment the court first held that because the owner did not notify the attorney general, the court would not entertain his challenge to the constitutionality of the statute. The court then rejected the owner's construction of the statute, holding that the construction adopted by the Wisconsin Department of Revenue was not contrary to any legislative intent or history regarding the statute. The court also rejected the owner's contention that § 70.47(7)(aa) was a tax imposition statute requiring a restrictive construction. The court held that it was a procedural statute that should be liberally construed to permit a determination on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for the town.

 

1920 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vick


No. 80-1046


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


101 Wis. 2d 735; 306 N.W.2d 308; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3995



March 20, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63 (1).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the jury instructions created an unconstitutional presumption that he was under the influence of an intoxicant while he was driving from the fact that he was under the influence of an intoxicant at the time he was tested. In reversing, the court held that the phrase "within two hours after the alleged operation of a vehicle" could have caused the jury to believe or have bolstered the belief that evidence showing a blood alcohol level of 0.10 percent or more at any time within two hours of operation of the vehicle was sufficient evidence for finding that defendant was intoxicated at the time he drove his car. The proved fact in defendant's case was that his blood alcohol level was 0.13 percent at the time it was tested. The jury could have interpreted the instruction at issue to permit it to find from the proved fact that defendant was under the influence when he was driving his car. Accordingly, the instruction violated due process by being open to an interpretation creating such a presumption because under the facts, the court could not say that there was no reasonable possibility that the presumption could not have contributed to the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1921 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ANDERSON v. KINSEY


No 80-744


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


101 Wis. 2d 731; 306 N.W.2d 306; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3933



February 24, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county: JOHN P. BUCKLEY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee, who worked for the Wisconsin Department of Transportation, sought review of a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha county (Wisconsin), which dismissed her action against defendant supervisor seeking damages for slanderous statements allegedly made by the supervisor.


OVERVIEW: The employee had not claimed that the supervisor had started certain rumors about her health, but she had alleged that he perpetuated them and sought her discharge because of them. The supervisor had moved for dismissal based on the failure to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted and that the trial court lacked personal and/or subject matter jurisdiction. The action was dismissed because the employee had not complied with the notice requirements established by Wis. Stat. § 895.45(1) (1977). The employee sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court found that the employee admitted she had not filed a notice of claim within 90 days of the incident, as required by Wis. Stat. § 895.45(1). The court further ruled that the record supported the trial court's conclusion that no material factual issue existed which would have removed the case from the provisions of § 895.45(1). The court concluded that but for the supervisor's official responsibilities and duties, he would have had no occasion to make the alleged statements and that the notice requirements should have been met.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the employee's slander action.

 

1922 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re A. H.


No. 80-218


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


101 Wis. 2d 730; 306 N.W.2d 304; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4031



February 24, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from order of the circuit court for Columbia county: JAMES KARCH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court: --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother challenged a judgment by the circuit court for Columbia county (Wisconsin), which denied the mother's motion to vacate the trial court's order terminating her parental rights under Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(e), (b).


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that it was in the best interests of the child to terminate the mother's parental rights and place the child for adoption. On appeal, the mother argued that she was improperly denied a jury trial, the trial court applied an incorrect burden of proof, and there was insufficient evidence to establish grounds for termination. The court disagreed and affirmed the order of termination. First, the court held that under Wis. Stat. § 48.31(2) (1977), hearings under the children's code were to be held to the trial court, unless the parent demanded a jury trial. The mother's counsel made a strategic decision on her behalf to proceed before the trial court. She could not reopen the proceedings on hindsight. Second, the court held that the burden of proof was established by Wis. Stat. § 48.31(1) (1977), which required a "clear and convincing" standard. The trial court applied the correct standard. Third, the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the termination of the mother's rights. There was evidence of physical abuse by the mother's husband. The court held that the inability to protect the child constituted neglect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of termination.

 

1923 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ROOT


No. 80-786-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


101 Wis. 2d 731; 306 N.W.2d 306; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3882



February 18, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: TED E. WEDEMEYER, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court, in Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him on two counts of third degree sexual assault, placed him on probation for six months on each count consecutively, with a condition of probation that he serve each term in the house of correction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his conduct did not support separate counts of sexual assault because they were part of a single act of sexual intercourse, that he was entitled to a new trial because the trial court failed to instruct the jury on the weight of a false statement he made to the police, and that Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3), under which he was charged, was unconstitutional on the grounds of vagueness and overbreadth. The court affirmed the judgment. Defendant was properly charged and convicted of two offenses, which did not result in his being placed twice in jeopardy for the same offense. Each act required a separate volition and each resulted in a new and different degradation of the victim and a different invasion of her interest in being protected from sexual assault. The failure to give the omitted instruction was not error, as it was not requested by defendant's counsel and defendant was not prejudiced by the lack of the instruction. The statute was a constitutional exercise of the state's police power because it could not subject an individual to punishment for engaging in consensual sexual activities where there were no overt words or acts signifying consent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of two counts of third degree sexual assault.

 

1924 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nye


No. 80-219-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 398; 302 N.W.2d 83; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3257


December 8, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
January 27, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Burton A. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of sexual assault. Defendant challenged the order denying his post-conviction motions seeking a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The compliant against defendant was that he forcibly had sexual intercourse with his 14-year-old stepdaughter. The trial court's instructions to the jury stated that sexual contact was the intentional touching of the intimate parts, clothed or unclothed, of a person to the intimate parts, clothed or unclothed, of another, or the intentional touching by hand, mouth or object of the intimate parts, clothed or unclothed, of another, if that intentional touching could be reasonably construed as being for the purpose of sexual arousal or gratification. Defendant was convicted of sexual assault. On motions after verdict, a new trial was sought on the ground that the sexual contact instruction was unconstitutional. Defendant's postconviction motions were denied. On review, defendant argued that the jury instruction was unconstitutional in that it reduced the criminal burden of proof to a lesser standard. The court agreed and held that the jury instruction unconstitutionally reduced the State's burden of proof. However, because the jury could not have reasonably construed defendant's conduct as being for a purpose other than sexual gratification or arousal, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order.

Prairie Du Chien v. Evans

OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that under Wis. Stat. § 345.60 (1977). In affirming the judgment the court observed that Wis. Stat. § 343.30(1q)(a) permitted, but did not require, the trial court to refer defendant for an assessment or traffic safety school in lieu of revocation. The court noted that for a first time offender § 343.30(1q)(c) indicated that a minimum three month revocation was the penalty, unless the trial court ordered an assessment or traffic safety school. The court held that the fact that defendant had to consent to the § 343.30(1q)(a) alternatives did not give him the right to choose those alternatives. The court rejected, for lack of evidence, defendant's suggestion that § 343.30(1q) was applied to him in a discriminatory fashion in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1, and his claim that the trial court failed to give sufficient reasons for the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

In re Estate of Bilsie


No. 79-1067


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 342; 302 N.W.2d 508; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3262


February 6, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
January 22, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Robert R. Pekowsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a contestant and the contestant's attorney, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which required appellants to pay to respondents, a proponent and a guardian ad litem, attorney's fees that arose from an objection to the probate of a decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: The contestant objected to the proponent's petition to admit the decedent's will to probate. After the trial court admitted the will to probate, it found that the contestant's objection was frivolous under Wis. Stat. § 814.025(3)(b) and ordered appellants to pay respondents attorney's fees and costs. On appeal, the court affirmed the order against appellants. The court concluded that the standard of conduct for litigants and their counsel provided under § 814.025(3)(b) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that allowance of attorney's fees pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 814.025 did not deny access to the courts in violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9. The court determined that the trial court applied the proper burden of proof to the contestant's claim of lack of testamentary capacity and that the denial of the proponent's motion for summary judgment did not establish that the contestant's objection had a reasonable basis. The court found that Wis. Stat. § 814.025 was not applied retroactively. The court concluded that § 814.025 did not permit it to assess attorney's fees for a frivolous appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that required the contestant and the contestant's attorney to pay the proponent and the guardian ad litem for the attorney's fees that arose from the objection to the probate of the will.

 

1927 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. SIMS


No. 80-1076-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


100 Wis. 2d 748; 303 N.W.2d 855; 1981 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3794



January 13, 1981 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: CLARENCE R. PARRISH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint charging defendant with four counts of recipient Medical Assistance Fraud, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 49.49(1)(a)3. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that § 49.49 (1)(a)3 was facially vague and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Prosecution was commenced by a complaint charging defendant with four counts of Medical Assistance Fraud. All counts were charged as misdemeanors and arose from defendant allegedly obtaining Ritalin for her son by means of her Medicaid card. The trial court filed a decision dismissing the criminal complaint on the ground that § 49.49(1)(a)3 was facially vague and unconstitutional. The court noted that Wis. Stat. § 968.01 defined a criminal complaint as a written statement of the essential facts constituting the offense charged. The court held that there were not sufficient allegations set forth in the complaint to charge defendant with a violation of Wis. Stat. § 49.49(1)(a)3. The complaint failed to set forth all of the essential facts constituting a crime under § 49.49 (1)(a)3. The court noted that the statute contemplated that a Medicare recipient, with intent to fraudulently secure more benefits than were due, violated the statute when he or she concealed information that would be relevant to such a determination by a health care provider. Based on the complaint, it was not possible to determine whether defendant had secured a benefit in a greater amount than was due.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of dismissal on non-constitutional grounds.

 

1928 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


United States Fire Ins. Co. v. E. D. Wesley Co.


No. 80-017


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


100 Wis. 2d 59; 301 N.W.2d 271; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3265


November 19, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
December 26, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leander J. Foley, Jr., Judge. Judgment against Brey, Stuewe & Braun, Inc. Judgment against E. D. Wesley Company.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment against Brey reversed and cause remanded with directions. Judgment against Wesley affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurer and an oil company, sought review of judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which, in separate judgments, dismissed their actions for damages caused by a break in a pipeline against appellee contractors. Issues included whether the trial court abused its discretion in allowing one contractor to amend its answer and in holding that the six-year limitation in Wis. Stat. 893.155 applied to the causes.


OVERVIEW: The insurer and the oil company commenced the action for damages sustained when an underground pipeline burst, resulting in an oil spill that injured certain property. The pipeline was designed, constructed, and installed by the contractors. Two contractors answered separately and denied negligence and raised as an affirmative defense the statute of limitations. The other contract answered and only denied any negligence. The trial court granted the motions of the two contractors to dismiss. The trial court concluded that the action was commenced more than six years after the substantial completion of construction, thus, the action was barred by § 893.155. The trial court permitted the other contractor to amend its pleading to raise the statute of limitation's defense. The court held that for purposes of applying the statute of limitations to an action to recover damages caused by a break in an oil pipeline, an oil pipeline was an improvement to real property. The court noted that the record failed to disclose the trial court's reasoning for granting the motion to amend the pleadings. This failure constituted an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the actions against two contractors. The court reversed and remanded the cause of action as to the other contractor for de novo consideration of the contractor's motion to amend its answer.

 

1929 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


MAPLE DALE-INDIAN HILL EDUC. ASSN. v. FOX POINT JOINT SCH. DIST. NO. 8


No. 80-595


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


100 Wis. 2d 743; 301 N.W.2d 464; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3284



December 19, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: PATRICK J. MADDEN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found the school district was estopped from challenging the constitutionality of a statute after collective bargaining mediation with respondent association.


OVERVIEW: The association was the labor organization representing all teachers employed by the school district. The parties commenced negotiations for a new collective bargaining agreement. After 28 bargaining sessions, the association petitioned the Employment Relations Commission for commencement of mediation-arbitration. However, the school district twice refused to sign the new collective bargaining agreement incorporating the mediator-arbitrator decision. The issue on appeal was whether a municipal employer who participated in procedures for settlement of labor disputes pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 111.70(4)(cm) was estopped from challenging the constitutionality of that statute after the arbitrator rendered a final and binding decision favorable to the employees. The court held that the constitutional challenge was untimely and the school district was estopped from asserting it. The school district asserted a strong public interest in judicial resolution of its constitutional challenge. This public interest was outweighed by the public interest in the holding of parties to the benefit of their bargains arrived at after extensive voluntary negotiations. The court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which found the school district was estopped from challenging the constitutionality of a statute after collective bargaining mediation with the association.

 

1930 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


CITY OF MADISON v. LEFFLER


Nos. 79-811 and 79-1568


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


100 Wis. 2d 741; 301 N.W.2d 463; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3341



December 19, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for Dane county: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge. Reversed and remanded. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments reversed and causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two actions, plaintiff city appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which declared that one of its parking ordinances was unconstitutional as applied to defendant violators.


OVERVIEW: The city appealed judgments declaring one of its parking ordinances unconstitutional as applied to the violators. Because the court concluded that the ordinance was not unconstitutional on its face and because neither violators presented any facts to show that the ordinance was unconstitutional, the court reversed. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional on its face. It did not establish classifications based on constitutionally prohibited distinctions, and it was not an ex post facto law, impaired no contractual obligation, and affected no vested right. Even though the ordinance treated members of the same class differently, there was no evidence that the different treatment was arbitrary and impermissibly discriminatory, and without reasonable justification in furthering the purposes of the ordinance. The record did not even show standing on behalf of the violators to challenge the contested ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court, in favor of the city, reversed the judgment of the trial court declaring one of the city's parking ordinances unconstitutional as applied to the violators. The court remanded the action to the trial court.

 

1931 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. PATRI


No. 78-187-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4121



December 19, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment and orders of the circuit court for Waupaca county: FREDERICK A. FINK, Judge. Appeal from judgment dismissed, orders affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --The orders denying defendant's motions for a new trial and modification of sentence following the manslaughter conviction are affirmed. The order of this court granting the motion of the state to withdraw an argument in the appeal following the arson trial is vacated. The appeal from the judgment in the arson trial is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin), defendant was convicted of the crime of manslaughter. Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of her motions for a new trial and for modification of her sentence. Defendant also appealed from a judgment entered as a result of separate trial on the charge of arson, wherein she was found not guilty by reason of mental disease.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot her husband, hid his body in a shed, and then set fire to their house. A fire investigator conducted two searches of the house and outbuildings without a warrant. After his initial investigation, he later returned to the property and found the husband's body. Defendant argued that the warrantless searches were unconstitutional. Defendant's manslaughter conviction was affirmed. The court held that under the emergency doctrine or the exigent-circumstance rule, the searches were reasonable and did not violate defendant's constitutional rights. The court found that because an emergency existed, the investigator was entitled to search for the cause of the fire, and after he suspected that arson caused the fire, he was entitled to investigate further until he eliminated the grounds for that suspicion or found probable cause to believe that arson had occurred. The court also found that it was reasonable to search the house and the outbuildings in the immediate area, and that it was reasonable to conduct not only one but two searches of the buildings.


OUTCOME: The orders denying defendant's motions for a new trial and modification of sentence following her manslaughter conviction were affirmed. Defendant's appeal from the judgment in the arson trial, which found defendant not guilty by reason of mental disease, was dismissed.

 

1932 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ZALUCHA v. BOARD OF REGENTS OF THE UNIV. OF WISCONSIN SYS.


No. 79-1902


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


99 Wis. 2d 806; 301 N.W.2d 461; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4088



November 24, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county, WILLIAM F. EICH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which held in favor of respondents, the university and the board of regents, and affirmed the regents' decision that the student was not a resident for tuition remission purposes under Wis. Stat. § 36.27(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: The regents declared that the student was not a resident for tuition remission purposes under Wis. Stat. § 36.27(2)(a), and the student initiated an action. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the university and the regents and affirmed the regents' decision. The student sought review. Pursuant to the statute, the student, who had been a bona fide resident of the state for 12 months preceding the semester, was entitled to an exemption from the nonresident portion of tuition. The court held that in determining the bona fide residence, the regents were permitted to look at the filing of a state tax return, eligibility to vote in the state, motor vehicle registration, and place of employment. The court determined that it was required to review the regents' decision under the substantial evidence test and was not permitted to overturn the regents' decision unless it was not supported by substantial evidence. The court held that the student had failed to establish that he was a resident for 12 months and that he was not entitled to the tuition exemption. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which granted judgment in favor of the university and the regents and affirmed the regents' decision declaring that the student was not a resident for tuition remission purposes.

 

1933 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olsen


No. 80-343-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 572; 299 N.W.2d 632; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3251


October 10, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
November 24, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Vernon County: William L. Reinecke, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Vernon County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of disorderly conduct, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 947.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others became aware that a nuclear power plant was making shipments of spent radioactive fuel rods to another state for storage. They were blocking the road in demonstration when they were asked by a sheriff to move. When they refused, they were arrested and charged with disorderly conduct. Defendant was convicted, and he moved for post-conviction relief, but his motion was denied. He appealed, arguing, inter alia, that he was entitled to raise the defense of necessity and that the trial court erred in excluding evidence that would have established his defense. The court affirmed, holding that the defense of necessity was unavailable to a demonstrator who sought to stop a shipment of spent fuels that he believed were unsafe because the doctrine was generally inappropriate to justify acts of civil disobedience. Such a defense would require that defendant's actions were caused by the pressure of a natural physical force, and no offer of proof could have shown that. Even if the trial court erred, it would have been harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct.

 

1934 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kollasch v. Adamany


No. 79-1579


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 533; 299 N.W.2d 891; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3249


August 20, 1980, Argued  
November 24, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Benedictine nuns appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Dane County (Wisconsin) that claimed that the State's threat to tax what they charged for meals served to those that visited their premises violated their right to the free exercise of their religion in contravention of the Federal Constitution, the Wisconsin Constitution, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Defendant was the Secretary of the Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 77.52(1) imposed a sales tax on all retailers for the privilege of selling tangible, personal property. The court rejected the nuns' contention that the sales tax did not apply to their sale of meals to business groups. Wis. Const. art. I, § 18 and the U.S. Const. amend. I guaranteed the free exercise of religion, and a separate issue was whether or not the tax violated that right to that free exercise. The court found that providing meals to guests and joining them while they ate furthered the ecumenical dialogue that the nuns wanted to establish and that the meal was viewed traditionally as a religious activity. The court ruled that the provision of meals by the nuns was a purely religious activity and in no way a commercial enterprise. However, the court held that although the nuns were engaged in a religious activity in providing meals to their guests for consideration, the requirement that they collect a sales tax on the sale of those meals was neither a tax on religion nor a burden to their exercise of religion. Significant to the court was that the State could not utilize the tax easily to deter the nuns from exercising their religion.


OUTCOME: Ruling against the nuns, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County: John B. Buchen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions to vacate the agency's order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant operator an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which affirmed an amended order of respondent, State of Wisconsin Division of Motor Vehicles, which suspended for six months the operator's probationary license to drive.


OVERVIEW: On August 24, 1979, the Division of Motor Vehicles ordered the operator's probationary license be suspended for a period of two months beginning August 24 because the Division's records showed that the operator had accumulated 13 demerit points for convictions of three traffic violations that occurred in 1979. On October 30, 1979, the Division of Motor Vehicles issued the operator an amended order suspending his license for a period of six months beginning August 24 because its records showed Best had accumulated 19 points, which represented the prior 13 points plus six points for conviction of a traffic violation which occurred on September 22, 1979. The operator petitioned for review and argued that he had been deprived of procedural due process and of the equal protection of the laws. The trial court affirmed the suspension. The operator again appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the State did not afford the operator the requirements of procedural due process in that it failed to promulgate ascertainable standards for the exercise of administrative discretion in determining the length of license suspensions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to vacate the Division's order of suspension.

 

1936 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lederer


No. 80-113-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 430; 299 N.W.2d 457; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3241


September 10, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
October 28, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Victor Manian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of third degree sexual assault contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(3). Defendant also challenged the order that denied his motions for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly committed nonconsensual sexual activities. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statutory consent definition, the sufficiency of the consent evidence, and the adequacy of jury instructions. The court held that the statute was not constitutionally overbroad because its plain terms demonstrated that failure to resist was not consent and required that the State had to prove that the act of sexual intercourse was without consent. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence that the victim had objected throughout the activities and had been threatened by defendant that things would be worse if she did not comply. The court found no error in the trial court's refusal to order the victim to submit to a mental examination because defendant's allegation that the report was necessary to assess her credibility was not a strong and compelling reason. The court also found no error in the trial court's refusal to instruct on prior inconsistent statements because the instructions given adequately stated the law applicable to the facts and properly entitled the jury to determine the weight to be accorded to the statements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction and the order that denied his motions for postconviction relief.

 

1937 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Basinas v. State


No. 79-1552


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 412; 299 N.W.2d 295; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3232


August 6, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
October 27, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: George R. Currie, Reserve Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirming the decision of respondent state personnel commission (commission) dismissing the employee's appeal of his reassignment for want of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a career executive with the state. He was reassigned but his salary was not affected. The employee filed two appeals of his reassignment, one to the state personnel board. The board refused to undertake an investigation of the claim. The employee filed a petition to review the board's action. The trial court affirmed the board's decision and the employee did not appeal. His other appeal, to the commission was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the employee's reassignment to another career executive position was not a demotion, even if the new position had a lower pay range and that Wis. Stat. §§ 230.45, 230.44 did not confer subject matter jurisdiction on the commission to hear his appeal. Even if Wis. Adm. Code § Pers. 30.10 could be read to authorize the commission to hear an appeal from a career executive reassignment, the rule could not confer jurisdiction where none was granted by statute. The commission correctly dismissed the appeal. The employee's reassignment was not a demotion and the term "transfer" found in the statute authorized his reassignment as provided in the administrative rules.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court dismissing the employee's request for review of his reassignment.

 

1938 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allison


No. 80-115-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 391; 299 N.W.2d 286; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3237


October 15, 1980, Argued  
October 21, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.
Related proceeding at State v. Allison, 226 Wis. 2d 158, 594 N.W.2d 418, 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 316 (Wis. Ct. App., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of conviction on resentence to confinement of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: John F. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for rape and sexual perversion in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 944.01(1) and 944.17. He appealed from a judgment of conviction on resentence to confinement by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin). The circuit court refused to give defendant credit for time served on an unrelated conviction that was voided.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape contrary to Wis. Stat. § 944.01(1) and sexual perversion contrary to § 944.17. He was sentenced to 30 years for the rape offense and four years for the sexual perversion offense, to run consecutively. Defendant's sentence on the rape charge was subsequently reduced to 29 years to give him credit for pretrial incarceration time. Defendant had previously been convicted of one count of rape and one count of sexual perversion and served about 21 months for that conviction. Later, the conviction was overturned. Thereafter, defendant moved for resentencing on the conviction claiming that the invalidation of the conviction entitled him to receive credit for time already served on the prior conviction. The trial court reimposed the same sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The court reasoned that recognizing defendant's claim for credit would have the anomalous effect of rewarding the habitual criminal with credit while the person who did not commit a later crime was not similarly compensated. Rewarding habitual criminality was clearly against public policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

1939 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jankowski v. Milwaukee County


No. 79-1896


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


99 Wis. 2d 803; 300 N.W.2d 82; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3976



October 14, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LAURENCE C. GRAM, JR., Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff involuntary detainee sought review of an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county (Wisconsin); which granted summary judgment to defendant county in the detainee's class action for a declaratory judgment seeking to cancel bills for care and maintenance arising from institutionalization at the county mental health center.


OVERVIEW: The detainee was a member of a class of persons who were detained and committed to the mental health center, and whose detentions and commitments were declared unconstitutional. The county commenced collection efforts against members of the class for their care and maintenance under Wis. Stat. § 46.10. The detainee argued that it was violative of public policy and inequitable to impose liability on detainees for their confinement, that § 46.10 would have to be construed in an absurd way to permit recovery for illegal commitments, and that imposition of liability for the cost of care and treatment was a denial of due process. The court found that § 46.10 was clear and unambiguous in imposing liability for care, maintenance, services, and supplies upon any person committed to a county mental institution. The court found no equitable or constitutional prohibition against enforcing the statutory liability created by § 46.10. The court saw no reason to excuse the detainee from liability under § 46.10 for valuable services rendered to him by the county, merely because of the defective procedures by which he was placed at the mental health center.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1940 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


ALLEN v. STATE


No. 79-1982-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


99 Wis. 2d 803; 300 N.W.2d 82; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3979



October 14, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: ERRORS to review a judgment and order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), for first-degree murder. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in allowing testimony concerning his prior convictions; that Wis. Stat. § 906.09 was unconstitutional; that one of the jury instructions given by the court was unconstitutional; and that he was entitled to a new trial in the interests of justice.


OVERVIEW: Intending to call defendant as a witness, defense counsel moved to suppress his prior criminal convictions. The trial court denied the motion, and defense counsel elicited testimony on direct examination concerning the convictions. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that elicitation of the testimony was a matter of trial strategy that estopped defendant from raising any alleged error, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to suppress where the convictions occurred within 10 years prior to trial, where the continuous and repetitive nature of the offenses reflected upon defendant's credibility, and where an appropriate limiting instruction was given. The court held that § 906.09 did not violate due process or equal protection rights or the right to trial by an impartial jury, and that the jury instruction did not impermissibly shift the burden of persuasion. It held that an incident in which a bailiff was robbed in the hotel in which the jury was sequestered did not create a miscarriage of justice or make it more likely that a new trial would produce a different result, and denied the motion for a new trial in the interests of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1941 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kahn v. McCormack


No. 80-051


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 382; 299 N.W.2d 279; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3236; 19 A.L.R.4th 346


September 3, 1980, Argued  
October 14, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Gordon Myse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants bail bond sureties sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which determined that an amendment to Wis. Stat. § 969.12(1) and (2), which eliminated corporate sureties and sureties for profit for criminal bail bonds, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The amendment to Wis. Stat. § 969.12(1) and (2), effectively put the sureties out of the bail bond business. A lawsuit was filed challenging the constitutionality of the amended statute. A temporary restraining order was granted. The sureties contended that the amended statute deprived them of property without due process of law and of equal protection of the laws contrary to U. S. Const., amend. XIV, and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The trial court ruled that the amendment was constitutional and vacated the temporary restraining order. The court affirmed holding that in the exercise of its police power, a state may forbid, as inimical to the public welfare, the prosecution of a particular type of business, or regulate a business in such manner as to abate evils deemed to arise from its pursuit. The test was if there was a reasonable and practical ground for the law or classification whether the challenge was based upon due process or equal protection grounds. The law was reasonably related to concerns of the commercial bail bonding system's potential for abuse and corruption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that the amended statute was constitutional.

State v. Goebel


No. 80-129-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


99 Wis. 2d 804; 300 N.W.2d 83; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4023



October 10, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ozaukee county: WALTER J. SWIETLIK, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and that denied defendant's motions to reduce the amount of the fine that was imposed as a condition of his probation and to suppress the marijuana that was found at the scene.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the initial detention and questioning and the subsequent search were unconstitutional and that the fine was imposed without giving consideration to his ability to pay. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, concluding that Wis. Stat. § 968.24 and the Fourth Amendment justified the acts that led to discovering the marijuana and that there was no legal or factual basis for overturning the ruling that defendant was able to pay the modified fine that was imposed. The court reasoned that the presence of defendant's stopped car partially on the road suggested a possible need for assistance and justified the initial stop and that the suspicious behavior and nervousness that defendant and his passenger exhibited when the first officer approached provided reasonable indications of possible criminal activity that warranted further questioning. The court also held that reasonable questioning was occurring when the first bag of marijuana accidentally slipped into view from under the car seat and that discovery justified the further search and defendant's arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute and the denials of his motions to reduce the modified fine that was imposed as a condition of probation and to suppress the marijuana that was seized.

 

1943 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kaiser v. City of Mauston


No. 79-1759


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 345; 299 N.W.2d 259; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3243


April 21, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
September 19, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Juneau County: J. K. Callahan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a lake improvement district, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin), which, in a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiff taxpayers, granted the taxpayers a permanent injunction enjoining the city and the district from giving effect to a lake rehabilitation plan which would involve drawing down and dredging a lake in the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought a declaratory judgment action against the city and the district, contending that the district was never validly created. The trial court entered a declaratory judgment in favor of the taxpayers. The city and the district contended that the trial court had no jurisdiction to hear the matter, that the passage of time barred the taxpayers from seeking a declaratory judgment, and that the taxpayers lacked standing. The court held that the taxpayers were not required to seek review of the city's annexation of part of the lake bed before the Department of Natural Resources prior to bringing their declaratory judgment action. Recourse to the Department would have been a futile act because the Department was clothed with no right to determine whether the annexation procedure was legal. Laches did not bar the taxpayers' action because nothing in the stipulated facts indicated that they had knowledge of the illegality of the annexation at the time the annexation ordinance was passed or that they acquiesced in the illegal procedure. The allegation that the city had spent or proposed to spend public funds illegally was sufficient to confer standing on the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted the taxpayers a permanent injunction enjoining the city and the district from giving effect to a lake rehabilitation plan.

 

1944 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. VOLK


Nos. 80-035-CR and 80-036-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


98 Wis. 2d 755; 300 N.W.2d 80; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3785



September 18, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed two judgments from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him of delivery of cocaine contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 161.16(4) and 161.41(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether the Uniform Controlled Substances Act, Wis. Stat. ch. 161, violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Defendant contended that the exclusion of intoxicating liquors, malt beverages, and tobacco pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 161.11(5) from the scope of Wis. Stat. ch. 161 created a privileged classification thereby depriving him of equal protection of the law. The court disagreed and upheld the trial court's judgments. The court held that a party challenging the constitutionality of a statute had the burden of establishing that the statute was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. He had to overcome the presumption of constitutionality with all doubts to be resolved in favor of the statute. It was evident from the declaration of intent contained in Wis. Stat. § 161.001 that the Wisconsin Legislature determined the defined controlled substances to present special threats to society deserving of special solutions. Finally, a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute could not succeed when grounded upon the assertion that the statute did not embrace all possible abuses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

State v. Dalton


No. 80-270-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Motion denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Clark v. Foster, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 169006 (W.D. Wis., Dec. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Burton A. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) for first-degree murder, kidnapping by deceit, and first degree sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for first-degree murder, kidnapping by deceit, and first degree sexual assault. The evidence showed that defendant lured the victim to his residence, where he handcuffed and gagged her, had forcible sexual intercourse with her, and then killed her. Defendant contended that he did not have the intent to kill the victim and that it was error to exclude psychiatric testimony that defendant did not have intent to kill at the time of the homicide. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and concluded that the circuit court did not err in excluding the psychiatric testimony since the witness had no scientific knowledge which formed the basis for his opinion that defendant lacked the specific intent to kill. The court found that the spousal privilege had been waived and concluded that the wife was properly permitted to testify that defendant admitted to her that he killed the victim and had buried the body near the house. The court held that defendant's conduct in deceiving the victim by taking her to his home without protesting constituted kidnapping by deceit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction against defendant for first-degree murder, kidnapping by deceit, and first degree sexual assault.

 

1946 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hall


No. 80-222-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


98 Wis. 2d 755; 300 N.W.2d 80; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3798



September 8, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MARVIN C. HOLZ, Judge. Affirmed in part, reversed in part. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment of conviction and the order denying postconviction relief on the attempted armed robbery, reversed; Judgment of conviction and the order denying postconviction relief on all other counts, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of three armed robberies, one attempted armed robbery, and several other related crimes, including first-degree murder, stemming from the other offenses. Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to grant his motion for severance. He asserted that he was compelled to choose not to testify in his defense because to do so could have resulted in self-incrimination. The court affirmed the convictions except for the attempted armed robbery, finding that defendant's subjective impressions of what he was "forced" to do during his trial were not enough to render his failure to testify involuntary. The court found that until the subject matter of defendant's testimony and the actual questions were known, disputes as to whether defendant waived his privilege against self-incrimination as to those questions were not factually presented. Defendant also claimed that convictions arising out of one incident unconstitutionally put him in double jeopardy because all the charges were based on the same conduct. The court concluded that there was no double jeopardy violation under the "same evidence test" because it focused on the elements of the statutes violated, not defendant's actions. The court reversed the attempted armed robbery conviction, finding that there was no unequivocal act toward an armed robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and order denying postconviction relief on all counts except the attempted armed robbery. The court reversed the judgment of conviction and order denying postconviction relief on the attempted armed robbery count.
