Wipperfurth v. U-Haul Co. of Western Wisconsin, Inc.


No. 80-144


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 516; 297 N.W.2d 65; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3194


June 30, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
August 26, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found for respondent dealer in his action for breach of a distributorship contract.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into a contract to use the dealer's service station as a dispatching and receiving location for the corporation's rental trucks. The corporation terminated the contract with 30 days notice, pursuant to the contract. The dealer argued that notice failed to comply with the Wisconsin Fair Dealership Law (WFDL). The trial court found for the dealer. On appeal, the court reversed holding that the legislative history of the statute supported the view that it was not meant to be retroactively applied. The court held that the contract between the parties was valid and the notice was sufficient under the contract. Because the WFDL was not to be applied retroactively, the dealer was not entitled to recover.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for the dealer and found for the corporation.

 

1948 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Edmond v. State


No. 79-1185-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


98 Wis. 2d 749; 297 N.W.2d 515; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3748



August 25, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: ERROR to review judgments and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments and orders of the trial court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted them of first-degree murder, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.01, 939.05, second-degree murder, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.02, 939.05, armed robbery, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(a), (2), 939.05, and armed burglary, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.10(1), (2)(a), 939.05.


OVERVIEW: An elderly couple was found dead in their home. When the police arrived, they found that the two had both been badly beaten, the husband had a wire hanger wrapped around his neck, and the wife was partially nude and had been sexually assaulted with a beer bottle. The entire house had been ransacked. Defendants were convicted and each sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the convictions. The court rejected defendants' argument that the testimony about the beer bottle was evidence of a sexual assault with which defendants were not charged and should have been excluded under the "other crimes" rule. The court determined that the evidence had not fallen within the exclusion of the "other crimes" rule. Rather, it was part of the complete story of the robbery and murder of the couple and was very relevant to establishing the depraved mind element of the second-degree murder charge. The court further rejected defendants' argument that the evidence was shocking to the conscience and fundamentally unfair. A description of the assault would not have been excluded merely because the assault was brutal. Testimony concerning the beer bottle was brief, concise, and not overly descriptive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and the orders of the trial court that convicted defendants of first-degree murder, party to a crime, second-degree murder, party to a crime, armed robbery, party to a crime, and armed burglary, party to a crime.

 

1949 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Madison v. Garrott


No. 79-742


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


98 Wis. 2d 749; 297 N.W.2d 515; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3902



August 25, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a trial court's decision that convicted him of four counts of violating Madison, Wisconsin General Ordinances § 9.33 and imposed separate forfeitures for each one.


OVERVIEW: The city charged defendant with permitting the conduct of a massage establishment without a license, employing an unlicensed technician, knowingly allowing an employee to give genital massages, and letting an employee expose her genitals to another person. These activities violated § 9.33. The court held: (1) while the regulation of commercial sexual activity was of paramount state concern, Wis. Stat. § 62.11(5) authorized the city to regulate commercial massage; (2) state statutes regulating sexual conduct were compatible with and did not preempt the city's massage establishment ordinance; and (3) the city's massage establishment ordinance did not unconstitutionally infringe on free speech or privacy interests, and that it violated neither the Equal Protection nor the Due Process Clauses of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

 

1950 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Briggs Transp. Co.


No. 79-1833


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


98 Wis. 2d 750; 297 N.W.2d 516; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3910



August 25, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: WILLIAM C. SACHTJEN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which determined that defendant truck operator was not guilty of violating a civil forfeiture statute, Wis. Stat. § 347.47(3), and dismissed the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a number of twin trailer trucks. When one of its trucks was stopped at a weigh station, an inspector found that a dolly that connected the truck's two semitrailers was secured to the first semitrailer by one safety chain. The inspector, believing that Wis. Stat. § 347.47(3) required the use of two safety chains running between the dolly and the first semitrailer, issued defendant a citation. The trial court found defendant not guilty and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 347.47(3) did not apply to trailers having a gross weight in excess of 10,000 pounds. The uncontroverted testimony was that the trailer that was the subject of this action weighed more than 10,000 pounds. In reaching this conclusion, the court examined the legislative history of the statute, which it found to be ambiguous when read in conjunction with the administrative rules that it incorporated. The legislative history demonstrated a continuing concern with providing additional safety precautions only where they were needed. The court found that the legislative intent was to exempt large trucks, where additional safety measures were not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1951 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Broullire


No. 79-1827


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


98 Wis. 2d 747; 297 N.W.2d 514; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3824



July 28, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago county: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge. Vacated and remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment vacated and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applicant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff State and concluded that the applicant was required to complete a driving test in an automobile before a license to drive a motor-driver tricycle could be obtained pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.07(4).


OVERVIEW: The applicant claimed that Wis. Stat. § 343.07(4), which required him to complete a driving test in an automobile before a license to drive a motor-driver tricycle could be obtained, unconstitutionally violated his right to freedom of movement. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the State, but on appeal, the court dismissed the appeal and vacated the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that because the Attorney General was not served with notice of the constitutional challenge of the statute at the trial court level, neither the trial court nor the appellate court had subject matter jurisdiction to decide the issue. Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11), which required service of the Attorney General any time a statute, ordinance, or franchise was alleged to be unconstitutional, applied to all cases involving constitutional challenges, not just in cases requesting declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal, vacated the trial court's order, and remanded the cause.

 

1952 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


COUNTY OF PORTAGE v. STEINPREIS


Nos. 80-037 and 80-038


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


98 Wis. 2d 748; 297 N.W.2d 515; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3940



July 28, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage county: JAMES H. LEVI, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, Portage County, Wisconsin, in favor of plaintiff county in the county's small claims action to recover the unpaid cost of county ambulance services and the filing fee for the action. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 299.21(3) on the grounds that it denied him equal protection of the law and the right to a jury trial and constituted a "purchase of justice."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was told he would have to pay $ 43.00 for a jury trial in the small claims action as required by § 299.21(3). This sum included the suit tax, clerk's fee, and jury fee. His motion for an order declaring § 299.21(3) unconstitutional was denied. He agreed to an immediate entry of judgment against him and appealed. The only issue before the court was the prepayment of jury fees. Defendant had standing to challenge § 299.21(3) as a member of a class of small claims litigants. He did not waive his right to challenge the constitutionality of § 299.21(3) by consenting to the judgment, and his challenge was not moot. The court noted that the costs of administering a jury trial and the burden to the State in providing a jury were no greater in small claims actions than they were in non-small claims actions filed under Wis. Stat. chs. 801-807. No legitimate state objective was served by this legislative classification. The right to a jury trial was guaranteed under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5. Wis. Stat. § 299.21(3), which required small claims litigants to pay a jury fee, violated the equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the county in its small claims action to recover unpaid ambulance service costs from defendant was reversed.

 

1953 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State, Law Enforcement Standards Board v. Lyndon Station


No. 78-456


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 229; 295 N.W.2d 818; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3189


August 30, 1979, Argued  
July 28, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order and a judgment of the Circuit Court for Juneau County: Raymond E. Gieringer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order and judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Wisconsin Law Enforcement Standards Board sought a writ of mandamus in the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin) to compel defendant village to terminate the employment of its chief of police, who was appointed in violation of Wis. Admin. Code § 201(1)(d). The trial court found that the statute was valid and issued the writ of mandamus. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village's chief of police was convicted of 26 counts of misconduct in public office in violation of Wis. Stat. § 956.12. The village alleged that Wis. Admin. Code § 2.01(1)(d) did not apply because the violations for which the police chief had been convicted were misdemeanors. The court held that, because the convictions were for felonies, Wis. Admin. Code § 2.01(1)(d) was applicable, and the village's hiring of a convicted felon as the village's police chief violated that section. The chief of police position was created by legislative act and was a permanent position. The power of the chief of police was sufficient that the police chief was an officer of the village. The offenses for which the chief of police was convicted were punishable by a year's imprisonment in a state prison. The village alleged that the police chief had a property interest in his employment that could not be terminated without a due process hearing. The court held that the village lacked standing to assert the rights of the police chief and that the village lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's issuance of a writ of mandamus to compel the village to terminate the employment of the village's chief of police.

 

1954 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Madison v. Schultz


No. 79-689


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 188; 295 N.W.2d 798; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3187


November 2, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
July 24, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Angela B. Bartell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, owner of a massage parlor, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of owning, operating or managing massage establishments, employing unlicensed massage technicians, knowingly allowing the technicians to give genital massages, and permitting them to expose their sexual or genital parts to another person, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 9.33.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of owning, operating or managing massage establishments, employing unlicensed massage technicians, knowingly allowing the technicians to give genital massages, and permitting them to expose their sexual or genital parts to another person in violation of Madison General Ordinances § 9.33. On appeal, defendant claimed that Plaintiff City had no authority to legislate in the area of criminal sexual conduct because this area was primarily a matter of statewide concern, and that § 9.33 violated her First Amendment right. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and held that the local ordinance was a proper exercise of the city's broad police powers. The fact that the state had enacted comprehensive legislation governing sexual morality did not proscribe the City from adopting an ordinance in the same area, which went farther in prohibition. Additionally, the court held that defendant could claim no protection under the First Amendment for her actions, because a masseuse's actions in disrobing did not constitute "speech" which the first amendment protected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of owning, operating or managing massage establishments, employing unlicensed massage technicians, knowingly allowing the technicians to give genital massages, and permitting them to expose their sexual or genital parts to another person.

 

1955 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mayer v. Kirsenlohr


No. 79-540


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


98 Wis. 2d 745; 297 N.W.2d 513; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3938



July 23, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court for Adams county: ANDREW P. COTTER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbor challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Adams County (Wisconsin), which dismissed her complaint alleging that defendant store owners were selling obscene magazines in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.21 (1977) and that they created a nuisance by violating Wis. Stat. § 823.09, the "bawdyhouse" statute.


OVERVIEW: The store owners operated a grocery store in which they sold magazines that the neighbor felt were obscene. The neighbor claimed that the store owners violated Wis. Stat. § 944.21 (1977), which prohibited the sale of obscene materials, and that as a result, she suffered shame, embarrassment, and emotional distress. She also claimed that by selling the magazines, the store owners violated the "bawdyhouse" statute. The trial court dismissed the complaint, and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 944.21(1)(a) had been previously declared unconstitutionally overbroad because it conflicted with U.S. amend. I. Therefore, any offense created by the statute was not a crime. The court also concluded that the second cause of action was properly dismissed because Wis. Stat. § 823.09 did not apply in this case. The use of the store for the display and sale of allegedly obscene publications did not constitute "lewdness" within the purview of the statute because the sale or exhibition of a magazine was not a sexual act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1956 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sikora v. Oak Creek


No. 79-1677


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


98 Wis. 2d 747; 297 N.W.2d 514; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3776



July 16, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a part of a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: RALPH J. PODELL, Judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions to enter judgment pursuant to the opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the City of Oak Creek and its building inspector, sought review of part of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded to respondent property owners a peremptory writ of mandamus for the issuance of a building permit.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to City ordinances, the Oak Creek Plan Commission required the property owners to enter into a development agreement for the installation of a water main before the City would issue a building permit to them. The property owners were required to deposit almost half of the estimated cost of the construction with the City. The trial court found that the Commission's decision requiring the installation of a water main was arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable. The court overturned the trial court's judgment. The court held that when a municipality had not exceeded the power delegated to it under the clear terms of the enabling legislation, the discretion of the municipality had to go unchallenged. Here, the City ordinances accomplished the recognized objective of providing a sanitary water system for the community. Requiring the property owners to make the deposit did not exceed the reasonable needs of meeting this end, nor did it result in an arbitrary, capricious, and unreasonable application of the enactment. The ordinances were in accord with the intent and standards promulgated by the legislature, and the Commission did not exceed the ordinances' purpose or terms.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause with directions to enter judgment in favor of appellants.

 

1957 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Reddin v. Meekma


No. 80-316


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


99 Wis. 2d 56; 298 N.W.2d 192; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3228


June 5, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
July 10, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dodge County: Thomas W. Wells, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order denying petition for a writ of habeas corpus affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed an order from the Circuit Court, Dodge County, Wisconsin, that denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus for release from respondent sheriff's custody. The prisoner was arrested under an extradition warrant executed pursuant to the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Wis. Stat. § 976.03, and released on a personal recognizance bond.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted in Kentucky in 1969 for robbery, sentenced to eight years in prison, and released on parole. His parole supervision was transferred pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 57.13. He was charged in 1974 with murder. Kentucky issued a warrant and asked that the prisoner be held in custody pending disposition of the murder charge. The prisoner pled guilty to manslaughter and was sentenced to nine years in prison. Kentucky filed a parole revocation warrant in 1975 as a detainer. The prisoner was released on mandatory parole in 1979 and arrested under the extradition warrant. The court noted that Kentucky had the right to retake the prisoner under § 57.13 but chose to extradite him; thus, the prisoner properly challenged the legality of his arrest under Wis. Stat. § 976.03 by applying for the writ. He argued that he was not subject to extradition because he fully served his Kentucky sentence in Wisconsin. Kentucky's position was that the eight-year sentence was tolled prior to 1979. The court left that question and the validity of Kentucky's parole revocation to Kentucky. The extradition documents were facially valid; the writ of habeas corpus was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The order that denied the prisoner's application for a writ of habeas corpus for release from the sheriff's custody was affirmed.

 

1958 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Juneau County Forest Withdrawal Appeal Review Committee


No. 80-694


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


98 Wis. 2d 103; 295 N.W.2d 218; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3175


June 5, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
June 25, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals appealed an order of the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), which dismissed their petition to review a decision by respondent, the Juneau County Forest Withdrawal Appeal Review Committee, allowing respondent Juneau County to withdraw 960 acres of its land from the forest land program.


OVERVIEW: Juneau County owned land which it had previously entered into a forest land program pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 28.11. In 1975, the County Board decided to withdraw 960 acres of its land from the forest land program. It followed the procedure required by Wis. Stat. § 28.11(11)(a), and passed a resolution requesting the Department of Natural Resources (DNR) to issue an order withdrawing the 960 acres from the program. The DNR denied the county's request. The county board passed a resolution withdrawing the land from the county forest law. The individuals petitioned the Dane County Circuit Court for judicial review of the Review Committee's decision pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 227.15 and asked the court to stay enforcement of the appeal review committee's order and for a judgment holding Wis. Stat. § 28.11(11)(a), unconstitutional. The court affirmed and held that the trial court did not have jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. ch. 227 to hear the individuals' petition and therefore properly dismissed it because the Review Committee was not a State agency. The court found that the Committee was not a State agency because Committee's functions were primarily of county-wide concern.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the individuals' petition for review.

 

1959 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. MERHISH


No. 80-765-CR-NM


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


97 Wis. 2d 760; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4131



June 24, 1980, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)5, STATS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of welfare fraud in violation of Wis. Stat. § 49.12(6).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a welfare recipient who acquired income producing property, intentionally failed to inform the welfare authorities about it, and continued to receive about $ 2,200 in assistance thereafter. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court accepted the no merit brief filed by appellate counsel pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.32. The court rejected the suggestion that Wis. Stat. § 49.12(6) was unconstitutionally vague. The court then held § 49.12(6) was not arbitrary and capricious simply because it permitted the prosecutor to charge one continuous felony or several discrete misdemeanors. The court next dismissed the notion that the requirement that a welfare recipient had to report the acquisition of property violated the privilege against self-incrimination. The court held that the terms "fraud" and "asset" did not have to be defined by jury instructions. The court held that the jury was entitled to disbelieve defendant's claim that she acquired the property for her mother. The court concluded by holding that defendant's one year prison sentence was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's welfare fraud conviction.

 

1960 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SORGEL ELEC. v. LABOR & INDUS. REVIEW COMMN.


No. 79-1589


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


97 Wis. 2d 759; 295 N.W.2d 835; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3637



June 16, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: GARY A. GERLACH, Judge. Afffirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer, an electric company, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent, the Wisconsin Labor and Industry Review Commission. The decision held that the limitation of an employee's accident and sickness benefits to six weeks if the absence was related to pregnancy constituted discrimination by the company against the employee on the basis of sex.


OVERVIEW: The employer's benefit plan provided for payment of specified weekly disability benefits for a maximum of twenty-six weeks if related to sickness or accident, but limited the benefits to six weeks if an employee's absence was related to pregnancy. In response to an employee's complaint, the Commission issued a decision holding that the employer's practice constituted discrimination against the employee upon the basis of sex, contrary to the Wisconsin Fair Employment Law, Wis. Stat. §§ 111.31-111.37. The trial court affirmed and the employer sought further review. The court affirmed. The court held that the fact that the benefits at issue were in a collectively bargained labor contract afforded the employer neither relief nor a defense. The court noted that where the legislative will was expressed in peremptory terms of a statute, it was paramount and absolute and could not be varied or waived by the private conventions of the parties. The court also found that the Commission's decision did not impose an unreasonable burden on interstate commerce and was therefore not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1961 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


COUNTY OF ROCK v. JACKSON


No. 80-416


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


97 Wis. 2d 760; 295 N.W.2d 835; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3735



June 16, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock county: GERALD W. JAECKLE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In proceedings by respondent county, defendant appealed a default judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which imposed a forfeiture, including costs, on defendant because he operated a motor vehicle in excess of the applicable speed limit, in violation of Rock County, Wis., Gen. Ordinances § 1.01, which adopted Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled not guilty to a traffic violation and requested a jury trial, but he did not post the jury fees and did not appear at trial. The trial court entered a default judgment, finding him guilty of speeding in excess of the speed limit. After his appeal of the oral judgment was dismissed, defendant filed several motions and appealed the judgment on the basis that there was no jurisdiction to prosecute him civilly for violation of a state statute and that he had a right to a jury trial. The court affirmed. Defendant was not denied his right to procedural due process as the county brought a civil action to recover a civil forfeiture for violation of a county ordinance. Defendant was not denied his right to a jury trial; U.S. Const. amend. VII was not applicable to state court trials and the requirement of prepaid jury fees under Wis. Stat. § 345.43(1) did not interfere with the right to a jury trial under Wis. Const. art. I, § 5. The trial court had proper jurisdiction because the county was seeking only to enforce its own ordinance, and there was no evidence that Wis. Stat. §57(4) was enacted because of coercion or bribery. Defendant had proper notice of the trial date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which imposed a forfeiture, including costs, on defendant for operating a motor vehicle in excess of the speed limit.

 

1962 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


NORTHRIDGE BANK v. COMMUNITY EYE CARE CTR., INC.


No. 78-781


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


97 Wis. 2d 756; 295 N.W.2d 833; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3603



June 13, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: GARY A. GERLACH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found it insolvent and appointed a receiver under Wis. Stat. ch. 128.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff bank, an alleged creditor of the company, filed a petition against it. On July 19, 1978, an order was entered appointing a receiver. The order was stayed for a period of time to allow the company to file a bond so as to obtain a stay pending appeal. The bond was not filed and the stay was dissolved on September 13, 1978, when another order was entered dissolving the stay, appointing the same receiver, and transferring all the company's assets to the receiver. The company's attorney presented a judgment to the trial court. The trial court then adjudicated the company an insolvent and appointed a receiver to liquidate the corporation under Wis. Stat. ch. 128. The court affirmed the judgment, by holding that the company did not have a legitimate argument of vagueness regarding the term "insolvent" because the term was specifically defined in Wis. Stat. § 128.04.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which found the company insolvent and appointed a receiver.

 

1963 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. HINTZ


No. 79-1695


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


97 Wis. 2d 759; 295 N.W.2d 835; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3624



June 13, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: LEAH M. LAMPONE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found defendant guilty of operating an automobile while under the influence of an intoxicant, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1) and 346.65(2)(a)3, and sentenced defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had been twice before convicted of driving under the influence, was again found guilty of operating an automobile while under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant appealed, arguing that Wis. Stat. § 346.65(2) constituted an ex post facto law. The court held that § 346.65(2) clearly required consideration of prior ordinance violations by a trial court sentencing defendant for driving while under the influence of an intoxicant. The increased penalties did not subject defendant to additional penalties for earlier violations because the punishment received by defendant was for his current offense and not his prior offenses. At the time of defendant's third offense, § 346.65 had been in effect for seven months. Section 346.65 clearly stated that the trial court would consider defendant's two prior municipal convictions; thus, defendant should have been put on notice that another offense within a five-year period would be counted as his third conviction resulting in a mandatory fine and jail sentence. Defendant had adequate notice of the penalties and had an opportunity to conform to the law as it existed at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1964 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bartus


Nos. 79-561-CR. 79-562-CR -


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Three


97 Wis. 2d 757; 295 N.W.2d 833; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3709



June 10, 1980 


NOTICE:

UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported Multiple Times in the Bound Volume at: 97 Wis. 2d 757, 295 N.W.2d 833.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon county: NATHAN WIESE, Judge, presiding. Affirmed. 

APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon county: RALPH STRANDBERG, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment for respondent, the State of Wisconsin, and convicted the taxpayer on two counts of selling tangible personal property without a seller's permit, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 77.52(12).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer held a seller's permit for his oil burner service. His permit was revoked because the taxpayer failed to remit sales tax to the state. The taxpayer continued to operate his service after revocation of the permit. The taxpayer challenged the constitutionality of the sales tax law. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the Wisconsin Supreme Court determined that the sales tax was a valid exercise of constitutional authority and that it did not violate either the state or the federal constitutions on equal protection grounds. Further, the taxpayer failed to meet his burden of showing beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislature had no rational basis for enacting the tax legislation. The court further found that since the record was devoid of any information concerning the amount of time the taxpayer spent collecting or paying the sales tax, he failed to sustain his burden of showing that the State violated any minimum wage laws. The court found that the State's evidence that the taxpayer sold tangible personal property when he did not hold a seller's permit was uncontradicted and that the verdicts were amply supported by credible evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1965 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


TIMM v. MACE


No. 79-1475


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


97 Wis. 2d 755; 295 N.W.2d 226; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3727



May 27, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia county: HOWARD LATTON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sellers appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which granted defendant buyers' motion to reopen a default judgment of strict foreclosure of a land contract and allowed redemption by payment of the amount due under the judgment with interest and an additional sum. The sellers contended that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to modify the judgment and that the order was an impairment of contract.


OVERVIEW: When the buyers defaulted on a land contract, the sellers obtained a default judgment of strict foreclosure. When the buyers failed to make the first payment required by a court-established redemption payment schedule, the sellers applied for a writ of restitution. At about the same time the buyers' attorney advised the sellers' attorney that the buyers were able to pay the entire balance owing on the contract. However, pursuant to the sellers' urging, the sheriff executed the writ. The buyers then moved under Wis. Stat. § 806.07 to reopen the judgment and allow redemption, and the trial court modified the judgment to allow redemption upon payment of the amount of the judgment with interest and an additional sum. The court rejected the sellers' argument that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to modify the judgment. Strict foreclosure was an equitable action and § 806.07(1)(h) gave the trial court discretion to grant relief from the judgment. The court refused to entertain the sellers' argument that the modification unconstitutionally impaired a contract because that argument was not made in the trial court and the modification did not appear to modify any contractual obligations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1966 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bougneit


No. 79-556-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 687; 294 N.W.2d 675; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3163


November 29, 1979, Argued  
May 27, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: Burton A. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of attempted first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted first-degree murder. On appeal, defendant argued that the circuit judge erred in refusing to give a mistake of fact instruction, and that the circuit court erred in giving an instruction regarding the loss of the privilege of self-defense. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the circuit court properly refused to instruct the jury on mistake of fact, because the evidence did not raise a mistake of fact question. Defendant's theory of defense was not based upon an erroneous perception of the facts, which actually existed. Further, the court held that the circuit court correctly instructed the jury regarding the loss of the privilege of self-defense, because defendant's conduct was expressly prohibited by criminal law and his words were intended to provoke a disturbance. A person who engaged in unlawful conduct of a type likely to provoke others to attack him was not entitled to claim the privilege of self-defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of attempted first-degree murder.

 

1967 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


DRENNING v. STATE


Nos. 78-938-CR & 78-939-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


97 Wis. 2d 753; 295 N.W.2d 225; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3721



May 23, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from the judgments of the circuit court for Rock County: GERALD W. JAECKLE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendants of second-degree murder, armed robbery, and concealing identity during the commission of a crime contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.02, 943.32(1)(a) and (2), and 946.62, respectively.


OVERVIEW: The charges stemmed from the murder of a service station attendant. Defendants contended that the death was accidental and occurred after one defendant went to the gas station to sell a gun. According to defendant, during a dispute over the price of the gun, the weapon discharged. Subsequently the victim shoved defendant and the gun discharged again. Defendants contended that the testimony of an accomplice was on its face unreliable and incredible as a matter of law. The court rejected this contention, holding that the record did not show that the accomplice's intoxication rendered her incapable of remembering the events to which she testified. Further, the court held that some of the facts remembered by the accomplice were corroborated. The court rejected defendants' contention that there was insufficient evidence to convict them for armed robbery because the jury was required to speculate as to whether anything was actually taken from the gas station. The court held that although the precision of the state's evidence and the method of determining the amount taken were not exemplary, there was sufficient evidence for the jury to have found that money had been taken by defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for second-degree murder, armed robbery, and concealing identity during the commission of a crime.

 

1968 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Guardianship of Eberhardy


No. 78-661


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 654; 294 N.W.2d 540; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3155


May 17, 1979, Argued  
May 23, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Wood County: Dennis D. Conway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardians sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which denied the guardians' petition for an order authorizing them to sign a consent for the incompetent's sterilization.


OVERVIEW: The guardians submitted a petition for an order authorizing them to sign a consent for the incompetent's sterilization. The trial court denied the petition and the guardians sought review. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 801.04(1), the trial courts were given subject matter jurisdiction when conferred by the constitution and state statutes. The court determined that, absent a specific statutory authority for the sterilization of the incompetent, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider the action and to order such medical procedure. The court further found that the right to procreate was one of the basic civil rights of man and held that the state courts were not authorized to order the taking away of such right. The court affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which denied the guardians' petition for an order authorizing them to sign a consent for the incompetent's sterilization.

 

1969 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. BANG


Nos. 79-1486 and 79-1487


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


97 Wis. 2d 756; 295 N.W.2d 227; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3687



May 20, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Pierce county: WILLIAM E. McEWEN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested for driving a motor vehicle while intoxicated, and he refused to submit to an evidentiary breath test. After a hearing held pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(8)(b)(1), the circuit court for Pierce county (Wisconsin) ordered defendant's license revoked for six months. The trial court also held that Wis. Stat. §§ 343.305, 346.63 were constitutional and denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the county failed to introduce sufficient evidence at the hearing to support the trial court's finding that his refusal to take the evidentiary breath test was unreasonable. The trial court had the right to accept the testimony of the arresting officers, and the officers' testimony was adequate to support the findings made by the trial court. The testimony showed that defendant was issued a citation for driving while intoxicated and that he received a copy of the notice of intent to revoke after he refused the breathalyzer test. He was given the full range of his implied consent rights. Defendant contended that the implied consent statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305, violated his due process right because it limited a refusal hearing to specific issues. Defendant's constitutional arguments were based on speculation and theory. The court would not indulge in academic exercises. He also challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(4). The presumption of intoxication enacted by the legislature had a rational connection to the ultimate fact to be proven. The statute was also not a "guilt per se " provision because the State still had to prove its case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court.

 

1970 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. State Public Defender v. Percy


No. 80-298


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


97 Wis. 2d 627; 294 N.W.2d 528; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3160


April 24, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
May 16, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Daniel R. Moeser, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The circuit court is directed to enter judgment declaring that secs. 48.355(4) and 48.365, Stats. 1977, are applicable to all juveniles whose legal custody is in the department by virtue of adjudication of delinquency and further providing that the department may within thirty days of the date of that court's judgment file petitions to extend the orders by which it acquired such custody prior to the effective date of secs. 48.355(4) and 48.365, Stats. 1977.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Secretary for the Department of Health and Social Services, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), requiring him to apply the Children's Code, Wis. Stat. § 48 (1977) to all children in the department's custody, including those whose custody was acquired under the statute before the effective date of its amendment, November 17, 1978.


OVERVIEW: Two agencies concerned with the legal rights of juveniles brought an action on behalf of juveniles adjudicated delinquent under the old Children's Code and whose legal custody was transferred to the Department, challenging the Department's intent to maintain legal custody over those juveniles for periods greater than one year, as authorized by the old code, without obtaining judicial extensions of custody under the new code. The trial court ordered the Department to apply the new Children's Code to all children in the department's custody and to file petitions for extension of custody pursuant to the new code within 30 days On appeal, the court held that the terms of the department's custody could be modified by a statute enacted after custody was acquired. The court that the new code was to be liberally construed in a manner favoring the best interests of the child, and held that the custody termination and extension provisions of the new code, being deemed in the better interests of children than those of the old code, had to prevail, regardless of when the child was adjudicated delinquent.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the trial court to enter judgment declaring that Wis. Stat. §§ 48.355(4) and 48.365 (1977) was applicable to all juveniles in the legal custody of the department by virtue of adjudication of delinquency and further provided that the department could within 30 days of the date of that court's judgment, file petitions to extend the orders by which it acquired such custody prior to the effective date of §§ 48.355(4) and 48.365.

 

1971 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


LEVY v. MILWAUKEE CTY.


No. 79-1028


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


96 Wis. 2d 736; 293 N.W.2d 183; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3552



April 15, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from an order and a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order and judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded plaintiff landowner litigation expenses in the condemnation proceeding initiated by the landowner. The landowner cross-appealed the amount of litigation expenses he was awarded.


OVERVIEW: A jury awarded the landowner compensation for land acquired by the county through eminent domain. The landowner's motion requesting litigation expenses was initially denied. A few months later, Wis. Stat. § 32.28, which provided for litigation costs in a condemnation action, became effective. The landowner renewed his motion for litigation costs, which was granted. The county appealed. The court held that the trial court's judgment in the condemnation action was granted and rendered, but had not been entered nor perfected on the date that § 32.28 became effective. Section 32.28 applied to all actions or proceedings on its effective date regardless of when the action was commenced. The legislative intent, clearly expressed in § 32.28, applied to an action in which a judgment had been rendered, but not entered nor perfected. Where the attorneys failed to keep adequate time records, the trial court's determination of hourly rates for the four attorneys was proper because the trial court expressed its full appreciation of the complexity of the issues involved and counsel's competence and success at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1972 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Woodman v. Wisconsin Dep't of Health & Social Services


No. 79-1497


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


96 Wis. 2d 466; 292 N.W.2d 352; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3146


March 11, 1980, Submitted on Briefs  
April 8, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Chippewa County: Robert F. Pfiffner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Chippewa County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent state department of health and social services (DHSS) to terminate the father's benefits under the Aid to Families with Dependent Children (AFDC) program because the father owned two vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The DHSS terminated the father's AFDC benefits because he owned two cars in violation of Wis. Stat. § 49.19(4)(em). The court affirmed the trial court's affirmation of the DHSS's decision. The statute did not violate the supremacy or equal protection clauses. 45 C.F.R. § 233.10(a)(1) expressly required states to set eligibility requirements. Thus, the federal government did not intend to preclude state regulation in the area of eligibility. Further, the states had the power to impose conditions on applicants in furtherance of state welfare policy as long as the conditions were not inconsistent with the Social Security Act. A purpose of § 49.19(4)(em) was to require families with limited resources to allocate those resources so as to maximize the amount available for family support. Scare family funds were not to be diverted to unnecessary vehicles. States also had the authority to limit property that could be reserved by an AFDC family. Wis. Stat. § 49.19(4)(em) placed a reasonable restriction, as each automobile would drain a family's resources. Finally, the statute had a rational basis because a family with needy children was not to divert assets to an unnecessary second vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1973 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Carolan v. Sheboygan County Dep't of Social Servs.


No. 79-1013


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


95 Wis. 2d 742; 293 N.W.2d 181; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3414



March 26, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: F. H. SCHLICHTING, Judge. Vacated and remanded with directions. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which terminated their rights to their minor child and awarded custody to respondent county department of social services (DSS).


OVERVIEW: The DSS sought to terminate the parents' parental rights. The parents demurred, challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 48.40(2)(b) on vagueness grounds. The trial court terminated their rights. On appeal, the parents again challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The court found that because the Attorney General was not served with notice of a constitutional challenge to the statute at the trial court level as required by Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11), neither the trial court nor the court of appeals had subject matter jurisdiction to decide the issue. The court then exercised its discretionary authority under Wis. Stat. § 752.35 and vacated the trial court's order and remanded with directions to provide the proper notice to the Attorney General. The court held also that the trial court should decide which party should provide the proper written notice to the Attorney General and noted that the trial court could provide such notice. Lastly, the court noted that a sufficiency of evidence issue had been properly raised in addition to the constitutional issue, therefore, instead of dismissing the appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, it remanded the whole issue.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the case with directions for the trial court to designate who was to notify the Attorney General and to proceed consistent with the opinion. The court noted that the case need not be retried, but the constitutional issue, if it was to be presented, could be presented after proper notice.

 

1974 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Winnebago v. Neale


Nos. 79-864, 79-865, and 79-866


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


95 Wis. 2d 741; 293 N.W.2d 181; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3420



March 26, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for Winnebago county: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) of violating Winnebago County, Wis., Zoning Ordinance § III-A. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants each had a one-third interest in three lots on a channel leading to a lake. One of the lots was separated from the other two and was unimproved. Defendants used the unimproved lot for the storage of their boats. The county prosecuted defendants for violating § III-A. At trial, defendants argued that the ordinance was ambiguous and thus it had to be construed in their favor. The trial court found that the ordinance was unambiguous and convicted defendants of the charged offense. On appeal, the court held that: (1) § III-A of the ordinance was not ambiguous and, thus, it was not required to be construed in defendants' favor; (2) defendants failed to show that the ordinance allowed an invalid exercise of police power denying them equal protection where its clarity showed no room for the zoning administrator to prosecute or not prosecute based on his own whim and caprice; and (3) the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague where it gave defendants fair notice that their conduct was prohibited by § III-A.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

1975 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


PHILLIPS v. STATE


Nos. 79-579-CR, 79-580-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


95 Wis. 2d 740; 293 N.W.2d 180; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3516



March 26, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the circuit court for Grant County: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle after his license was revoked, sentenced him to 10 days in jail, and ordered him to pay a fine and costs. Defendant alleged that the complaint and the underlying license revocation procedures were invalid, and that the mandatory sentence of Wis. Stat. § 343.44 was cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's driver's license was revoked for two months but he drove his car during the revocation period. As a result, defendant was convicted under Wis. Stat. § 343.44 of operating a motor vehicle after his license was revoked. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: Defendant waived his objections to the complaint because he did not object to the long-form complaint until he filed his post-conviction motions. In addition, because defendant did not show that he was prejudiced by any defects in the complaint, Wis. Stat. § 971.26 precluded the judgment from being affected by reason of any defect. Defendant waived his claim that the lack of a mandatory hearing on the license revocation was unconstitutional because he did not request a hearing and because he did not raise the issue until he filed his post-conviction motions. The mandatory sentence of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(2) did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment although defendant was a first time offender, because defendant could not have violated § 343.44 without first violating other traffic laws, and his violation of § 343.44 showed a wanton disregard of the traffic laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1976 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Milwaukee v. Proegler


No. 79-1080


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 614; 291 N.W.2d 608; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3138

March 18, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Michael J. Skwierawski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant in violation of Milwaukee County, Wis., Ordinance tit. I, § I (adopting Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)). Defendant had argued that the breathalyzer evidence should have been suppressed on the ground that he was not informed that his license could be revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found asleep in is parked car, which was running. He was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant's license was revoked. He appealed, and the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the failure to advise defendant prior to administration of the breathalyzer test of the potential revocation of his driving privileges upon conviction of a violation of § 346.63(1) did not constitute a denial of due process or an illegal search and seizure. The court concluded that the trial court's finding that defendant "operated" his vehicle within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(3) even though it was parked was supported by the evidence. Finally, the court held that the application of § 346.63(3) and the implied consent to breathalyzer test in Wis. Stat. § 343.305 to defendant was constitutional. The court found that it was not arbitrary or invidious for the legislature, having regard for public welfare, to enforce the statutory provisions against all intoxicated persons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, which found defendant had operated a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.

 

1977 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Clark County v. Acheson


No. 79-1063


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


95 Wis. 2d 736; 289 N.W.2d 375; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3547



January 23, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court for Clark county: LOWELL D. SCHOENGARTH, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants property owners sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin) rendered in favor of respondent County of Clark, in an action by the County to collect the value of logs, wood, and timber taken from properties on which the Count held tax certificates for unpaid property taxes.


OVERVIEW: The property owners failed to pay property taxes on farm lands owned by them. When the property owners harvested logs, wood, and timber from the properties, the County instituted an action to levy upon the profits. The property owners sought review, contending that the tax on their farm land was not in compliance with the state and federal constitutions, and was also excessive, unequal, and obsolete. The court ruled that the property tax did not abridge the property owners' rights under the 14th Amendment of the U.S. Constitution because although the payment of property taxes was involuntary neither slavery nor involuntary servitude resulted from the tax or failure to pay the taxes, and likewise, the farm property tax did not rest upon an improper classification for purposes of equal protection of the laws. The court also ruled that as farmers, the property owners were not required to pay a disproportionate amount of tax despite the fact they were taxed on their income and on their property used to derive their income. Lastly, the court ruled that it was not up to the courts to determine whether the property tax was obsolete and should be abandoned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
