Ryan v. State


No. 79-1131-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


95 Wis. 2d 83; 289 N.W.2d 349; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3111


December 14, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
January 21, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Errors to review a judgment and orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Robert W. Landry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) for rape in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.01, robbery in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.32(1), sexual perversion in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.17, false imprisonment in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.30, and habitual criminality in violation of Wis. Stat. § 939.62.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for rape, robbery, sexual perversion, false imprisonment, and habitual criminality. The record showed that defendant attacked the victim in an alley where he knocked her down, threatened to kill her, and forced her to have sexual intercourse. Defendant contended that he went to the alley and attempted to help the victim. To corroborate his story, defendant introduced the testimony of a fellow prisoner who testified that he was in the area at the time of the assault and remembered hitting someone. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and concluded that the circuit court did not err in striking the testimony of the defense witness. The court held that by the witness's invocation of his privilege against self-incrimination, the State was denied the right to meaningful cross-examination and the information given by the witness was so vague and inconclusive as to merit no weight by the jury. Also, there was no error in refusing to allow another witness to testify regarding admissions against interest made by the fellow prisoner since the prisoner's statements could not withstand the probable cause requirement for charging him with the crimes at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction against defendant for rape, robbery, sexual perversion, false imprisonment, and habitual criminality. The court also affirmed the circuit court's order denying defendant's motion for a new trial and defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.

 

1980 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tyson


No 79-681


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


95 Wis. 2d 735; 289 N.W.2d 375; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3404



January 15, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: MICHAEL P. SULLIVAN, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver sought review of an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county (Wisconsin), which entered judgment revoking his motor vehicle operation privilege for failure to consent to an evidentiary blood alcohol test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a single-car accident and was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, in violation of a Milwaukee ordinance in conformity with Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). The charge was dismissed at the municipal court level. Defendant refused to take an evidentiary chemical test and was granted a hearing in the circuit court on his refusal. He contended that because the charge of operating a vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant was dismissed before the hearing establishing his refusal to take the evidentiary test, the trial court could not statutorily or constitutionally revoke his operating privilege. The trial court rejected both contentions, and found that defendant had in fact refused to submit to tests, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 343.305. Wis. Stat. § 343.305(7)(d) calling for the reinstatement of operating privileges on the dismissal of charges was repealed. The effect of the repeal was to allow for the continued prosecution of a refusal, even if drunk driving charges were dismissed. There was probable cause to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

1981 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sherman Agric. Lime v. Barron County


No. 79-620


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


95 Wis. 2d 734; 289 N.W.2d 374; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3499



January 15, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment entered in the circuit court for Barron county: D.J. STERLINSKE, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lime company brought an action against defendant county for a declaration that Wis. Stat. § 59.873 was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint. The company appealed, contending that § 59.873 violated the public policy doctrine of the Wisconsin Constitution and unconstitutionally allowed a political subdivision to engage in private business in direct competition with private enterprise.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 59.873 provided that a county could manufacture agricultural lime, sell and distribute it to farmers, and acquire land for such purposes. The county operated an agricultural lime business under § 59.873. Its quarry was located in another county. The county operated three trucks to transport the lime to consumers and also directly sold lime to consumers at the quarry. A county committee was formed to establish policies and make decisions concerning the operation of the business, and a county agent assisted in managing the quarry. The committee and agent were compensated by public tax revenues. The county paid no taxes and was able to sell lime for less than the company. The court held that § 59.873 was constitutional as it served a public purpose by providing an economic benefit to the agricultural community. When first enacted, § 59.873 introduced the use of agricultural lime into farming operations. Thus, its continued use was necessary for modern farming. Although the county's operation competed with private enterprise, it was a permissible municipal activity as it promoted the general public welfare. Thus, the county's use of public funds was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1982 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Morales v. Department of Indus., Labor & Human Relations


Nos. 78-871 & 78-872


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


95 Wis. 2d 733; 289 N.W.2d 374; 1980 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3540



January 10, 1980 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane county: P. CHARLES JONES, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their petition for review of an order of respondent Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) for lack of jurisdiction, and from an order of the same court refusing to grant a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations (DILHR) to issue findings and orders on the petitioners' complaints.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had dismissed petitioners' petition for review of an order of LIRC for lack of jurisdiction because the petition was not served and filed within the 30-day time limit prescribed by Wis. Stat. § 227.16(1)(a). The court rejected petitioners argument that the 30 days did not begin to run because they were not served with a certified copy of the order, and that they should have had 33 days to serve and file their petition because service was made by mailing. LIRC's decision was under Wis. Stat. § 111.36(3m) and, under Wis. Stat. § 111.37, the time for instituting review proceedings was governed by Wis. Stat. § 227.16, which required service of the decision by mail as provided in Wis. Stat. § 227.11. Wis. Stat. § 801.15(5), on which petitioners relied, applied only to judicial actions and not to proceedings before or appeals from administrative tribunals. The court also affirmed the trial court's refusal to issue a writ of mandamus to compel DILHR and its secretary to issue written findings and orders on the petitioners' complaints because the duty of the DILHR secretary to review the hearing examiner's findings was not clear or free from substantial doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1983 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Klimas


No. 78-553-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


94 Wis. 2d 288; 288 N.W.2d 157; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2790


March 15, 1979, Argued  
December 20, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County: Edwin C. Dahlberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for second degree murder was affirmed on appeal and he sought postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06. The Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) denied relief, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his wife and was convicted of murder. He argued that he was denied due process because psychiatric evidence concerning his state of mind was excluded and the trial court refused to give a manslaughter instruction. After the conviction was affirmed on direct appeal, a federal court ruled that Wisconsin's practice of excluding psychiatric testimony concerning the accused's capacity to form the specific intent to kill deprived a criminal defendant of the right to present evidence. In affirming the court held that the psychiatric evidence should have been admitted because it was clearly relevant to disprove the specific intent element of first-degree murder, but the error was harmless where defendant was convicted of second degree murder, a crime without a specific intent element. Where the proffered psychiatric testimony that defendant's act was impulsive did not tend to show that it was uncontrollable or that defendant was then in a state of the highest degree of exasperation, rage, anger, sudden resentment, or terror necessary to establish heat of passion manslaughter, its exclusion did not deprive defendant of his constitutional right to present a defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying postconviction relief.

 

1984 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ABDELLA


No. 79-086-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District III


94 Wis. 2d 694; 289 N.W.2d 372; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3056



December 11, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgement and an order of the circuit court for Price county: DAVID A. CLAPP, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Price County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of violating Wis. Admin. Code § Ag. 114.03, a regulation enacted under Wis. Stat. § 100.20(2), relating to unfair trade practices.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a contract to sell a farm implements dealership. The contract failed to state the advertising medium. Defendant was charged with unfair trade practices, pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § Ag. 114.03. The trial court convicted defendant. On defendant's appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that § 114.03 required one soliciting advance fees to furnish a contract which identified each advertising medium used, that defendant's contract only referred obliquely to the advertising method, that § 114.03 did not abridge defendant's constitutional rights to contract or to free speech, that Wis. Stat. § 100.20(2) only required a public hearing for the issue of the regulation (which was accomplished), not to a public hearing for each complaint, that the legislature did constitutionally create a criminal penalty for the violation of the regulation, that defendant could not challenge the jury instructions for the first time on appeal, and that sufficient evidence supported the verdict so that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions for directed verdict, for judgment notwithstanding verdict, and for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, convicting defendant of failure to disclose fully his advertising medium for selling real estate in violation of the unfair trade practices' regulations.

 

1985 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. State


No. 78-832-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 875; 289 N.W.2d 318; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2767


September 19, 1979, Argued  
November 20, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County: James Wilbershide, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order reversed and caused remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of attempted first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The jury was given an instruction providing that, where there were no circumstances to prevent or rebut the presumption, the law presumed that a reasonable person intended all the natural, probable, and usual consequences of his deliberate acts. If one person assaulted another violently with a dangerous weapon, likely to kill, then when there were no circumstances to prevent or rebut the presumption, the legal and natural presumption was that death was intended. Defendant's sole claim on appeal was that the instruction violated the Fourteenth Amendment in that it shifted the burden of proof to defendant, it invaded the fact-finding function of the jury, and it was an irrational presumption. The court agreed, reversed defendant's conviction, and remanded the case for a new trial. The court found that a reasonable juror could have easily viewed the instruction as mandatory as opposed to permissive. Although mandatory, it was rebuttable. However, the mandatory rebuttable presumption was one that shifted the "burden of persuasion" as opposed to one that shifted the "burden of production" and was therefore unconstitutional. The error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded for a new trial.

 

1986 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


SHERMAN v. STATE


No. 79-347-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


93 Wis. 2d 698; 287 N.W.2d 855; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2973



November 15, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: ERROR to review an order of the circuit court of Milwaukee county: HUGH R. O'CONNELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied a motion for postconviction relief brought after he was convicted of extortion, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.30(2) (1975). Defendant claimed that when compared with Wis. Stat. § 943.30(1) (1975), charging him under Wis. Stat. § 943.30(2) constituted a denial of equal protection. He also alleged that § 943.30(2) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: A woman received a call from defendant threatening to have her husband and children shot by a sniper. He instructed her to place money in a bag and take it to a particular location. The police were notified and defendant was apprehended when he picked up the money. He was convicted and filed a motion for postconviction relief, which was denied. He appealed and the court affirmed the decisions. The court found that under the rational basis test, the court only had to determine whether there existed any reasonable basis for the classification. As a rational basis did exist for the punishment differential between Wis. Stat. §§ 943.30(1) and 943.30(2) because the threat of physical violence justified a more severe sanction than a mere threat of injury, the constitutionality of § 943.30(2) was upheld. Defendant's claim that § 943.30(2) was void for vagueness for failure to give fair notice of the conduct forbidden was without merit because it clearly prohibited threats of physical violence in furtherance of a plan to extort money. Because § 943.30(2) gave adequate notice of its coverage, it did not offend the due process clauses of the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision convicting defendant and denying his motion for postconviction relief.

 

1987 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


American Motors Corp. v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 77-703


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


93 Wis. 2d 14; 286 N.W.2d 847; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2773; 21 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 654; 21 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P30,408


October 25, 1978, Argued  
November 2, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the findings of the Wisconsin State Department of Industry, Labor, and Human Relations (DILHR) that the employer had violated the Wisconsin Fair Employment Act (WFEA), Wis. Stat. §§ 111.31 through 111.37, by discharging appellee employee on the basis of his religion. The employee cross-appealed the denial of back pay.


OVERVIEW: The employer argued that the trial court erred in sustaining the DILHR finding that the WFEA required Wisconsin employers to accommodate the religious needs of their employees. The employee, an engineer, and two other new employees were required to participate in a rigorous six-month training program. Partway through the program, the employee requested leave of absence to attend a religious function of his church. At that time, he did not explain that his attendance was considered mandatory by his church. His request was denied, and he was ultimately told that he would have to work the days in question or be terminated. The trial court affirmed the DILHR's finding of discrimination on the basis of religion. The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed in part. The court held that the WFEA required the employer to make reasonable accommodations for the employee's religious practices and that the burden was not met by showing inconvenience to the employer. The court reversed that part of the judgment denying the award of back pay, holding that the statute created a private cause of action for wages lost because of a discrimination occurring prior to its effective date.


OUTCOME: That part of the judgment that denied an award of back pay to the employee was reversed, and the judgment was modified accordingly. As modified, the judgment against the employer was affirmed.

 

1988 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Withers v. Portage County (In re D.S.)


No. 79-071 -


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District Four


92 Wis. 2d 911; 286 N.W.2d 647; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2942



October 26, 1979 


NOTICE:

UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the orders of the circuit court for Portage county: ROBERT C. JENKINS, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --The orders of the court terminating appellant's parental rights are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which terminated the mother's parental rights to her sons in a proceeding commenced by respondent county department of social services seeking termination of the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of a judgment terminating her parental rights, the mother contended that the trial court judge erred in refusing to recuse himself on the grounds of prejudice and that the findings as to the mother's ability to care for her sons were not sustained by the evidence. In affirming, the court held that although the mother had no statutory right to a change of judges, she could move for the judge to disqualify himself on grounds of prejudice. However, the judge was not required to accept the allegations of prejudice at their face value; a showing of prejudice in fact had to be made. In the instant case, the judge rejected the allegations of prejudice, and his statement as to why he would not recuse was convincing as to his lack of prejudice and his intention to do justice on the basis of the record. Thus, the judge did not err in refusing to recuse himself. Finally, the trial court's findings permitting termination of parental rights under Wis. Stat. § 4840 were supported by evidence that the mother had substantially and repeatedly neglected her sons and was unable for a prolonged indeterminate period to give them the parental care and protection necessary for their health.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1989 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. COLUMBIA CORP. v. TOWN BD. OF PAC.


Nos. 78-366, 78-367, 78-368


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


92 Wis. 2d 907; 286 N.W.2d 645; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2940



October 8, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia county: ANDREW P. COTTER, judge. Reversed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions to enter an order requiring the town board to approve the preliminary plats in question.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which upheld a decision by respondent town board (board) denying the landowner's application for approval of three subdivision plats.


OVERVIEW: The landowner applied for approval of subdivision plats. The board rejected the application pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 236. The landowner then sought review of the board's decision, and the circuit court upheld the decision, finding that it was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or discriminatory. On appeal from the circuit court order, the court reversed. The court held that the board had no discretion to reject the proposed plats under Wis. Stat. § 236.13, unless the plats conflicted with an existing statutory requirement of Wis. Stat. § 236 or an existing written ordinance, master plan, official map, or rule as provided by Wis. Stat. 236.13(1)(a) through (e). The court reasoned that the committee notes to Wis. Stat. § 236 indicated that the statutory revisions were designed to prevent the review and rejection of plats on the basis of standards that had not been articulated and communicated to potential subdividers in advance. The court held that provisions of the preamble to the chapter contained in Wis. Stat. § 236.01 conferred no separate or other authority on local units of government to reject plats in the exercise of the review powers contained in Wis. Stat. § 236.13(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order upholding the board's denial of the landowner's application for approval of proposed subdivision plats. The court remanded the cause with directions to order the board to approve the preliminary plats.

Graney v. Board of Regents of University of Wisconsin System


No. 79-202


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 745; 286 N.W.2d 138; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2755


July 26, 1979, Argued  
October 8, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Pending. This Petition was not Decided at the Time the Volume Went to Press. Its Disposition will be Reported in a Later Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Richard W. Bardwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant terminated faculty sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted respondent board of regents' motion for summary judgment in an action filed by the terminated faculty seeking damages and declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The terminated faculty were tenured members of the University of Wisconsin System under Wis. Stat. § 37.31(1971). The terminated faculty contended that § 37.31 created a contract between the state and tenured faculty members that was breached by the board of regents; that the board of regents' power to terminate tenure rights because of a financial exigency could not be delegated; and that the procedures used violated their due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court found that the terminated faculty were precluded from bringing the action because of the doctrines of sovereign immunity and public officer civil immunity and because they failed to exercise their exclusive method of review through administrative procedures. The court held that the terminated faculty were precluded from asserting the due process issue under the doctrine of res judicata because that issue was determined in the federal court action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1991 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Columbia Corp. v. Town Bd. of Pacific


Nos. 78-366, 78-367, 78-368


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 767; 286 N.W.2d 130; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2756


April 13, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
October 8, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County: Andrew P. Cotter, judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment reversed and cause remand-with directions to enter an order requiring the town board to approve the preliminary plats in question.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which upheld the rejection by the Town Board of the Town of Pacific of three subdivision plats, proposed under Wis. Stat. ch. 236, which were part of a plan to develop 528 acres of the corporation's land in the Town of Pacific for residential and recreational use.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the corporation's submission of the proposed subdivision plats, the Town had adopted no standards or guidelines for use in deciding whether to approve such plats. On appeal of the Board's rejection of the subdivision plats, the circuit court held that the Board's action had not been unreasonable, arbitrary, or discriminatory and upheld the Town's rejection of the plats. The principal issue on appeal was whether the Board had discretion under ch. 236 to reject a proposed plat in the absence of previously adopted standards or guidelines for approval. In reversing the decision in favor of the Board, the court held that local units of government, such as the Town, had no discretion to reject proposed plats under Wis. Stat. § 236.13, unless the plat conflicted with an existing statutory requirement of Wis. Stat. ch. 236 or with an existing written ordinance, master plan, official map, or rule as provided by Wis. Stat. § 236.13(1)(a)-(e). Thus, the Board, having failed to take the only lawful actions it could take under Wis. Stat. § 236.13, forfeited its right to act at all with respect to these plats under Wis. Stat. § 236.11(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the Board and remanded with directions to order the Board to approve the preliminary plats.

 

1992 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Asso. of Nursing Homes, Inc. v. Journal Co.


No. 78-214


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 709; 285 N.W.2d 891; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2752


September 12, 1979, Oral Argument  
October 5, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order and judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Ralph J. Podell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order and judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nursing home association sought the issuance of an order in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) to compel defendant newspaper company to publish the association's full-page advertisement responding to published investigatory reports on nursing homes. The trial court denied the request and granted the newspaper's motion to dismiss. The association sought appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The association prepared a response to a series of investigative reports dealing with the quality and care of nursing homes, and wished to publish the response as a full-page advertisement in the two newspapers owned by the newspaper company. The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the association had not set forth a claim upon which relief could be granted. The court held that a court could not compel the publisher of a daily newspaper to accept and print an advertisement exactly as submitted. The court held that the newspaper company had a right to expect that the courts would respect and protect their constitutional right to exercise their prerogative in accepting or rejecting proposed advertising material. The court held that there was nothing in United States Constitution, any federal law, or any controlling precedent that would allow the court to compel a private newspaper to publish advertisements without editorial control of their content merely because such advertisements were not legally obscene or unlawful. The court held that editorial policy should not be the subject of judicial interference. The court affirmed the dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no dispute that, as presented, the association failed to allege any facts that would serve as the basis of a claim sufficient to withstand a motion to dismiss. The court affirmed the order and judgment of dismissal.

 

1993 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. ANDERSON


No. 79-889


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


92 Wis. 2d 907; 286 N.W.2d 645; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2838



October 4, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court of Milwaukee county: PATRICIA CURLEY, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss license revocation proceedings pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(3)(b) on the ground of failure to obtain personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1). He subsequently refused to submit to a test to determine the presence or quantity of alcohol in his blood. Upon his refusal, defendant was given a document known as "Notice of Intent to Revoke Operating Privilege." Defendant claimed that the document was an insufficient means of obtaining jurisdiction over his person for further adjudication of the matter because it did not contain a statement of probable cause, and because it was not issued by a neutral judicial officer. Defendant moved to dismiss the proceedings against him on the ground that the trial court had failed to obtain personal jurisdiction. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court noted that the Wisconsin statutes explicitly recognize that the "Notice of Intent to Revoke Operating Privilege" provided a sufficient documentary basis for obtaining personal jurisdiction. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional under the Fourth Amendment, because the statute was not a criminal statute. The court noted that there was no potential for fine or imprisonment or both.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

HERAN v. STATE


No. 77-805-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


92 Wis. 2d 906; 287 N.W.2d 853; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2881



September 25, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the county court for Manitowoc county: WARREN GRADY, Judge; and APPEAL from and order of the circuit court for Manitowoc county: ALLAN DEEHR, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a judgment of conviction for failing to provide proper food, water, and shelter to confined animals, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 948.13, 948.14 (1977), but remanded for an evidentiary hearing as to the reasonableness of expenses assessed under Wis. Stat. § 948.17 as a condition of probation. The trial court reassessed the investigation expenses.


OVERVIEW: Officers removed several farm and domestic animals from defendants' farm because the animals were in poor physical condition from inadequate food, water, and shelter. Defendants initially waived their rights to an attorney and to a jury trial, but they later retained counsel. Defendants were fined and placed on probation. In the present appeal, the State moved to strike all issues except the sufficiency of the evidence because the issues were not presented to the circuit court on appeal. The court denied the State's motion for reasons of judicial administration and policy. The court further held that: (1) because of defendants' voluntary and intelligent waiver of a jury trial, the State's failure to consent to the waiver, as required by Wis. Stat. § 972.02, was harmless error; (2) the testimony showed that the shelter provided by defendants was inadequate compared to normally accepted husbandry practices, and it sufficiently established defendants' ownership or responsibility over the animals; and (3) the assessment of expenses did not raise the issue of unconstitutional discrimination based upon wealth because defendants had not yet faced imprisonment for failure to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order of the circuit court.

 

1995 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. S & S Meats, Inc.


No. 78-629


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


92 Wis. 2d 64; 284 N.W.2d 712; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2746


April 13, 1979, Submitted on Briefs  
September 25, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to Review Denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: P. Charles Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle owner challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered a judgment of forfeiture of a vehicle allegedly used in illegal drug trafficking, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 161.55. The trial court also refused to reopen the judgment. The issue was whether the State had to prove that a controlled substance was acquired and transported in Wisconsin in order to justify the forfeiture of the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the evidence showed that the substances seized were probably "acquired" in Illinois. Therefore, the heroin seized from his vehicle was not "property" as described in § 161.55(1)(a). The court held that § 161.55(1)(d) imposed a sanction on the act of transporting controlled substances, not on the act of acquiring them. Though the acquisition in Illinois was not punishable under Wisconsin law, the transportation of those substances in Wisconsin triggered the imposition of the forfeiture sanction regardless of where the substances were acquired. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the heroin was being transported for purposes of sale rather than for personal use. According to the expert testimony, it had a street value of between $ 4,250 and $ 7,000. Finally, the crime laboratory expert's testimony that, in her opinion, to a reasonable degree of scientific certainty, the substance was heroin was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the substance was heroin.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1996 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. 79-178


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District IV


92 Wis. 2d 905; 287 N.W.2d 853; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2958



September 24, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the circuit court for Dane county: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found that defendant forfeited $ 30 plus costs for violating Wis. Stat. § 346.57(5) by operating a motor vehicle 10 miles per hour over the posted limit.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment that defendant forfeited $ 30 plus costs for violating Wis. Stat. § 346.57(5) by operating a motor vehicle 10 miles per hour over the posted limit. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court concluded that the legislature properly classified a speeding violation as a civil rather than criminal matter.The court found that the constitutional right to counsel did not apply because a speeding violation was not a crime and that defendant waived his right to a trial by jury because he did not pay the jury fees. The court determined that a uniform traffic citation and complaint that was issued to defendant gave the trial court jurisdiction over him pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.11(5). The court found that a radar reading of defendant's speed did not constitute either a search or seizure of his automobile and that a state trooper's testimony based upon his reading of his radar equipment was admissible because it was based on personal knowledge.The court concluded that defendant failed to show that the state trooper's practice of selectively arresting speeding motorists was without justifiable discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that defendant forfeited $ 30 plus costs by operating a motor vehicle 10 miles per hour over the posted limit.

 

1997 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Genova v. State


No. 78-790-CR


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin


91 Wis. 2d 595; 283 N.W.2d 483; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2718


June 20, 1979, Argued  
September 21, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Victor Manian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order from the Circuit Court, in Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of theft, party to a crime. His sentence was withheld and he was placed on probation. The trial court denied defendant's postconviction motions for dismissal of the action, for judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the jury verdict, or alternatively, for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant launched a constitutional attack against the instructions to the jury based upon due process grounds. The instruction stated that when there were no circumstances to prevent or rebut the presumption, the law presumed that a reasonable person intended all of the natural, probable, and usual consequences of his deliberate acts. Defendant also contended that the language in the instruction as given to the jury was contrary to the requirements of Wis. Stat. § 903.03(3). The court affirmed the conviction and found no error in the instruction. It determined that a presumption was not involved at all but that the instruction actually dealt with an inference. The jury remained free to consider additional evidence before accepting or rejecting the inference. Ultimately the decision on the issue of intent was left to the trier of fact alone.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction for theft, party to a crime. The court also affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's postconviction motions for dismissal of the action, for judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the jury verdict, or alternatively, for a new trial.

 

1998 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


AMERICAN INS. CO. v. CONTINENTAL CAS. CO.


No. 78-799 and 78-800


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District I


92 Wis. 2d 907; 286 N.W.2d 645; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2841



September 20, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court of Milwaukee county, MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.

Recommendation:


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and its insurer, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded damages to a person injured as a result of an accident which occurred during a police chase, and which refused to limit the damages under Wis. Stat. § 895.43 .


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were whether Wis. Stat. § 895.43, which limited damages against a city, was constitutional, whether the insurance contract waived the statutory ceiling, and whether Wis. Stat. § 345.05, which applied specifically to governmental liability for automobile accidents and which contained no such limitation, controlled over Wis. Stat. § 895.43. The court first noted that the Wisconsin Supreme Court had held § 895.43 constitutional. The court then noted that where a general and a specific statute related to the same subject matter, and there was conflict, the specific statute controlled. Because Wis. Stat. § 345.05 was more specific than Wis. Stat. § 895.43, the former controlled. The court rejected the city's contention that the legislature had inadvertently failed to repeal or amend Wis. Stat. § 345.03. Furthermore, Wis. Stat. § 895.43 specifically provided for exceptions to its own coverage by reference to "other statutes" which controlled over § 895.43. Finally, the court held that policy language agreeing to waive the right to use defenses available to the insured respecting governmental immunity was a waiver of the limitation of municipal liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment against the city and the insurer without regard to the statutory limitation of damages.

 

1999 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. KARNITZ v. SIPPEL


No 78-758


Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District II


92 Wis. 2d 905; 287 N.W.2d 853; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2877



September 18, 1979 


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: ALLAN J. DEEHR, Judge. Affirmed. 



DISPOSITION: By the Court. --Judgment affirmed.

Recommendation:


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which adjudged him to be the father of a child and held him liable for all expenses incurred for lying-in and attendance of the mother during pregnancy and for past care and support of the child in a paternity action under Wis. Stat. § 52.22 and Wis. Stat. § 52.25. The trial court also entered an order for future child support.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the action was improperly commenced, that statutes requiring past and future support for children were unconstitutional because they arbitrarily discriminated against men, and that the mother had an affirmative duty to contribute toward the financial support of the child. The court held that the action was properly commenced because the district attorney had authority to bring the complaint on information and belief. The court opined that the requirements in Wis. Stat. § 52.37, which provided for the father's payment of pregnancy-related expenses, the past care and support of the child, and the future support of the child did not violate equal protection standards. The court opined that the classifications were germane to the welfare and protection of the child, equalized the responsibilities between the parents, and relieved the public of the burden of supporting the child. In the court's view, although not measurable in money, the services rendered by the mother in providing for the child's emotional and physical needs were equally as valuable as the cash support provided by the father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2000 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. KARNITZ v. SIPPEL


No. 78-758


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


92 Wis. 2d 905; 287 N.W.2d 853; 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3505



September 18, 1979, RELEASED  
September 18, 1979, FILED


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(b)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan county: ALLAN J. DEEHR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity action, defendant father appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) that adjudged him to be the father of the child at issue, deemed the father liable for expenses incurred by the mother during her pregnancy and for past care and support of the child, and ordered that the father pay future child support, arguing that Wis. Stat. ch. 52 arbitrarily discriminated against men.


OVERVIEW: A paternity action was commenced against the father, and the circuit court determined that he was the biological father of the child and ordered that he pay the mother's pregnancy-related expenses and pay child support. The father appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that there was a rational basis for the distinction between men and women under Wis. Stat. ch. 52. Both the father and mother should share in the obligations involving their a child; while the mother bore the physical burdens of pregnancy, it was reasonable to expect the father to share in the responsibility by paying the financial costs of the pregnancy. As to child support, the responsibilities of father and mother were equalized, but support by the father was determined in part by the resources of the mother and the desirability that the mother remain at home. Although not measurable in money, the services rendered by the mother were equally as valuable as the cash support provided by the father. The State's interest in the welfare of the child and in equalizing the responsibilities of the parents justified such a classification in regard to future support of the child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.
